201 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Trs. of the Police Pension & Ret. Sys. v. Weed


No. 60,793


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 23; 719 P.2d 1276; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 129



May 28, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma Honorable Charles Owens, Judge. This appeal arises from action commenced in the District Court of Oklahoma County by the Police Pension and Retirement Board of Oklahoma City, seeking declaratory relief to cease pension benefits of Fred Weed pursuant to 11 O.S. 1971 § 541(p) and Oklahoma City Code § 2-342 (1970). The district court held the statute and ordinance, purporting to divest Weed of his pension benefits based on his felony conviction, to be unconstitutional..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a city's police pension board of trustees, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which held that Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 541(p) (1971) and Oklahoma City, Okla., Code § 2-342 (1970), which purported to divest appellee retired city employee of his pension benefits based on his felony conviction, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the employee retired, he began receiving his pension. He was then convicted of conspiring to distribute a narcotic controlled substance. The board requested that the trial court terminate the employee's pension benefits under Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 541(p) (1971) and Oklahoma City, Okla., Code § 2-342 (1970). The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the statute and ordinance were unconstitutional under Okla. Const. art. 2, § 15, which provided that no conviction would work a forfeiture of estate. Once the employee qualified for his pension, it became a vested property right. Nothing in the record showed that his pension benefits were obtained by or acquired in pursuance of illegal activity; the felony conviction occurred four years after retirement. The employee's vested right to his pension could not be forfeited as a consequence of his felony conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment declaring that the statute and ordinance purporting to divest the employee of his pension benefits were unconstitutional.

 

202 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. Meachum


No. 62,095


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 18; 718 P.2d 1354; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 122



May 6, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Edward M. McDanel, Judge. Appellant questions the validity of the denial of his requested relief in the District Court of Cleveland County. In that proceeding appellant attacked the Department of Corrections' reclassification of the prisoner as a security risk not eligible for incarceration in a minimum security facility by virtue of a past escape. It is contended this action, taken under Corrections' rules instituted after the escape, violate constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which, in his proceeding for post-conviction relief against appellees, Director of the Oklahoma Department of Corrections and a correctional facility warden, attacking the Department's reclassification of appellant as a security risk, denied such relief. Appellant argued that such action violated constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: Appellant escaped from a state correctional facility. He was later convicted of such escape. Subsequently, Okla. Stat. tit. 57, § 510 (Supp. 1983) was enacted, which authorized the Department to enact rules and punishment for recalcitrant prisoners. Pursuant to § 510, the Department instituted a new security risk rating scale. Under such scale, appellant was reclassified as a security risk and deemed ineligible for minimum security incarceration. Appellant sought post-conviction relief, arguing that such action violated constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws. The trial court denied relief. On appeal, the court initially noted that the prohibition against ex post facto laws was intended to secure substantial personal rights against arbitrary legislation and not to limit legislative control of procedures that did not affect matters of substance. The court then held that appellant did not have a substantial personal interest in the place of his confinement. Whatever deprivation he experienced after the change in security status did not encroach upon his liberty interest; such interest was extinguished to the point that the State could confine him where it wished.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellant's request for post-conviction relief.

 

203 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Gilbert Cent. Corp. v. State


No. 61,521


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 6; 716 P.2d 654; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 109



March 25, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 27, 1986.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff construction company presented a certification order requesting clarification of Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 24.3 (1981) after the Oklahoma Attorney General issued an opinion advising the defendants Oklahoma Department of Transportation and its officers that the construction company, pursuant to § 24.3, could not continue to work under an existing construction contract with defendants, the state and the department.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the clear, unequivocal, and unambiguous language of Okla. Stat. tit. 51, §24.3 (1981), was to prohibit certain felons from making sale of real or personal property to the state or any political subdivision thereof. There being no contrary indication from the language of the statute, the court held that it was the sale of real or personal property that is debarred. The court held that upon applying the word "sale" as used to the statute, a highway construction contract did not constitute a "sale" and was therefore not within the prohibition of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the provisions of the statute did not apply to the construction company's contract because it encompassed contracts for the sale of goods and the contract the construction company had been maintaining with defendants was a construction contract, which was a contract for services.

 

204 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. Okla. Firefighters Pension & Ret. Sys.


No. 64,354


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 8; 718 P.2d 348; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 110



March 25, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified Questions of Law From the United States District Court for the Western District of Oklahoma. Two questions of law have been certified to this Court by the United States District Court for the Western District of Oklahoma pursuant to the State's statutorily provided procedure therefor. The questions involve the constitutionality of the repeal of certain portions of retirement acts of public employees which reduced the benefits provided by those acts. The questions involve two classes of employees; those whose rights to the benefits had "vested" or "accrued" prior to the repeal of the act, and those employees whose retirement benefits had not vested in them prior to the effective date of the repeal. Certified Questions Answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two questions of law were certified to the court by the United States District Court for the Western District of Oklahoma regarding the constitutionality of the repeal of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 49-136 (1981) and Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 50-120 (1981), thus reducing the retirement benefits provided to plaintiff public employees. The action was filed against defendants, a firefighters' retirement plan, a police retirement plan, and others.


OVERVIEW: The statutes at issue had granted automatic pension adjustments as part of the employees' pension programs. 1983 Okla. Sess. Laws 143, § 8 repealed those two statutes The public employees were of two classes; those whose rights to the benefits had "vested" or "accrued" prior to the repeal of the act, and those employees whose retirement benefits had not vested prior to the effective date of the repeal. The district court certified two questions to the court. In response to the first question, the court decided that those employees who had retired or who could have retired and become eligible for payment of pension benefits prior to the effective date of the repeal of the pension provisions acquired a right under those provisions which could not be detrimentally affected by subsequent acts of the legislature. The court noted that no contract existed between an employee and the state, concerning the state pension plan, unless and until the pension vested. In response to the second question, the court found that 1983 Okla. Sess. Laws 143, § 8 was not unconstitutional as applied to the employees who had not become eligible for benefits prior to the effective date of the repeal.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions.

 

205 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Missouri-Kansas-Texas R.R. Co. v. State


No. 60,429


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 108; 712 P.2d 40; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 172



December 24, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Oklahoma Corporation Commission. An appeal from the Commission Order No. 238528, in Cause No. 27470, whereby the Commission granted powers of eminent domain to ETSI, et al. ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad company sought review from an order by the Oklahoma Corporation Commission that issued a license to appellee pipeline company to exercise eminent domain powers in the construction of a coal slurry pipeline. Both the commission and the pipeline company challenged the railroad's standing to appeal the issuance of the license.


OVERVIEW: The railroad was a competitor of the pipeline company who had previously appeared before the commission and opposed the license application. The railroad company contended, inter alia, that the commission lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the pipeline company, that the commission's action was preempted by federal law, and that the enabling statute was unconstitutional. The court ruled that the railroad company had standing but the order was proper. The court held that: (1) as a competitor of the licensed company, the railroad had standing as an "aggrieved" party; (2) the commission had subject matter jurisdiction over the pipelines because Okla. Const. art. IX, § 34, which defined transportation companies that the commission was permitted to regulate was not exhaustive, but was intended to include new modes of transportation; (3) the regulation of coal pipelines was not pre-empted by congress because the state law did not stand as a obstacle to the accomplishment and execution of the full purposes and objectives of congress; and (4) a joint venture was still a legal entity upon which the right of eminent domain could confer under Okla. Stat. tit. 27, §§ 7.1-7.11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the license.

 

206 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Woods Dev. Co. v. Meurer Abstract & Title Co.


No. 59,640


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 106; 712 P.2d 30; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 176



December 24, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Pawnee County, Oklahoma. Honorable W. Keith Rapp, Judge. Appellant landowner originally brought suit individually and as class action against abstract company, claiming abstract company exacted charges in violation of mandatory fee schedule as set forth in 1 O.S. 1981 § 7 (repealed 1984). Following trial court's direction, landowner added as parties defendant all abstract companies in Oklahoma. Certiorari was granted to review a certified interlocutory order in which the trial court concluded that 1 O.S. 1981 § 7 was advisory only, and if enforced would be unconstitutional as confiscatory, unreasonable and vague. JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed an interlocutory order from the District Court of Pawnee County (Oklahoma), which concluded that Okla. Stat. tit. 1, § 7 (1981) was advisory only, and unconstitutional as confiscatory, unreasonable, and vague. The landowner brought an action against defendant abstract and title company, claiming their charges violated the mandatory fee schedule set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 1, § 7 (repealed 1984).


OVERVIEW: The company prepared five abstracts and submitted a bill for fees greater than those set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 1, § 7 (repealed 1984). The landowner brought an action for a refund of charges exacted by the company in excess of the statutory fee schedule for abstracts ordered and delivered over the past five years. He also sought delivery of the five abstracts upon payment of the statutory charges. The trial court found that the maximum fee schedule established in 1910 was advisory only and its strict enforcement was unconstitutional. If applied to the current abstracting industry, the schedule was vague, economically unreasonable, and confiscatory. The trial court directed the company to calculate its charges for abstracts prepared for the landowner in an amount not to exceed 40 times the charges stated in the statute. The trial court took judicial notice that current movie prices were 40 times what they were in 1910. The trial court then certified the ruling for interlocutory appeal. On appeal, the court held that the statute was mandatory but agreed that it was unconstitutional. The court found, however, that the trial court's comparison to movie prices was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the order that found the statute that set fees for title companies unconstitutional. The court reversed the part of the order that found that the statute was advisory only and not mandatory. The court reversed the portion of the order that purported to calculate maximum fees based upon a multiple factor of 40 and remanded for a determination of the company's reasonable compensation.

 

207 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re Baby Boy D


No. 62,024


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 93; 742 P.2d 1059; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 182



November 12, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from order of trial court sustaining the appellee's objection to jurisdiction and motion to quash and dismissing the appellant's Petition to Vacate Decree of Adoption and Remand Custody.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Indian father sought review of an order of the trial court (Oklahoma) that sustained appellee adoptive parents' objection to jurisdiction and motion to quash, and dismissed his petition to vacate a decree of adoption. Appellant claimed that he was denied due process rights of notice and opportunity to be heard, and that the adoption proceedings were subject to invalidation under the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 1901-1963.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Indian father sought to set aside a decree of adoption on the grounds that the adoption of his son without consent or notice was subject to invalidation under the Indian Child Welfare Act (ICWA), 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 1901-1963 and Oklahoma Indian Child Welfare Act (OICWA), Okla. Stat. tit 14, §§ 40-49, and denied him due process. The trial court sustained appellee adoptive parents' objection to jurisdiction and motion to quash, and dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court held that appellant did not have standing under the ICWA and OICWA to vacate the decree because they applied when Indian children were being removed from an Indian home, and granted standing only to the parent from whose custody the child was being removed. The court held that appellant did have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Oklahoma adoption statutes that did not require an unwed father's consent, but that U.S. Const. amend. XIV only protected parent-child relationships of biological parents who had actually exercised their responsibility for rearing their children. The court held that it was error to deny appellant's motion to proceed in forma pauperis and remanded on that issue only.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that dismissed appellant Indian father's petition to vacate a decree of adoption of his son. The court held that Fourteenth Amendment did not protect appellant where paternity had not been acknowledged or established and appellant had never accepted any responsibility for his child. The court reversed the denial of appellant's motion to proceed in forma pauperis and remanded.

 

208 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Davis


No. 58,468


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 85; 708 P.2d 1102; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 158



October 22, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIV. 4. In a post-divorce interparental proceeding to terminate paternal rights based upon grounds provided in 10 O.S. 1981 § 1130, the District Court, Lincoln County, Donald E. Powers, Judge, ordered that the father's parental bond with his minor daughter be severed. The Court of Appeals reversed. Certiorari was granted on the mother's petition. THE COURT OF APPEALS' OPINION IS VACATED AND THE TRIAL COURT'S ORDER IS REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother obtained certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division 4 (Oklahoma), which reversed a decision from the trial court that appellant father's parental bond with his minor daughter be severed for his failure to pay child support. The trial court's decision arose in a post-divorce interparental proceeding to terminate paternal rights based upon grounds provided in Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The dispositive issue on certiorari was whether an involuntary termination of a parental bond might be effected in a private interparental proceeding based on Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130(A)(4) (1981). The court held that all contests instituted under the Juvenile Code must first be judicially examined or "screened" for "intake" before they were allowed to proceed. The court, sitting in the administration of the so-called juvenile process, functioned as the legally trained discretionary authority charged with the duty of balancing societal interests with those of the child. Because the record was devoid of any evidence of harm sufficient for invocation of governmental intervention, the mother's sole recourse to affect the father's status vis-a-vis his child lay either in a private action countenanced by Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 9 (1981) or in an adoption without his consent under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 60.6(3) (1981). The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (1981) grounds were not invokable in a private suit by the custodial parent who sought termination of parental rights of the noncustodial parent. Thus the court answered the question in the negative.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the appellate court. The court reversed the trial court's termination order without prejudice to the mother's post-remand institution of a suit or to her joining in a proceeding to terminate the paternal bond in an adoption to be effected without the father's consent.

Citicorp Sav. & Trust Co. v. Banking Bd. of State


No. 61,663


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1985 OK 63; 704 P.2d 490; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 202



July 23, 1985, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE OKLAHOMA BANKING BOARD



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of a judgment of appellee, the Oklahoma Banking Board, which denied the bank's application for a certificate of authority pursuant to Okla. Banking Code art. III, Okla. Stat. tit. 6, §§ 301-313 (1982).


OVERVIEW: The bank sought the certificate of authority to engage in the savings and trust business as successor to a corporation it had acquired. Such a certificate, issued by the Board, would allow the bank to commence operations. The Board found the bank had satisfied the requirements of Okla. Stat. tit. 6, § 313 (1982) for approval of an application for certificate of authority, but denied the application without prejudice because there was an appeal or an earlier order of the Federal Reserve Board approving the acquisition, and the Board deemed the issues of the appeal "inextricably intertwined" with the Board's consideration of the application at issue. Affirming the Board's decision, the court held that the Board had discretion as to whether or not to issue the certificate and that it did not abuse its discretion or act in an arbitrary or capricious manner by not issuing the certificate. The court rejected the bank's contention that it was denied equal protection under the laws because a rational basis for the differential treatment accorded the bank existed in that such treatment furthered legitimate state interests as set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 6, § 307.1 (1982).


OUTCOME: The Board's decision was affirmed.

 

210 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


White v. Amoco Prod. Co.


NO. 58,913


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1985 OK 55; 704 P.2d 470; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 199; 85 Oil & Gas Rep. 616



July 16, 1985, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CORPORATION COMMISSION OF THE STATE OF OKLAHOMA



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an unleased mineral owner, sought review of a decision of the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma, which dismissed appellee oil company's pooling application. The mineral owner contended that the oil company significantly delayed the forced pooling proceeding which resulted in an unconstitutional taking of his drilling rights.


OVERVIEW: The question presented on appeal was whether bonus money was required to be paid to owners of unleased mineral interests when a forced pooling application was dismissed at the request of the moving party when drilling operations had proven the land concerned would not produce hydrocarbons. The mineral owner contended that the commission erred in sustaining the oil company's motion to dismiss without providing compensation for damages caused by the oil company's delay in the pooling application proceedings. Specifically, the mineral owner asserted that during the period of conversion his property rights were held captive and that the lease value of his mineral rights dropped precipitously. The court sided with the position of the oil company because the pooling application was not sufficiently delayed to deny the mineral owner of the fair market value of his drilling rights. Further, the mineral owner made no effort to lease his mineral rights to others during the pendency of the pooling application although the he was permitted to do so and had done so in the past.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the decision of the commission, which dismissed the oil company's pooling application.

 

211 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Glenn Smith Oil Co. v. Sheets


No. 60,028


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 56; 704 P.2d 474; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 192; 1985-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P66,715



July 16, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court in Muskogee County, Oklahoma, Honorable Hardy Summers, Trial Judge. Appeal from trial court's order enjoining sale of gasoline in violation of Unfair Sales Act, 15 O.S. 1981, §§ 598.1 et seq. Court of Appeals, Division No. 3, affirmed. Certiorari granted to consider case of first impression and constitutional question: whether Unfair Sales Act is constitutional as applied to the sale of gasoline.



DISPOSITION:  CERTIORARI GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED; ORDER OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) granting injunction in favor of appellee in an action alleging unfair sales practices with a view to injure competitors, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 15, §§ 598.1 et seq. (1981).


OVERVIEW: During the period when Oklahoma experienced a citywide "gas war", appellant sold gasoline at a price below the retail cost. Appellee claimed that appellant's conduct was for the purpose of lessening competition and that it irreparably injured appellee. Lower court granted appellee's motion for injunctive relief to restrain the retail sale of gasoline below cost. On appeal, appellant contended that the sale of gasoline could not be said to constitute the sale of merchandise within the meaning of the Oklahoma Unfair Sales Act (Act), Okla. Stat. Tit. 15, §§ 598.1 et seq. (1981). Alternatively, appellant urged that the Act was unconstitutional as applied to the sale of gasoline. The court held that gasoline was one of the ordinary commodities of trade and therefore constituted "merchandise". The court asserted that the state had authority under its exercise of police power to fix prices or place regulatory controls on business and the Act did not contravene U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Okla. Const. art. II, §§ 2, 7. Therefore, the order of the trial court for permanent injunction against appellant was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order of permanent injunction restraining appellant's sale of gasoline below cost was affirmed because the state had power under the U.S. Constitution to regulate sale of gasoline as merchandise.

 

212 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Griggs v. State ex rel. Okla. DOT


No. 60,656


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 51; 702 P.2d 1017; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 130



July 2, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From The District Court, Mayes County. William J. Whistler, Judge. In an action by an automobile passenger and her husband to recover damages for bodily injury and loss of consortium, the trial court rendered judgment on State's demurrer to the petition. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, automobile passenger and her husband sought review of a judgment by the District Court, Mayes County (Oklahoma), which ruled in favor of appellee State. The passenger and her husband brought an action to recover damages for bodily injury and loss of consortium.


OVERVIEW: A State vehicle collided with a car in which the passenger was riding. The passenger and her husband sought recovery for bodily injury and loss of consortium. The State invoked the doctrine of sovereign immunity, and the trial court ruled in its favor. The passenger and her husband appealed, claiming that the doctrine of governmental immunity was unconstitutional and that they should be allowed to proceed because there was a substantive change in the law. The court stated three factors for ascertaining when retroactivity of a new pronouncement should be restricted: (1) the decision must have established a new principle of law, either by overruling clear past precedent or on an issue of first impression whose decision was not clearly foreshadowed; (2) the reviewing court must weigh the merits of applying the rule retroactively by considering its prior history, purpose and effect, and whether retroactivity would further or retard its operation; and (3) the reviewing court must consider the inequity flowing from retroactive application. The court found no infirmity in a recent decision of the court regarding immunity to refuse the conferral of the new rule upon pending cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the State, dismissing the passenger and her husband's claim for damages for bodily injury and loss of consortium.

 

213 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


First of McAlester Corp. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


Nos. 60,488 Surviving number, 60,653 Consolidated with No. 60,488


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1985 OK 52; 709 P.2d 1026; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 131



July 2, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Oklahoma Tax Commission Order No. 83-05-10-15. Appellants sought review of an Oklahoma Tax Commission Order which denied appellants' and all other banks' claims for refund and denied all exclusions from net income for calculations of bank tax liability accrued prior to Memphis Bank & Trust Co. v. Garner, 459 U.S. 392, 74 L. Ed. 2d 562, 103 S. Ct. 692 (1983) and determined that Memphis Bank should be applied prospectively only. The issues presented in the instant consolidated matter are whether 68 O.S. 1981 §§ 2370 and 2371 (repealed 1983) were unconstitutional and, if so, whether this Court's determination of the unconstitutionality of such statutes should be applied retroactively or prospectively only from January 24, 1983, the date of the Memphis Bank decision.



DISPOSITION:  Vacated in Part and Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant banks challenged an order of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission, which denied the banks' claims for refunds, denied all exclusions from net income for calculations of bank tax liability accrued prior to a United States Supreme Court decision, and determined that the decision should be applied prospectively only.


OVERVIEW: The United States Supreme Court issued a decision that held that a Tennessee excise tax on banks unconstitutionally discriminated in favor of obligations issued by the state and against federal obligations. The banks sought a refund of "in lieu tax" paid to the state through the Commission pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 2370 and 2371 (repealed 1983). The Commission denied the banks' claim for a refund and denied all exclusions from net income for calculations of bank tax liability accrued prior to the Supreme Court's decision, holding that the decision was to be applied prospectively only. The court vacated the order in part and affirmed in part. The Commission's administration of the bank tax act, §§ 2370 and 2371, unconstitutionally discriminated against federal obligations by computing the basis of the tax as federal taxable income plus the interest income on obligations of states other than Oklahoma. The Supreme Court's decision was to be applied prospectively only because the rule could be effectuated without retroactive application and retroactive application would result in a large refund of taxes, which would put an enormous financial burden upon the state.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the Oklahoma Tax Commission's order in part and affirmed in part.

 

214 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cumbey v. State


No. 59,795


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 36; 699 P.2d 1094; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 195



May 7, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma. The Honorable Edward M. McDanel, Trial Judge. Appellant-inmates brought action challenging constitutionality of statutory provisions authorizing (1) 20% compulsory savings from employment in prison industries; and (2) withholding by the State of Oklahoma an amount not in excess of 50% of prison inmates' income from all other employment during incarceration for costs of incarceration. Trial court held statutory provisions constitutional.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates sought review of the decision of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which sustained appellee State of Oklahoma's demurrer in the inmates' action challenging the statutory provisions authorizing 20 percent compulsory savings from employment in prison industries and withholding an amount not in excess of 50 percent of prison inmates' income from all other employment during incarceration for costs of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: The inmates filed an action challenging the constitutionality Okla. Stat. tit. 57, § 549.5 (Supp. 1984), which authorized 20 percent compulsory savings from employment in prison industries, and Okla. Stat. tit. 57, § 542 (Supp. 1984), which authorized withholding an amount not in excess of 50 percent of prison inmates' income from all other employment for costs of incarceration. The state demurred. The district court sustained the demurrer and held the statutory provisions were constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the inmates had no inherent legal right to the payment of wages for their work in prison industries or to determine its form or amount. The inmates' 20 percent prison accounts were conditional credits of potentially accessible funds, not vested property interests. The court held that prison officials had a legitimate goal of providing the inmate with funds upon his release to assist him in readjusting to society. The court held that a withholding of the fruits of prison labor not in excess of 50 percent for costs of incarceration was rationally related to the legitimate goal of maintaining state prisons in conformity with constitutional standards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

 

215 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


McDowell v. Austin


No. 62,386


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1985 OK 33; 699 P.2d 1100; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 203



April 30, 1985, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. Honorable Robert F. Martin, District Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a person who pleaded guilty to a charge of driving while intoxicated, sought review of an order of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which sustained appellee court clerk, court director, and district attorney's motions to quash for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and dismissed his action under the Oklahoma Declaratory Judgment Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 23, § 1651 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a plea of guilty to a charge of driving while intoxicated, was sentenced and fined, and ordered to pay court costs, which were set by statute at Okla. Stat. tit. 28, § 153 (1981). He subsequently filed an action under the Act requesting the trial court to declare the statute in question unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that appellant should have raised the question of the constitutionality of the court costs statute at the trial level in the traffic case. Because he failed to do so, he could not use the Act to raise the question at this later date. The trial court sustained appellees' motions to quash for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and dismissed the case. Upon appeal, the court affirmed the order. The purpose of a declaratory judgment was to declare rights not theretofore determined and was not to determine rights previously adjudicated. Furthermore, the court held that court costs must be litigated in the action in which they were taxed and not in a subsequent suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which sustained appellees' motions to quash for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and dismissed appellant's action under the Oklahoma Declaratory Judgment Act.

 

216 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hughes Drilling Co. v. Crawford


No. 61207


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 16; 697 P.2d 525; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 124



February 26, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 16, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Review a Certified Interlocutory Order; District Court of Logan County. Petitioner seeks review of certified interlocutory order wherein trial court determined it had jurisdiction of wrongful death action by parents of minor son against his employer for death caused by injuries covered by the Workers' Compensation Act.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED. ORDER OF TRIAL COURT OVERRULING OBJECTION TO JURISDICTION REVERSED. CAUSE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought certiorari from the court to review a certified interlocutory order from the District Court of Logan County (Oklahoma), in which the trial court determined that it had jurisdiction of a wrongful death action by plaintiff parents, whose minor son died from work-related injuries covered by the Workers' Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 1 et seq. (1981).


OVERVIEW: The parents, whose minor son died from injuries incurred while working on an oil and gas drilling rig, contended that they were not limited to workers' compensation benefits. Alleging the employer's negligence and reckless disregard for the son's safety, the parents claimed wrongful death under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1055 (1981). The court found that the parents could recover as heirs-at-law if they sustained pecuniary loss under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 22.9 (1981). The court pointed out that under the constitutional amendment, the legislature did not destroy a wrongful death action, but it limited the amount. The court explained that the amendment's valid purpose was to allow the legislature to limit the pecuniary loss that could be recovered by those taking action under the wrongful death statutes for deaths covered by the Workers' Compensation Law. The court concluded that because a limitation was explicitly recognized by the provision on which the parents relied, they did not meet their burden of showing that a legislative enactment was unconstitutional in the face of a presumption of validity under Oklahoma law, and the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, reversed the trial court's order overruling the employer's objection to its jurisdiction over the parents' claim for death benefits, and remanded with instructions to dismiss.

 

217 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cate v. Archon Oil Co.


No. 60,148


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1985 OK 15; 695 P.2d 1352; 1985 Okla. LEXIS 110; 40 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1941; 83 Oil & Gas Rep. 576



February 19, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Muskogee County. Honorable William Bliss, Trial Judge. This is an appeal from an order confirming the sheriff's sale of an oil and gas lease. The trial court confirmed the sale after determining that because the lease was personalty, the sale was subject to less stringent statutory guidelines.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant leaseholder appealed the order of the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma), confirming the sale of its oil and gas lease pursuant to plaintiff judgment creditor's execution and subsequent purchase of the lease, classified as personalty, for $ 500 as opposed to the contended value of $ 45,000. The sale had been conducted pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 764 (1981) that required two-week publication notice of the sale.


OVERVIEW: While the property had been advertised as a sale of lands and tenements, the creditor failed to comply with the law requiring that a bid on such realty was required to amount to two thirds of the appraised valuation. Thus, the leaseholder asserted a failure to follow proper statutory authority, voiding the sale. Although it reversed the district court judgment due to the constitutional insufficiency of notice by publication for such sales, the court held that the lease conveyed an estate in the realty, but was not itself realty within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 706 (1921). Instead, the lease was properly classified as chattels real and was, therefore, personal property. However, decrying the inability of §§ 757 and 764 to provide the personal notice required by constitutional due process concerns, the court determined that Uniform Commercial Code, Okla. Stat. tit. 12A, §§ 2-706(3), 9-504(3) (1981) required that the leaseholder be properly notified of the sale. Further, the court held that failure to afford personal notice to one who held a security interest, such as the leaseholder, resulted in an unconstitutional exercise of jurisdiction as to such interest holders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the district court.

 

218 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ricks Exploration Co. v. Okla. Water Res. Bd.


Nos. 58,350, 59,172, No. 58,350 Surviving Number


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 73; 695 P.2d 498; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 177; 83 Oil & Gas Rep. 584



October 16, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 16, 1984; Rehearing Denied February 26, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the District Court, Oklahoma County. Carmon C. Harris [in 58,350] and William S. Myers, Jr. [in 59,172], Judges. In two proceedings before the Oklahoma Water Resources Board, mineral lessee was denied standing to seek either a special or a provisional temporary groundwater permit. Upon separate appeals to the district court, the Board's rulings were affirmed. The appeals stand consolidated for disposition by a single opinion.



DISPOSITION: THE FIRST APPEAL [58,350] IS DISMISSED, DISTRICT COURT'S JUDGMENT IN THE SECOND APPEAL [59,172] IS REVERSED AND THE CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mineral lessee sought review of a judgment entered in the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which dismissed the lessee's appeal from the Oklahoma Water Resources Board's denial of the lessee's application for a provisional temporary permit to withdraw groundwater from the land. In a second appeal, the lessee sought review of the district court's affirmance of the Board's denial of his application for a special permit.


OVERVIEW: The lessee's application for a provisional temporary permit for groundwater use was denied on the ground that the lessee had not obtained permission from the surface owner to withdraw the water and thus did not have standing to seek a permit under the Oklahoma Groundwater Law, Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1020.1 et seq. (1981). The lessee's request for a special permit was denied for the same reason. The district court dismissed the lessee's appeal from the denial of his first application and affirmed the Board's denial of his second application on the basis that the decisions were correct. On further review, the court ruled that lessee's first appeal was from a non-final order so that the district court should have dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction rather than on the merits. As to the second appeal, the court ruled that the lessee had a proprietary interest in the reasonable non-domestic use of groundwater that was sufficient to place the lessee in the category of "owners" within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1020.11(D) (1981) and could not be precluded from obtaining a permit for lack of standing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order dismissing the lessee's appeal from the denial of his application for a provisional temporary permit, but remanded with directions to modify the decision to effect a dismissal of the case for want of jurisdiction. The court reversed the district court's judgment affirming the Board's denial of the lessee's application for a special permit.

220 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cavett v. Peterson


Nos. 50962, 50961


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 59; 688 P.2d 52; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 171



September 18, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County; William S. Myers, Jr., Judge. Three groups of appellants question on appeal a judgment arising from Trustees' petition in District Court to construe a trust. The questioned judgment construes the trust and rules on other pending objections filed by appellants dealing with validity of prior orders.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three groups of appellants, all of whom were either grandchildren or more remote issue of the settlor of a trust, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which construed the trust with respect to a variety of issues upon the petition of appellee trustees and affirmed the validity of prior orders entered with respect to the administration of the trust.


OVERVIEW: In the course of construing the trust, the trial court sustained the validity of various orders and decisions that had been entered in prior proceedings related to the administration of the trust. The trial court also, among other things, approved the trustees' payment of trust income to the settlor's children. Appellants claimed that the trial court erred in sustaining the validity of the prior orders and in approving the payment. The court affirmed. The court first determined that its prior decision that appellants were contingent beneficiaries was the law of the case and that the decision was binding because it was not palpably erroneous and it did not result in manifest injustice to the parties. The court also determined that the fact that not all of the contingent beneficiaries were served with process in the prior proceedings did not affect the validity of the orders because the contingent beneficiaries were not necessary parties under Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 175.23(C). The court also found that the trial court did not err in approving the income payment because the approval was not clearly in conflict with the provisions of the testamentary trust instrument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Tenneco Oil Co. v. El Paso Natural Gas Co.


No. 53201


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 52; 687 P.2d 1049; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 157; 82 Oil & Gas Rep. 322



July 17, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1984; As Corrected September 13, 14 and October 10, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District of Roger Mills County; Charles M. Wilson, Judge. Appeal from order of the district court quieting title in petitioners against named defendant and adjudicating and declaring petitioner's rights and duties under an operator's agreement, executed subsequent to forced-pooling order, affecting common source of supply as issued by the Oklahoma Corporation Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant gas company appealed an order of the District of Roger Mills County (Oklahoma), which quieted title in petitioner oil company against named the gas company and which declared the oil company's rights and duties under an operator's agreement, executed subsequent to a forced-pooling order, affecting the common source of supply as issued by the Oklahoma Corporation Commission.


OVERVIEW: The Oklahoma Corporation Commission subjected the parties to a forced-pooling order. The oil company was designated as operator of the unit; however, the oil company was unable to meet the drilling commencement deadline and notified the gas company. The parties signed then an operator's agreement. The oil company filed a quiet title action against the gas company, requesting a declaration of its rights to participate in the operation of a producing well. The gas company appealed and the court reversed the appellate court with directions to dismiss the oil company's cause of action for want of subject-matter jurisdiction. 222 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


First of Denver Mortg. Investors v. Riggs


Nos. 59,563 59,885


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 36; 692 P.2d 1358; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 134



June 5, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court of Oklahoma County, John M. Amick and Jack R. Parr, Judges. Appeal from rulings which terminated the enforcement of a foreign money judgment on the ground that it was dormant under Oklahoma law.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment creditor challenged rulings from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), terminating the enforcement of a money judgment against appellant judgment debtor as dormant under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 735 (1981) and the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 719 et seq. (1981). The creditor asserted estoppel to assert dormancy and that it had the right to revive the judgment.


OVERVIEW: In 1977 the creditor obtained a judgment in Colorado against the debtor. It filed the judgment in Oklahoma in 1977 under the Act. The trial court found the judgment dormant under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 735 (1981). The creditor refiled the judgment in Oklahoma under the Act in 1982. The trial court granted the debtor's motion to quash interrogatories and held that the refiling had not revived the judgment. The creditor appealed all rulings, asserting that the trial court erred in finding the judgment dormant and that it had a right to revive the judgment. The court disagreed and affirmed. It explained that under the Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 721, a foreign judgment was treated as if it had been rendered in the state of filing for purposes of enforcement. The judgment filed from a longer running state followed the shorter term of the state of filing. Thus, the rendition of judgment in Colorado started the dormancy period running under the Act. The judgment became dormant because no execution had issued on it within five years of judgment, as Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 735 (1981) required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rulings of the trial court.

 

223 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Atchison, Topeka & Santa Fe Ry. Co. v. State


No. 59,056


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 29; 683 P.2d 974; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 129



May 22, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma. An appeal from an order of the Corporation Commission granting the request of the Oklahoma Department of Transportation to designate two grade crossings with necessary signal devices and directing the Atchison, Topeka, and Santa Fe Railroad, Appellant, to construct and maintain such crossings.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railway company disputed an order of appellee Corporation Commission (Oklahoma), which granted the request of appellee Oklahoma Department of Transportation to designate two grade crossings with signal devices and direct the railway company to construct and maintain the crossings. The issues included whether the order was within the Commission's jurisdiction and whether the order violated the state and federal due process clauses.


OVERVIEW: The Commission asserted jurisdiction under Okla. Stat. tit. 17, §§ 81, 82, 84 (1981) and Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 128 (1981). On appeal, the court pointed out that the statutes had been settled law for more than 60 years. The court rejected the railway company's strained construction of Okla. Const. art. IX, §§ 18, 19, 35. The court held that the Commission's exercise of jurisdiction was proper under Okla. Const. art. IX, § 19 given that the construction of railroad crossings related to the railway company's public duties. It made no difference that the road where the crossings were to be placed was laid after the tracks. Requiring the railway company to pay for the crossings was not a taking without due process of law prohibited by Okla. Const. art. II, § 7 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Nor was there a violation of the equal protection clause. The constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 17, § 82 (1981), which required a railroad to bear the expense of highway grade crossings, was well established. Because the Department did not perfect an appeal by filing a petition in error and failed to object or seek review of an issue before the Commission, it could not obtain affirmative relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Corporation Commission.

 

224 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State. ex rel. York v. Turpen


No. 61,986


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 26; 681 P.2d 763; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 122



May 15, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Prohibition and/or Declaratory Judgment. Marvin York, President Pro Tempore of the Senate, petitions this Court to accept original jurisdiction to review the propriety of Attorney General's Opinion No. 83-202, and to clarify the right of the Legislature of the State of Oklahoma to proceed funding the Police & Firefighters' pension funds in accord with the current statutory scheme enacted by the legislature, including a statute repealing previous funding schemes, 1983 Okla. Sess. Laws, c. 143, § 8, which was, in effect, declared unconstitutional by the above mentioned Attorney General's opinion.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED; WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner President Pro Tempore of the Oklahoma State Senate, sought a writ of prohibition and/or declaratory judgment and petitioned the court to review the propriety of an opinion of respondent Oklahoma Attorney General. The opinion, in effect, declared unconstitutional 1983 Okla. Sess. Laws, ch. 143, § 8, a statute repealing previous funding schemes for police & firefighters' pension funds.


OVERVIEW: The opinion declared the repealing statute unconstitutional absent a showing that it was necessary to protect the actuarial soundness of the firefighters' and police officers' pension systems. In his petition for the writ, the senate president contended that the attorney general had no authority to declare an act of the legislature unconstitutional. The court denied the writ, holding that the opinion was to be considered advisory only and that it was not binding until finally so determined by an action in a district court of Oklahoma. For an opinion finding an act of the legislature unconstitutional to be binding upon state officers prior to judicial intervention was an unwarranted encroachment upon the power of the legislature to determine policy of the law applicable to state government. Such power properly rested only with the judiciary. Moreover, the opinion failed to embrace the basic presumption that an act was constitutional. Also, contrary to Oklahoma law, it placed the burden of going forth on some unnamed forum to prove that the act was necessary for it to be valid.


OUTCOME: The court denied the senate president's petition.

 

225 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Reherman v. Okla. Water Res. Bd.


No. 61,890


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 12; 679 P.2d 1296; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 111



April 5, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to assume original jurisdiction pursuant to 82 O.S.Supp.1982, § 1085.37, and Petition for Writ of Prohibition.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ASSUMED; WRIT OF PROHIBITION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought a writ of prohibition, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1085.37 (Supp. 1982), challenging the legality and the constitutionality of the sale of investment certificates by respondent, the Oklahoma Water Resources Board, to develop state and local plans for water control and use. Petitioners contended that the bond issue, at Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1085.31 et seq. (1981), was forbidden by Okla. Const. art. X, §§ 14, 15.


OVERVIEW: The Board passed resolutions accepting bids and authorizing the issuance and sale of investment certificates to provide funding for state and local plans. Under Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1085.33, the certificates were not an indebtedness of the State but were special obligations payable solely from the revenues derived from the projects. A revolving fund was created for security and collateral for certificates issued by the Board. The Board was allowed, in the event of default, to transfer monies from the debt service reserve fund to the debt service fund. The court found that the guarantee by the State of the loans to the public entities was an unconstitutional assumption by the State of debts, in violation of Okla. Const. art. X, §§ 14, 15. Thus, Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1085.41 (Supp. 1982), allowing for the pledge for collateral or security, violated Okla. Const. art. X, §§ 14, 15, as a pledge or lending of the State's credit. The court held that an invalid provision of a statute could not be made valid because of an apparent need for the proposed law. The constitutional restraints were insurmountable blocks to the approval of the Board's bond program.


OUTCOME: The court assumed jurisdiction and granted a writ of prohibition.

Callison v. Callison


No. 55,890


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1984 OK 7; 687 P.2d 106; 1984 Okla. LEXIS 106



March 13, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 18, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division I. Appellant appeals from the judgment of the district court which determined that he was the father of a minor child in an action initiated pursuant to 12 O.S. 1981 § 1277.2. On certiorari, the appellant alleges that the Court of Appeals erred in its holding that he had waived the argument that the three-year statute of limitations, prescribed by 10 O.S. 1981 § 83, was applicable; that the court lacked jurisdiction to determine paternity pursuant to 12 O.S. 1981 § 1277.2; and that HLA blood tests are inadmissible in paternity proceedings.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED. OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED. JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division I (Oklahoma), which held on certiorari that he waived the argument that the three-year statute of limitations to bring a suit for child support for an illegitimate child was applicable, that the lower court lacked jurisdiction to determine paternity, and that Human Leukocyte Antigen (HLA) blood tests were inadmissible in paternity proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellee mother brought suit against the putative father for divorce alleging a common-law marriage. The mother requested custody of the child born during the relationship and child support. The mother abandoned her attempt to prove the marriage, and asked that the lower court determine whether the putative father was indeed the father of the child. The lower court found the HLA test results, and other supportive evidence sufficient to establish paternity. The putative father was ordered to pay child support and attorney's fees. The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals and affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court held as follows: 1) the lower court had jurisdiction to determine paternity pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1277.2 (1981); 2) the three-year limitation period provided in Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 83 (1981) resulted in a denial of equal protection of the laws and the issue of whether the putative father had waived the defense of the statute of limitations was immaterial; and 3) the lower court had every right to take judicial notice of the HLA test and the test results.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals and affirmed the judgment of the lower court awarding child support to the mother.

In re Polin


No. 60,342


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 111; 675 P.2d 1013; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 249; 44 A.L.R.4th 1199



November 29, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected On Denial of Rehearing January 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable Robert D. Frank, Special Judge. The parents of an eighteen year old congenitally deaf woman brought this action to declare their daughter incompetent to manage her person and estate, and therefore in need of supervision. After a lengthy trial, Special Judge Robert D. Frank found Ms. Polin to be "judgmentally immature", capable of being manipulated by "artful and designing persons", and therefore incompetent under 58 O.S. 1981 §§ 851-852. This overbroad construction of Oklahoma's guardianship statues results in a chilling infringement of Ms. Polin's fundamental constitutional right to free exercise of her religious beliefs and the decision is therefore REVERSED with directions to vacate order appointing guardian and dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents appealed a judgment from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) that, in petitioner parents' action, declared the parents' daughter to be incompetent under Okla. Stat. tit. 58, §§ 851-852.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was 18 years old and was congenitally deaf and she had average to above average intelligence. Her parents were Jewish and raised her in that faith. The daughter became exposed to Christianity and expressed her interest in that faith. Her father forbade her from practicing that faith and, ultimately, the daughter moved away from her parents' home after she insisted on practicing that faith. Alleging that a certain Christian sect was brainwashing her, the parents filed a petition to have her declared incompetent and for guardianship. The trial court found that the daughter was "judgmentally immature", capable of being manipulated by "artful and designing persons", and therefore incompetent. On appeal, the court ruled that the case, prompted by familial disagreement, resulted in misconstruction of the incompetency statutes and in an intolerable chilling of the daughter's fundamental constitutional right of freedom of religion. The "artful and designing persons test" was inapplicable in cases when its application invaded the area of personal ideas, thoughts, and beliefs. The "judgmentally immature" standard used by the trial court did not satisfy any test for incompetency.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Tulsa Indus. Auth. v. State


No. 57,107

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Honorable William S. Myers, Trial Judge. Action under Declaratory Judgments Act (12 O.S.1981, § 1651, et seq.) seeking declaratory judgment that 60 O.S.1981, § 178.8 is not constitutionally infirm under Art. 10, § 11 of the Oklahoma Constitution, and for a determination that the Attorney General's opinion holding the statute to be unconstitutional be determined to be invalid and of no effect. From a judgment entered by the court below determining said statute to be constitutional in part and unconstitutional in part, plaintiffs below appeal, and defendants below cross-appeal.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND CAUSE DISMISSED FOR WANT OF A JUSTICIABLE CONTROVERSY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff local authorities appealed and defendants, the State of Oklahoma and its attorney general, cross-appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma finding Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 178.8 (1981) constitutional only in part in an action to invalidate the attorney general's opinion that § 178.8 violated Okla. Const. art. 10, § 11 brought under the Declaratory Judgments Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1651 et seq (1981).


OVERVIEW: Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 178.8 (1981) purported to make lawful five categories of contractual relationships between public trusts and their trustees. The State and the attorney general contended on appeal that the trial court erred in ruling that it had jurisdiction, that the local authorities were the real parties in interest, and that there existed an actual justiciable controversy, and they argued that it was error for the trial court to render an advisory opinion. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause with directions. The court noted that the record was devoid of any evidence or finding by the trial court of any specific instances wherein any of the local authorities had engaged in conduct within the facially authorized exceptions set forth, that there was no showing of any actual controversy between the local authorities and the State which permitted adjudication of any present rights, and that the case fell short of meeting any of the requisite facts or conditions which had to be met in order to invoke declaratory relief. The court held that the local authorities had not presented a justiciable cause which could be fairly adjudicated in the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court finding a statute constitutional in part and unconstitutional in part in the local authorities' declaratory judgment action against the State and the attorney general and remanded the cause with directions to dismiss.

No. 58,432


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 96; 675 P.2d 134; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 236



October 11, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected on Petition for Rehearing January 10, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court, Rogers County. Byron Ed Williams, Judge. Defendants appeal from summary judgment rested on the second of the plaintiff's two alternative pleas for recovery, while plaintiff counter-appeals from denial of its first theory for relief.



DISPOSITION: SUMMARY JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Northwest Rogers County Fire Protection District (Oklahoma), sought review of a decision by the District Court, Rogers County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff utility company regarding the district's tax assessment. The utility sought review of the district court's decision upholding the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 19, §§ 901.1-901.26 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The district assessed a property tax pursuant to the Fire Protection District Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 19, §§ 901.1-901.26 (1981) on property owners in the county in order to finance its fire protection operation. The utility paid the amount due, then challenged the validity of the assessment, arguing that the Act was unconstitutional or that the assessment was unlawful pursuant to Okla. Const. art. 10, § 7. The district court held the Act was constitutional, but the means of assessing the tax was not. On appeal, the court stated that the district did not constitute a county corporation under § 7. The court also held that there was legislative authority for the Act pursuant to Okla. Const. art. 5, § 36. The district could not levy ad valorem tax because it would be unconstitutional pursuant to Okla. Const. art. 10, § 9. However, the court noted that the fire protection was a local improvement even though it did not manifest its physical presence upon the affected property until a fire arose because it was established exclusively for the benefit of the property. In conclusion the court held that the assessment was a special assessment and lawful under the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's grant in favor of plaintiff and remanded the issue for further review.

GMC v. OKLAHOMA CTY. BD. OF EQUALIZATION


No. 58,438


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 Okla. LEXIS 216



July 26, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motor corporation challenged a decision from respondents, the Oklahoma County Board of Equalization, the county assessor, the county treasurer, and the Attorney General of Oklahoma, which denied the corporation ad valorem tax relief that it sought on the ground that a purported tax abatement contract was void.


OVERVIEW: The corporation had entered into a tax abatement agreement with a state official, which was not in accord with Oklahoma law at the time it was made. The legislature had no authority to grant the tax exemption. The corporation sought retroactive application based upon its reliance on the contract and challenged its requirement to pay ad valorem taxes. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that where the legislature was without constitutional authority to grant a tax exemption, then state officials could also not grant the exemption. The corporation was charged with notice of the state constitution and the limitations of public officials, and the court held that it could not rely on assumed authority by the legislature or public officials. The court held that the agreement was void because no public official could constitutionally grant the tax exemption allegedly contained in the agreement. Since the alleged agreement was unenforceable, the corporation was not entitled to the tax relief it sought. The court held that a contract which rested on an unconstitutional statute was itself void and created no obligation to be impaired by subsequent legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

232 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Okla. Alcoholic Bev. Control Bd. v. Parkhill Rests., Inc.


No. 52,566


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 77; 669 P.2d 265; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 211



July 5, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 4, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable Richard V. Armstrong, Trial Judge. Appeal from a judgment of the trial court determining that certain portions of Laws 1959, p.161, § 39, now 37 O.S. 1981, § 539, and Laws 1961, p.281, § 1, now 37 O.S. 1981, § 568, are unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma Alcoholic Control Board challenged a judgment from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which determined that Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 539, 568 (1981) of the Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 502 et seq. (1981) were unconstitutional and directed alcoholic beverages seized thereunder to be returned to appellee restaurant.


OVERVIEW: Incident to the arrest of restaurant employees, agents of the Board and police conducted a warrantless search of the premises and seized 400 bottles of alcoholic beverages. Individual "members" of the "club" labeled some of the bottles as belonging to them. The restaurant moved for an immediate hearing at which the district court held that the bottles were not subject to forfeiture. The district court held that the forfeiture provisions of the Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Act were "overbroad" because they permitted seizure of all alcoholic beverages in the possession of one who had violated the open saloon law, rather than limiting seizure to alcoholic beverages which constituted contraband. On appeal, the court held that seizure was limited to those bottles for which there was probable cause to believe they were possessed or used in violation of the Act. An important governmental interest outweighed any temporary loss of lawfully possessed property, justifying seizure of the alcoholic beverages before a hearing. Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 539 (1981) was not unconstitutional for lack of due process in failing to provide for notice and hearing prior to seizure of the liquor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court that held sections of the Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Act unconstitutional and remanded the cause for action consistent with its opinion.

 

233 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Miskovsky v. Tulsa Tribune Co.


No. 55,430


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 73; 678 P.2d 242; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 207; 9 Media L. Rep. 1954



June 21, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 20, 1983..


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Creek County, Oklahoma. Honorable Charles S. Woodson, Trial Judge. Appeal from an order of the trial court sustaining a demurrer to the original petition and to the amended petition in a libel case, and determining that the petition's defects are not amendable.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney appealed an order from the District Court of Creek County, Oklahoma, sustaining a demurrer to the original petition and to the amended petition in the attorney's libel case against defendants, a publisher and a printing corporation, and determining that the defects in the attorney's petition were not amendable.


OVERVIEW: The amended petition of the attorney, who was a public figure, alleged the publication by the publisher of nine separate items in the newspaper, alleged to be libelous. After a careful review of the publications both separately and together, the court found that none of them, nor all of them collectively, stated a cause of action for libel per se. None of the publications charged the attorney with a commission of a crime. Nor did they expose the attorney to public hatred, contempt, ridicule or obloquy, or tend to deprive him of public confidence, or injure him in his occupation within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1441 (1981). The attorney's amended petition was demurrably deficient in its failure to aver how the special damages were occasioned. The court held that the amended petition was fatally deficient in allegations of innuendo sufficient to withstand a demurrer. The court further held that all of the publications were clear and unequivocal in their meaning and import and, therefore, immutable to innuendo.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling sustaining defendants' demurrers to the attorney's original and amended petition and determining that the petition's defects were not amendable.

GMC v. Okla. County Bd. of Equalization


No. 58,438


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 59; 678 P.2d 233; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 186



May 17, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 2, 1983; As Amended on Grant of Rehearing July 26, 1983. Opinion Supplemented and Rehearing on Amended Opinion Denied October 4, 1983. Reported at: 678 P.2d 233 at 238. Order for Stay of Mandate October 4, 1983, Reported at: 678 P.2d 233 at 241.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court, Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Honorable Jack R. Parr, District Judge. George Keyes, County Assessor of Oklahoma County, issued to appellant, General Motors Corporation, a "Notice of Change of Assessed Valuation" on the General Motor's Assembly Plant located in Oklahoma City, Oklahoma. General Motors filed a protest with the Oklahoma County Board of Equalization and it denied the protest. General Motors appealed the denial of its protest to the District Court. The disputed taxes were paid under protest and General Motors filed suit for refund. The District Court rendered summary judgment in favor of defendant public officials (appellees) and General Motors appealed.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision of the Oklahoma County District Court (Oklahoma), which rendered summary judgment in favor of appellee public officials, in a tax protest action brought by the landowner.


OVERVIEW: A public trust sponsored the financing for the construction of the landowner's assembly plant. The county assessor issued to the landowner a notice of change of assessed valuation on the plant. In response, the landowner filed protest with the board of equalization, which protest was denied. Under protest, the landowner paid the disputed taxes and sought review of the denial. The district court rendered summary judgment in favor of the public officials. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The court found that trust properties in which private entities held a possessory and contractual interest by virtue of a lease agreement with a public trust as holder of legal title should be subject to ad valorem taxation. The court added that although property that belonged to a public trust should be exempt from taxation under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 6, the interest the landowner had in public trust property was subject to ad valorem taxation because the landowner was a lessee. The court held that the landowner's property was subject to the taxes in question unless the disputed tax abatement agreement was legally enforceable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the public officials.

McCarroll v. Doctors Gen. Hosp.


No. 55,893


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 54; 664 P.2d 382; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 190



May 10, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Honorable Stewart Hunter, Trial Judge. Appeal from an order of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of Appellee Doctors General Hospital by reason of the bar of 76 O.S. 1981, § 18.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant hospital in a medical malpractice action on the basis of the statute of limitations, Okla. Stat. tit. 76, § 18 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The statute provided a two-year limitations period. The patient alleged that she did not immediately learn and was unable to discover with reasonable diligence the existence of the injuries because her doctor misled her as to the cause of her symptoms. The court held that the statute, which applied only to health care providers, was constitutional because the legislature could classify similar businesses for special legislative treatment where such classifications were not arbitrary. Because the patient filed her action within two years of the date when she claimed to have learned of her injuries, the action was timely brought. It was for the jury to resolve the factual disputes regarding when the patient knew or should have learned of her injuries.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment order and remanded with directions to proceed further.

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT ON HEARING OF APPLICATION FOR CUSTODY FOR PURPOSES OF ADOPTION AND ON WRIT OF HABEAS CORPUS REVERSED; MOTION OF MICHAEL H. AND EUGENIA T. TO DISMISS APPEAL OF DEPARTMENT OF HUMAN SERVICES DENIED; APPLICATION OF KENNETH J. AND DEBRA D. FOR AN INJUNCTION ENJOINING EUGENIA T. FROM ADOPTING CHILDREN DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Human Services (DHS) and intervenors, prospective adoptive parents, sought review of the order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted a writ of habeas corpus prayed for by appellee applicants and directed DHS to relinquish physical custody of two dependent children and deliver them to the applicants. By order of the court, the trial court's orders were stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: In prior proceedings, a court adjudicated that two young children were deprived, and terminated the parental rights of their natural parents. The juvenile division of the district court committed custody of the children to the DHS, with authority to place them for adoption. The district court reserved the right to consent to adoption. Two days later the DHS placed the children with the prospective adoptive parents. The court-appointed attorney of record for the children, who was a member of the Public Defender's office, then announced in open court that she and her husband would like to apply to adopt the children. She filed a successful writ of habeas corpus petition seeking custody. The court held that DHS Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1115.1 enjoined upon DHS the preparation of a placement plan for a deprived child, and found that DHS performed it duties in a lawful manner and as specifically authorized by the district court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granting the applicants' petition for custody for purposes of adoption and writ of habeas corpus seeking custody.
