In re De Annexation of Certain Real Prop.


No. 57,803


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 44; 662 P.2d 1375; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 178



April 26, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Leflore County, Oklahoma. Honorable Pat Pate, Presiding. Appellees petitioned the Town of Talihina to detach from the Town's corporate limits certain property. Town denied the petition for detachment and appellees appealed to the district court pursuant to 11 O.S. 1981, § 21-106. The district court ordered the property detached and Town appealed.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Leflore County (Oklahoma), which ordered land owned by appellee property owners detached from the town's corporate limits.


OVERVIEW: The town denied the property owners' petition for detachment and they appealed to the district court pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 21-106 (1981). The district court ruled in favor of the owners and the town sought further review. On appeal, the court overturned the judgment. The court held that whether property should or should not be annexed to or detached from the corporate limits of a municipality was purely legislative. The court ruled that although the courts could have determined whether a governing board had acted within the scope of its legislative authority and whether such action was reasonable or unreasonable, the courts could not have determined whether a petition for annexation or detachment should have been granted and could have been granted without injustice to the inhabitants or persons interested. The court concluded that the determination was purely legislative and that Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 21-107 (1981) imposing such a duty on the judiciary was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and remanded for further proceedings.

 

238 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bass v. Justus (In re V.A.J.)


No. 55,187


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 23; 660 P.2d 139; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 159



March 15, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Oklahoma County. William C. Kessler, Judge. Divorced natural father, incarcerated under a life sentence for murder, appeals from trial court's order declaring his natural son eligible for adoption without paternal consent.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant divorced natural father sought review of an order of the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which declared his natural son eligible for adoption without paternal consent.


OVERVIEW: The father and appellee natural mother had a child. The father was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. The father and the mother divorced, and the divorce decree imposed no support obligation on the father. The mother was awarded custody of the child. After the mother's remarriage, appellee custodial stepfather sought to adopt the child without the father's consent. Over the father's objection, the trial court granted the adoption pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 60.6(3) (Supp. 1974), finding that the father had wilfully failed to provide any monetary support. In reversing on appeal, the court held that the father's meager monthly stipend could not be considered as a resource in gauging the father's ability to contribute. Moreover, imprisonment could not be equated with a wilful failure to contribute to the child's support under § 60.6(3) because the incarceration prevented the father from making any contribution to the child's support. The trial court erroneously relied on the father's incarceration as a ground for dispensing with his consent to the adopt, and the order allowing adoption without the father's consent was contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which declared the father's natural son eligible for adoption without paternal consent.

Mistletoe Express Serv. v. UPS


No. 56,150


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 27; 674 P.2d 1; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 158



March 15, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 10, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Honorable Carmon C. Harris, Trial Judge. Appeal from a judgment of the district court determining that the Restricted Parcel Carriers Act, 47 O.S.Supp. 1980, §§ 166.1 to 166.5 is constitutional.



DISPOSITION:  JURISDICTION UNDER THE DECLARATORY JUDGMENTS ACT WITH REFERENCE TO RULES AND REGULATIONS OF THE OKLAHOMA CORPORATION COMMISSION DENIED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT OTHERWISE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant carrier filed a complaint against appellee competitor challenging the constitutionality of the Restricted Parcel Carriers Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 47, §§ 166.1 to 166.5 (Supp. 1980). The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) held that the Act was constitutional. The action was brought under the Declaratory Judgments Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, §§ 1651 to 1657 (1981). The carrier challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The competitor had applied for a certificate from the Corporation Commission. The carrier challenged the Act's constitutionality. The trial court held that the Act was constitutional. The court affirmed. The Act did not violate Okla. Const. art. 5, § 57, which provided that legislative acts could embrace but one subject. Section 57 related to "every act of the legislature" and not to constitutional amendments. Second, the only limitations imposed upon a constitutional amendment under Okla. Const. art. 9, § 35, were that the constitutional enactment had to have occurred after the second Monday in January 1901, and that its operational effect had to have been confined to Okla. Const. art. 9 §§ 18 to 34, inclusive. The intention to amend the constitution with reference to Okla. Const. art. 9, §§ 18 to 34 of was clearly manifested in the language of § 5 of the Act. The Act was complete within itself and removed from the mischief Okla. Const. art. 5, § 57 was designed to avoid. The Act established a rational classification of restricted parcel carriers reasonably related to the public interest and not in violation of the Equal Protection Clause or the Oklahoma Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court denied jurisdiction under the Declaratory Judgment Act with respect to the rules and regulations of the Oklahoma Corporation Commission and otherwise affirmed.

 

240 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re Schrader


No. 55,967


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 19; 660 P.2d 135; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 154



March 1, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Appeals, Div. II. The City of Bethany appealed the granting of a zoning ordinance variance to the District Court of Oklahoma County. The District Court sustained appellant's demurrer to the evidence on the basis that the landowner did not present evidence sufficient to establish a right to a variance. This action was appealed and the cause was assigned to the Court of Appeals, Division II, for determination of constitutional infirmity allegedly arising from the vague nature of the ordinance and the power of the Board of Adjustment to rule on constitutional objections.



DISPOSITION: OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; DECISION OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner obtained a variance from the city board of adjustment. Appellee city sought review and the trial court set aside the board's decision. On appeal by the landowner, the Court of Appeals, Division II (Oklahoma) reversed and remanded with directions to reinstate the decision of the board. A writ of certiorari had previously been issued to review the case.


OVERVIEW: The landowner built a carport without obtaining a building permit. After the city notified her that the structure did not comply with the zoning ordinance, she applied for and was granted a variance by the board of adjustment. The trial court set aside the board of adjustment's decision. The court of appeals reversed. On writ of certiorari, the court of appeals' opinion was vacated and the trial court's decision was affirmed. The court held that the board of adjustment did not have the authority to determine the constitutionality of the ordinance, but the trial court did have such authority. Although the trial court did not state that the ordinance was constitutional, that ruling was implicit in its judgment. The words "building" and "structure" as defined in the ordinance gave fair notice to the landowner that she was prohibited from placing a carport in front of the minimum setback line. Thus, the ordinance was not vague as applied to her. The landowner was not entitled to a variance pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 44-407 (1981) because any hardship was created by her, the hardship was not peculiar to her property, and the variance would impair the intent of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals and affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Roberts v. Roberts


No. 55,069


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1983 OK 1; 657 P.2d 153; 1983 Okla. LEXIS 135



January 11, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Clifford E. Hopper, District Judge. Appellee filed an application to modify award of support alimony granted in divorce decree, on grounds of a substantial change in circumstances relating to need for such support, citing 12 O.S. Supp. 1979, § 1289(D), in that appellant was living in a "private conjugal relationship." Trial court granted the relief and appellant appeals on grounds of unconstitutionality of the statute and sufficiency of the evidence.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee former husband filed an application to modify an award of support alimony granted in a divorce decree on the grounds of a substantial change in circumstances relating to need for such support, citing Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1289(D) (Supp. 1979), in that appellant former wife was living in a private conjugal relationship. The District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) granted the relief. The wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties were granted a divorce. The husband was ordered to pay $ 10,000 in support alimony in three payments. After the first payment, the husband filed a motion to modify the divorce decree by terminating the other payments based on the wife's cohabitation, which motion was granted. On appeal, the wife challenged the constitutionality of § 1289(D), which made the voluntary cohabitation with a member of the opposite sex a ground for reducing or terminating support alimony so long as a substantial change of circumstances relating to need for support or ability to support was also proved. The wife also alleged that the trial court erred in finding a substantial change of circumstances and in finding that a private conjugal relationship existed. On appeal, the court affirmed the modification of the divorce decree, reasoning that there was nothing unconstitutional in § 1289(D). The purpose of the statute was not to regulate morality but rather to regulate support maintenance when the need for continued support had diminished or vanished. Absent an abuse of discretion, the court refused to reverse the discretionary decision of the trial court based on the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's modification of the divorce decree, terminating the husband's obligation to make additional payments of alimony based a substantial change in circumstances relating to need for such support.

Guy H. James Constr. Co. v. Okla. ex rel. Okla. DOT


No. 54,006


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 150; 655 P.2d 553; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 325



December 14, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. This was a declaratory judgment action wherein on Motion for Summary Judgment by Appellee, 61 O.S.1971, § 16 was ruled unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma Department of Transportation (DOT) sought review of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment to appellee construction company in its declaratory judgment action and declared that Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 16 (1971) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The construction company filed the instant action for declaratory relief to determine the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 16 (1971), which authorized the DOT and other state agencies to withhold money due on contract when the withholding was triggered by an unverified claim of an alleged creditor. The trial court held that § 16 was unconstitutional because it did not accord with due process and it afforded neither prior notice nor opportunity to be heard by the alleged debtor. The court affirmed, holding that depriving a general contractor of the use of money earned constituted interference with a significant properly interest to which the requirements of due process attached. The court found that § 16 failed to meet the constitutional standard for procedural due process because it did not address emergency situations, it had no provisions for prior notice or hearing, it failed to establish alternative safeguards for due process, and it was fatally imprecise as to what information was necessary for an alleged creditor to file a claim. The court also found that § 16 did not require alleged claims to be verified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re J.N.M.


No. 51,761


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 153; 655 P.2d 1032; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 330



December 14, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Woodward County, Honorable Ray Don Jackson, Judge. Appeal by natural parents of three children previously adjudicated deprived from judgment terminating their parental rights.



DISPOSITION:  JUDGMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged the judgment of the District Court of Woodward County (Oklahoma), which terminated their parental rights pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (1981) on the grounds that the parents' mental illness rendered them mentally incompetent to care for their children.


OVERVIEW: After the parents were found mentally incompetent and their children were declared dependent and neglected, the state sought termination of their parental rights pursuant to § 1130. The trial court terminated their rights, and the parents appealed. The court reversed, holding that although the parents had been diagnosed with mental illnesses, that fact alone was insufficient to form the basis of the termination of their parental rights under § 1130. The state did not present sufficient evidence to show a compelling interest in protecting the children from harm that required the intrusion into the family unit. Specifically, the court noted that the parents' mental illness, the effect on the children, and the parent's psychological outlook were not explained in any detail. Moreover, the certificates of sanity provided for in Okla. Admin. Code § 43A-55.2 (1981) did not serve the purpose of proving the requisite evidence in a termination of parental rights proceeding. Because the record did not show the requisite quantum of evidence that the mental illness of the parents posed actual or imminent harm to the children, the action was remanded for further fact finding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action for further proceedings.

Okla. v. County Bev. License No. ABL-78-145 of McMar Gen. Stores

Supreme Court of Oklahoma

Action by State of Oklahoma to revoke alcoholic beverage licenses for wrongful sales to minors. Purported appeal as against all defendants below dismissed except McMar General Stores, d/b/a McMar No. 2. McMar General Stores' Motion to Quash was sustained on the basis that 37 O.S.1971, §§ 241, 242 were held unconstitutional under Craig v. Boren, 429 U.S. 190, 97 S. Ct. 451, 50 L. Ed. 2d 397 (1976).



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error State of Oklahoma filed a petition in error from orders of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma) that were granted in favor of defendants in error, businesses with alcoholic beverage licenses. The district court sustained the businesses' motions to quash the State's 20 separate actions because a controlling precedent held that Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 245 (1971) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The State filed the actions against the businesses to revoke their licenses based on their wrongful sales to minors. The court reversed the contested order. The court dismissed the State's petition with respect to all but one of the businesses. The court determined that the State failed to file a petition in all 19 cases within 30 days from the contested order's date. The court found that the one timely filed petition did not include the other 19 actions and only referred to them as separate matters. The court ordered stricken the State's amended petition in error because Okla. Sup. Ct. R. 1.17(a) did not provide for amendment to substitute parties. The court declined to apply the rule so as to contravene the valid time limitation statute of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 990 (1971). The trial court incorrectly found that Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 241-242 (1971) was invalidated by the precedent's declaration that the definition of a minor in Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 245 (1971) was unconstitutional. The court held that the precedent did not affect the validity of Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 241-242 and that it reactivated the definition of a minor in Okla. Stat. tit. 15, § 13 (Supp. 1972).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the State's appeal as against all the businesses except for one. The court reversed as to that party.

Smith v. Smith


No. 55,082


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 115; 652 P.2d 297; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 269



October 5, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. David Winslow, District Judge. Trial court granted appellee's motion to modify support alimony based on 12 O.S. Supp. 1979, § 1289(D). Appellant challenges the retrospective application of 12 O.S. Supp. 1979, § 1289(D), dealing with modification of support alimony when the recipient voluntarily cohabits with a member of the opposite sex.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former wife challenged orders of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) that granted appellee former husband's motion to modify support alimony on the ground that the wife was voluntarily cohabiting with a member of the opposite sex under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1289(D) (Supp. 1979). The trial court granted the modification, terminated all future alimony payments and ordered each party to pay his or her own attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The parties' decree of divorce was granted before the effective date of § 1289(D). The decree directed the husband to pay support alimony in seven annual installments. His motion alleged that the wife's need for alimony had changed because of her cohabitation with a member of the opposite sex. The wife challenged the constitutionality of applying § 1289(D) to a judgment rendered before the statute's effective date. The trial court overruled her special demurrer. The court reversed the order. No language in § 1289(D) either expressly or impliedly indicated a legislative intent to give retrospective effect to the statute. Statutes were to be construed as having prospective operation unless a contrary intent was expressly indicated. Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1289(a) (Supp. 1979), pertaining to the termination of alimony on the recipient's remarriage, had already been held to have no application when a divorce was granted before its passage. The trial court did not err in refusing to grant attorney fees to the wife.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that overruled the wife's special demurrer and ordered the trial court to vacate its order terminating support alimony payments to the wife and to reduce arrearages to judgment.

 

247 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Tex. Okla. Express v. Sorenson


No. 56,273


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 113; 652 P.2d 285; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 270



October 5, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding to review an order of the Workers' Compensation Court sitting en banc awarding compensation for permanent partial disability,. Honorable Charles L. Cashion, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AWARD SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent employer sought review of an order of the Workers' Compensation Court (Oklahoma) that awarded claimant employee compensation for permanent partial disability. The employer contended, in part, that the trial court improperly admitted evidence and that Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 3.6 (1981), which required the employer to give a written undertaking to the employee before it could proceed with an appeal, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee's workers' compensation claim form alleged an injury to his left arm. The trial court's finding that suffered an accidental injury to his left hand, resulting in permanent partial disabled was affirmed by the workers' compensation court en banc. On appeal, the court held that the erroneous description of the employee's injury on his claim form was harmless error because the employer had not objected to the inaccuracy as required by Workers' Comp. Ct. R. 21. For the same reason, the employer's failure to object, the trial court's acts of conducting a physical examination of the employee's hand in open court and consideration of a medical report in an improper form, were not reversible errors. The court considered and rejected the employer's argument that Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 3.6 was unconstitutional under the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment, Okla. Const. art. 2, § 7; art. 5, § 46, holding that the statute was not only bottomed on a rational basis, but that it served a public interest, and the distinction and classification drawn by the statute withstood the inspection of scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the workers' compensation court's en banc decision affirming an award of permanent partial disability to the employee.

 

248 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Heisler v. Thomas


No. 55,888


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 105; 651 P.2d 1330; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 263



September 28, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Payne County, Oklahoma. Ray Lee Wall, District Judge. Appeal by the City of Stillwater from an order permanently enjoining the enforcement of a zoning ordinance.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the District Court of Payne County (Oklahoma) that granted an injunction to appellee landowner that permanently enjoined the city from enforcing a zoning ordinance to prohibit the landowner from using his property consistent with his request for a zoning change.


OVERVIEW: A city zoning map indicated that the landowner's property was zoned for multifamily residences, but when the landowner prepared to sell the property, it was discovered that the property's original single-family classification had never been changed. The city denied the landowner's request for a rezoning to allow twice the number of dwelling units, and the landowner filed his action for an injunction. Witnesses for the city testified that the zoning change would increase traffic congestion, noise, and flood danger, but the trial court found that the evidence did not establish that the zoning change would substantially increase these dangers as compared to single-family zoning. The court reversed the judgment. A municipality's legislative action in establishing a zoning classification was controlling if the classification's validity was fairly debatable. The evidence established that either the existing single-family classification or the requested rezoning would have been reasonable. The factors relied upon by the city in denying the rezoning were legitimate concerns, and its action was neither arbitrary nor an unequal exercise of police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment.

Democratic Party of Okla. v. Estep


No. 54,538


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 106; 652 P.2d 271; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 292



September 28, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 30, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding for a Prerogative Writ. The Democratic Party of Oklahoma seeks to compel respondents' performance of duties prescribed by the Oklahoma Campaign Finance Act and to declare ineffective an Attorney's General opinion which invalidates those provisions of the Act which authorize distribution of certain public funds to eligible candidates for public office and to recognized political parties.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ASSUMED, WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, Democratic Party of Oklahoma and its members, brought a proceeding seeking a prerogative writ to compel respondents, members of the Oklahoma Campaign Commission, to perform its statutory duties under Okla. Stat. §§ 18-101 et seq. (1981), and to declare ineffective an Attorney's General opinion which invalidated portions of the Act. The Republican State Committee of Oklahoma was allowed to intervene in the case.


OVERVIEW: The court considered whether under the Oklahoma Campaign Finance Act, Okla. Stat. §§ 18-101 et seq. (1981), it was constitutionally permissible to use public funds in payment for campaign-related expenses of candidates for public office and of political parties. The court held that in order to test the constitutional validity of the Act, it looked to the policy of the law as declared by the Oklahoma Legislature, the standards to be followed by an agency in carrying out the policy laid down by the lawmakers, and to administrative rules fashioned to implement the legislative will. The court held that the controversy lacked justiciability because the Act was devoid of an articulate pronouncement of legislative policy that embodied standards or guidelines capable of administrative implementation.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioners' request for a prerogative writ to compel respondents to perform their statutory duties.

Conoco, Inc. v. State Dep't of Health of Okla.


No. 56,070


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 94; 651 P.2d 125; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 257



July 27, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 5, 1982. As Corrected August 19, 1982. As Corrected October 4, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court, Kay County. Lowell Doggett, Judge. District court action, under 75 O.S. 1981 § 306 of the Administrative Procedures Act, for declaratory relief from state regulation controlling emissions from industrial sources. Trial court rendered judgment against the defending agencies.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee petroleum corporation filed an action against appellant state agencies under Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 306 (1981) of the Administrative Procedures Act, seeking declaratory relief from a state regulation controlling emissions from industrial sources. The District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma) rendered judgment against the defending agencies, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the state agencies amended a regulation limiting the density of plumes emanating from pollutant facilities, the corporation objected to the regulation and petitioned the Air Quality Council for a four-year variance to permit the corporation time to bring its refinery into compliance. The Council granted the corporation only a one-year variance and upheld the regulation. The Council's decision was approved by the Board of Health and the corporation did not appeal from either decision. Subsequently, the corporation challenged the regulation in an action for declaratory relief pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 306 (1981) and obtained a judgment against the agencies. However, the judgment was reversed on appeal. The court reasoned that § 306 was not intended to allow an aggrieved party to seek a declaratory judgment after an agency's final order had been issued and the time to appeal from that order had expired. The court held that because the corporation failed to timely perfect an appeal from the agencies' order pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 318(2) (1981), the trial court lacked jurisdiction to entertain a challenge to the order by means of a declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

251 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cartwright


No. 58,686


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 82; 657 P.2d 142; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 314



July 15, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Order on Rehearing November 8, 1982. Rehearing Denied November 9, 1982, Reported at: 657 P.2d 142 at 147.


PRIOR HISTORY: State of Oklahoma, by and through the Attorney General, brought an original proceeding applying to the Supreme Court to assume original jurisdiction and to grant a writ of prohibition or other relief against a certain District Court Judge and Associate District Court Judges of the First Judicial District of the State of Oklahoma to prohibit them from further proceedings in pending cases on the ground that the Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge, Seventh Judicial District, State of Oklahoma, has exclusive jurisdiction over the subject matter of the suits pending in the First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED; CERTAIN PENDING PROCEEDINGS ARRESTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State filed an application for a writ of prohibition against respondent other judges, which sought to prohibit them from conducting proceedings in a pending case on the ground that a district judge had exclusive jurisdiction over the matter.


OVERVIEW: The State was the trustee over certain school lands and trusts. It filed three actions involving lands held by the trust. The cases were assigned to a district judge, who made findings and rulings on the cases. The State then filed an application for a writ of prohibition to prohibit the other judges from deciding any issues in the cases. In granting the writ, the court determined that the issues presented to the district judge fell within the orbit of the Uniform Trusts Act. There was nothing in the Act to exclude a district court's jurisdiction over a trust established for school lands and trusts, despite the fact that the lands were given by the federal government. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 175.23, the district judge had original jurisdiction over the case. Moreover, venue was proper in the county where the trustee resided. If the court did not act to confine the issues properly determinable under the Act, there was a possibility that two trial courts would have entered conflicting decrees in the case. Because jurisdiction was acquired by the district judge, no other court with concurrent jurisdiction was permitted to interfere.


OUTCOME: The court determined that until the cases had been resolved, the proceedings before the other judges were arrested.

State Question No. 556 v. Albert (In re Initiative Petition No. 317)


No. 57,824


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 78; 648 P.2d 1207; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 339



June 25, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 28, July 12 and July 20, 1982..


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING TO DETERMINE VALIDITY OF INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 317, STATE QUESTION NO. 556. The sufficiency of Initiative Petition No. 317, is challenged both numerically and legally. The Petition, if approved as State Question No. 556, would change the boundaries for Oklahoma's six congressional districts as established by the 1981 Legislature. INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 317 DECLARED SUFFICIENT, BOTH NUMERICALLY AND LEGALLY, FOR SUBMISSION TO THE VOTE OF THE PEOPLE AS STATE QUESTION NO. 556.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Protestants filed an action challenging the sufficiency, both numerically and legally, of an initiative petition, which sought to change the boundaries for Oklahoma's six congressional districts as established by the 1981 Legislature. Proponents sought to uphold the sufficiency of the petition. The proceeding was bifurcated by the court with reference to a referee to determine the numerical sufficiency of the petition.


OVERVIEW: Proponents circulated an initiative petition that sought to change the boundaries for Oklahoma's six congressional districts as established by the 1981 Legislature. Protestants challenged the petition's sufficiency, both legally and numerically. The court bifurcated the proceeding with reference to a referee to determine the numerical sufficiency of the petition. Thereafter, the court adopted the referee's opinion and declared the petition sufficient, legally and numerically, for submission to the vote of the people. In reaching its decision, the court held that proponents' invocation of Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 9(D) did not render the circulation period inoperative and such circulation within the 90-day period was proper. The court also rejected protestants' assertions that the petition violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 2 and 2 U.S.C.S. § 2a(c) and that the petition violated U.S. Const. art. 1, § 4 and 2 U.S.C.S. § 7.According to the court, the electorate was entitled to invoke the initiative against a legislative congressional redistricting act, even though the initiative and the legislative enactment occurred during the same 10-year period and were based upon the same federal census.


OUTCOME: The court adopted the referee's opinion with respect to numerical sufficiency. The court declared the initiative petition sufficient, both numerically and legally, for submission to the vote of the people.

Jackson v. Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 16


Nos. 53,985, 53,993 Consolidated under No. 53,985


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 74; 648 P.2d 26; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 232



June 8, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Payne County, Oklahoma, Honorable Ray Lee Wall, Judge. Patricia J. Jackson, a probationary teacher, appeals from a declaratory judgment by the trial court that 70 O.S. Supp. 1977 § 6-103.2 does not require notification, admonishment and time for correction of alleged teaching deficiencies before a probationary teacher may be nonreemployed based on the Superintendent's recommendation. The Board of Education appeals from a determination by the trial court that it must state reasons or findings for its decision to nonreemploy the probationary teacher at the conclusion of a due process hearing. The appeals were consolidated.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff probationary teacher appealed the order from the District Court of Payne County (Oklahoma), which declared that Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 6-103.2 (Supp. 1977) did not require defendant school board to notify a probationary teacher of alleged teaching deficiencies before such a teacher could be nonreemployed. The board appealed the determination that it must state its reasons for its decision not to nonreemploy a probationary teacher.


OVERVIEW: The probationary teacher taught sixth grade. Her principal rated her as professionally competent, but did not witness her performance at any time during the year. Her contract was not renewed by the board based on the recommendation of the superintendent, who refused to disclose any specific reasons for her nonreemployment. After a hearing, the school board affirmed the superintendent's action but failed to state reasons for its decision. The teacher filed a declaratory judgment action, and the trial court held that the teacher was not afforded due process because of the board's failure to state reasons or disclose the evidence upon which its decisions were made. It awarded damages of $ 1,000.00. It also held that the admonishment statute, § 6-103.2, was inapplicable because the principal had no reason to believe the teacher would be nonreemployed. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the provisions of § 6-103.4 (B) entitled a probationary teacher to a due process hearing and that she be given a general explanation of the basis of a decision. The court also found that § 6-103.2 was not to a condition precedent to nonreemployment and did not apply to the superintendent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order finding that the school board had to provide the probationary teacher with the reasons for its decisions and that a probationary teacher need not be admonished before the board could decide not to nonreemploy her.

Indep. Sch. Dist. # 52 v. Okla. Indus. Auth.


No. 55,313


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 70; 646 P.2d 1276; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 230



June 1, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Joe Cannon, District Judge. Appellants sought to intervene as necessary and indispensable parties under 60 O.S. 1971, § 175.23(C) and 12 O.S. 1971, § 236. Trial Court denied their application. They appeal.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED TO DISTRICT COURT TO ADMIT APPELLANTS AS NECESSARY PARTIES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school districts sought relief from a decision by the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which dismissed the school district's application to intervene as necessary and indispensable parties, under Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 175.23(C) (1971), in the action by respondent public trust against defendant county officials for a determination of the beneficiaries of its funds.


OVERVIEW: One of the public trust's statutory functions was to collect payments in lieu of ad valorem taxes and to distribute those payments to the county treasurer or to local units of government in areas impacted by the business making the payment. The public trust filed a demand that the district court determine the beneficiaries of its funds. The school districts filed an application to intervene as necessary and indispensable parties to the action. On appeal, the court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 175.23(C) (1971) specifically provided that if any action based on any act or obligation of any beneficiary to the public trust's funds were made, such beneficiary was a necessary party to the proceedings. Without doubt, the school districts were beneficiaries of the public trust. The public trust admitted as much when it conceded that the school districts received impacted aid from the public trust in the past and were guaranteed a constitutional minimum percentage of the public trust's funds. The school districts were statutorily authorized to be added as necessary parties to the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decision dismissing the school district's application to intervene.

First Nat'l Bank v. Faulkner (In re Davidson)


No. 54,878


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 27; 641 P.2d 1110; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 191



February 23, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Washington County; James H. Laughlin, Trial Judge. Appeal of declaratory judgment action apportioning tax under 68 O.S. Supp. 1974 § 825 and exempting charitable devisees from tax.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee, a bank, sought review of the declaratory judgment of the District Court of Washington County (Oklahoma), which apportioned estate tax among beneficiaries under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 825 and exempted charitable devisees from tax. The lower court granted the claim of appellee executrix for reimbursement by the trustee of federal and state estate inheritance taxes paid, prior to disbursement of the trust to the beneficiaries.


OVERVIEW: An executrix paid estate inheritance taxes, both federal and state. The executrix demanded reimbursement from the bank that was trustee of a trust included in decedent's estate for tax purposes, prior to the disbursement of the trust to the beneficiaries. The trustee requested the direction of the lower court as to how it should proceed. The lower court ruled that under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 825 the state and federal taxes were subject to apportionment and that the trust was required to contribute. The lower court also exempted charitable beneficiaries from contribution. The trustee sought review. On review, the court concluded that the trust beneficiaries rather than the trust should bear the responsibility for payment of the apportioned estate tax. The court also concluded that it should be the responsibility of the executrix to determine the apportioned share of tax, which each beneficiary should pay, and to demand payment of each beneficiary. The court found that the trustee should be responsible only for termination of the trust and distribution of the assets to the beneficiaries. The court affirmed the exemption of charitable beneficiaries from contribution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the lower court that a decedent's estate should not be responsible for the payment of federal and state estate taxes and held that trust beneficiaries, not a trust, should bear apportioned responsibility for this payment. The court reversed the formula for apportionment determined by the lower court and remanded for recalculation of each beneficiary's share.

Okla. Educ. Ass'n v. Nigh


No. 57,361


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1982 OK 22; 642 P.2d 230; 1982 Okla. LEXIS 218



February 16, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding on Application to Assume Original. Jurisdiction and Issue Writs of Mandamus and Prohibition. Original action by Petitioners against the Commissioners of the Land Office of the State of Oklahoma, and the Honorable George Nigh and other members, for writs of mandamus and prohibition. Original jurisdiction assumed for the sole purpose of considering the constitutionality of 64 O.S. 1971, § 86.1, § 89, 64 O.S. Supp. 1979, § 52(c), 64 O.S. Supp. 1974, § 100, and 64 O.S. Supp. 1976, § 260.2. We find that said statutes are violative of Article XI, Section 1, Section 2, and Section 5 of the Oklahoma Constitution, and the Enabling Act of June 16, 1906, 34 U.S. St. at Large, pp. 267-278.



DISPOSITION: EXTRAORDINARY RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens filed an original proceeding that requested writs of mandamus and prohibition against respondents, the Commissioners of the Land Office of the State of Oklahoma and a judge. The citizens contended that Okla. Stat. Tit. 64, §§ 86.1, 89, § 52(c), § 100, and § 260.2 violated the Oklahoma Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The statutes in question established maximum rents which the commissioners could charge when leasing preference right land. They limited the rent to between two percent and four percent of the land's value. The citizens contended that the statutes at issue prohibited the commissioners from complying with the terms and purposes of the Oklahoma Enabling Act, which established Oklahoma's School Land Trust. The citizens further asserted that the statutes prohibited the commissioners from complying with the duties imposed upon them as managers of the trust under Okla. Const. art. XI, §§ 1, 2, 5. Thus, the citizens argued that the statutes were unconstitutional. The commissioners had an irrevocable duty to manage the land trust under the Enabling Act. The citizens contended that the below-market statutorily set interest and rents was solely for the benefit of farmers and ranchers. The court agreed with the citizens' position. The court held that the State could not use school land trust fund assets to subsidize its highway construction program or to subsidize farming and ranching. Thus, the statutes violated the Oklahoma Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court granted the citizens' petition for a writ of mandamus and prohibition.

Supp. 1973 § 8. The apparent sufficiency of signatures affixed to the initiative petition is also challenged.

OVERVIEW: The court first questioned whether a determination of the constitutionality of the subject matter of certain sections of the petition could prevent a costly and useless election. Bd. of Regents of the Univ. of Okla. v. Baker


No. 56,116


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 160; 638 P.2d 464; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 324



December 22, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Cleveland County, Oklahoma. Alma Wilson, District Judge. Certain employees of the University of Oklahoma brought a mandamus action against the Board of Regents of the University of Oklahoma directing the Regents to grant them an increase in salary as prescribed by the Legislature. The district court granted the Writ of Mandamus and the Board of Regents appealed.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Regents of the University of Oklahoma sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which held that the increase in salary provisions in 1979 Okla. Sess. Laws 981 did not interfere with the Board's authority under Okla. Const. art. XIII, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to 1979 Okla. Sess. Laws 981, the legislature directed all state agencies, including the Board, to increase the salary of all employees. When the Board failed to raise salaries, a writ of mandamus was sought to compel the pay increase. After the writ was granted, the Board sought review, claiming that the legislature's increase in salary had interfered with the Board's authority under Okla. Const. art. XIII, § 8. Upon review, the court held that in elevating the Board's status from a statutory to a constitutional entity, the people had intended to limit legislative control over University affairs. The court held that § 8 had established the Board as an independent body charged with the power to govern the University and that the Board's determination of faculty salaries was an integral part of its power to govern the University and a function essential in preserving its independence. Consequently, the court held that the legislature's salary increase was in conflict with § 8 because the increase had interfered with the Board's authority to make salary decisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which held that a salary increase directed by the legislature did not interfere with the Board's constitutional authority.

 

259 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. COUNTY BEVERAGE


No. 53,694


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 Okla. LEXIS 348



November 17, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CLEVELAND COUNTY, OKLAHOMA.

Honorable Preston Trimble, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged the decision from the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which sustained the motion to quash, filed by appellee licensees, the State's petitions to revoke the licensees' alcoholic beverage licenses because their employees had wrongfully sold an alcoholic beverage to a male minor in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 241 and 242 (1971), which had been held unconstitutional by the U.S. Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: The United States Supreme Court, in Craig v. Boren, 429 U.S. 190, 209, 97 S. Ct. 451, 50 L. Ed. 2d 397, 414 (1976), declared that Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 245 (Supp. 1972) created an unconstitutional and arbitrary age difference between males and females in defining a minor in relation to the sale of certain types of alcoholic beverages. The State, under Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 241 and 242 (1971), attempted to revoke the alcoholic beverage licenses of the licensees for selling to minors, but the licensees' motion to quash was granted. On the State's appeal the court noted that the trial court's rationale that Craig v. Boren also held that §§ 241 and 242 were unconstitutional was erroneous. The court noted that the gender difference only regarded the disparity in the ages of males and females, not the regulation of the sale of alcohol to minors. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 15, § 13 (Supp. 1972), which established the age of majority for both sexes in civil matters, was still applicable. The court found this controlling and held that Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 241 and 242 were not unconstitutional and reversed the granting of the motion to quash.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment sustaining the motion to quash the revocation of the alcoholic beverage licenses of the licensees.

Jury awarded actual and punitive damages and trial court awarded attorney fees. Insurance company appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurance company appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) that awarded plaintiff insured actual and punitive damages and attorney fees in an action for breach of contract and bad faith.

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed on the grounds that the insurance company failed to preserve for review its objections to the jury instructions given. The court also affirmed the award of attorney fees and punitive damages as proper.

Kuykendall v. Corp. Comm'n


No. 52,877


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 105; 634 P.2d 711; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 278; 71 Oil & Gas Rep. 364



September 22, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma. Honorable Rex Privett, Hamp Baker, and Jan Eric Cartwright Commissioners. An appeal from an order of the Corporation Commission denying appellants' application to vacate prior final orders of the Commission establishing 1440-acre drilling and spacing units in the Hunton formation common source of supply underlying a certain land area in Beckham County, Oklahoma, and to establish 640-acre drilling and spacing units.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mineral interest owners sought review of the decision of appellee Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma, which denied their application to delete certain sections of land from a previous order of the Commission relating to drilling and spacing units for production of oil and gas from a certain geologic formation and to establish a smaller drilling and spacing unit for production from that formation.


OVERVIEW: The mineral interest owners requested the Commission to vacate its prior order establishing a 1440-acre drilling and spacing unit for production from certain formations and to establish a 640-acre drilling and spacing unit. The Commission granted the request for all but one formation. The mineral interest owners appealed the denial, arguing that there had been a change of conditions or change in the knowledge of conditions that would prevent or assist in preventing waste of mineral resources. The court noted that every person had the right to drill wells on his own land and take all the minerals that he was able to reduce to possession, subject to the power of the state to prevent waste. The court stated that if the practical recoverability of minerals would be affected by increasing or decreasing the size of a drilling or spacing unit, the Commission could consider such factors as constituting waste. The court concluded that the Commission had properly considered the price of gas upon the economic inducement to produce and properly determined that there was no substantial change of conditions or substantial change in knowledge of conditions since the prior orders were entered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Commission denying the mineral interest owners' request for a change in the drilling and spacing unit for a certain formation.

 

262 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Union Tex. Petroleum v. Corp. Comm'n


No. 53,181 (Surviving number), (Nos. 53,226, 53,227 and 53,259 consolidated)


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 86; 651 P.2d 652; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 346; 75 Oil & Gas Rep. 105



July 21, 1981 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 9, 1982, Dissenting Opn. March 9, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma. In an application for an order modifying a previous drilling and spacing unit order of the Corporation Commission, applicant sought to de-space one-section units and re-space those units at 160-acre parcels, alleging change of conditions and change of knowledge of conditions. The Corporation Commission granted the requested relief. Protestants allege such an order of modification is not supported by substantial evidence and was infirm by virtue of improper notice to certain parties, and they prosecute this appeal.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil companies sought review of an order of appellee Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma, which granted an application to modify a previous drilling and spacing unit order of the Commission by vacating the previously existing 640-acre drilling and spacing units and establishing 160-acre drilling and spacing units.


OVERVIEW: The Commission had previously permitted increased density of wells on the units upon application of the holders of the rights on that unit. The immediately preceding orders governing the drilling rights on the area involved found that one well was sufficient to drain each 640-acre-unit. On appeal, the court held that (1) the mailing of a notice of the application to one company at an incorrect address was sufficient because there was no evidence that actual notice was not received; (2) the Commission's order was a nullity as to another company because no notice was sent at all to that company; (3) the evidence supported the Commission's conclusion that there had been a change in condition to warrant a modification of the existing order because experience had taught that one well would not effectively drain a 640-acre unit; (4) decreasing the size of the well units, as opposed to allowing increased density, was an available remedy under Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 87.1(d) (Supp. 1978); and the companies could not complain that the Commission failed to re-space the entire source because they argued for piecemeal proceedings before the Commission.


OUTCOME: The order of the Commission was affirmed, provided that no part thereof was valid insofar as it affected the rights and interests of a company that did not receive notice, and it was reversed insofar as it attempted to adjudicate the rights of that company.

Way v. Grand Lake Ass'n


Nos. 56,406 (Consolidated with 56,731), 56,731 (consolidated with 56,406)


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 70; 635 P.2d 1010; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 294



June 9, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma. Honorable David M. Cook, Trial Judge. On February 6, 1981, the District Court of Oklahoma County, David M. Cook, Judge, issued a writ of mandamus in an action brought therefor by plaintiff, below, Grand Lake Association, Inc., an Oklahoma nonprofit corporation, directing the Oklahoma Tourism and Recreation Commission, Oklahoma Tourism and Recreation Department, Abe L. Hesser, and David W. Way, Director of State Finance, and each and all of them to immediately approve certain claims submitted by plaintiff for payment under the provisions of Laws 1979, c. 289, § 16, as amended, Laws 1980, c. 268, § 4, from the appropriations provided in 1980 Session Laws, c. 354, § 1 as required by law, and issue the warrants necessary for payment of said claims. David W. Way, as Director of State Finance, defendant below, appeals. On April 23, 1981, the same trial judge in another action appealed here under No. 56,731 granted identical relief upon the identical issues and that cause has been consolidated for the purposes of appeal under No. 56,406.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, defendant state director of finance sought review of a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted judgment in favor of plaintiff non-profit corporation in the corporation's mandamus action to compel payment of certain claims submitted under the provisions of 1979 Okla. Laws 289, § 16, as amended, 1980 Okla. Laws 268, § 5, and 1980 Okla. Laws 354.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed a suit seeking to compel payment of matching funds under the Oklahoma Tourism and Recreation Act. The trial court entered a peremptory writ of mandamus directing the state department of finance to pay the claims properly submitted by the corporation from the appropriations as required by law and issue the warrants necessary for payment. On appeal, the state department of finance contended that mandamus was not the proper remedy because there was an adequate remedy at law and that the corporation could not enforce an alleged contractual right by writ of mandamus. The court held that the allowance of payment of the claims under the circumstances was a ministerial act enjoined upon the state finance department by statute. Mandamus was an appropriate remedy under the facts and circumstances. The court found that the appropriation statutes were in the nature of a unilateral contract between an agency of state government and the corporation and therefore not in violation of Okla. Const. art X, § 15.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Associated Builders & Contrs. of Okla. v. State ex rel. Okla. Dep't of Labor


Nos. 52,089, cons. with 52,350


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 50; 628 P.2d 1156; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 207; 25 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 735; 93 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,333



April 28, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, Honorable Charles L. Owens, Judge. Appellant contractors brought action in the District Court of Oklahoma County seeking injunctive relief and declaratory judgment against the Commissioner of the Oklahoma Department of Labor alleging, inter alia, the Commissioner had failed to comply with the provisions of the Administrative Procedures Act, 75 O.S.1971, § 301, et seq., in establishing a prevailing wage under the Minimum Wages on Public Works Act, 40 O.S.1971, § 196.1, et seq; that the provisions of the Minimum Wages on Public Works Act are unconstitutional; and, that the contractors were denied due process of law by reason of failure of proper notice. The trial judge sustained a demurrer to the petition, with amendment thereto, and dismissed the action.



DISPOSITION:  JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractors challenged a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which sustained demurrers to their petition against appellee Commissioner of the Oklahoma Department of Labor and dismissed the action. The contractors sought injunctive relief and declaratory judgment against the Commissioner based his noncompliance with the Administrative Procedures Act (APA, Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 301, et seq. (1971).


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner made prevailing rate determinations according to the federal rates done by the U.S. Department of Labor according to the federal Davis-Bacon Act, 40 U.S.C.S. § 276a. A set of rules and regulations was issued and filed with the legislature for use by the state Department for such determinations. A hearing was conducted where the Commissioner made findings of fact and conclusions of law; however, no evidence was allowed. Previous hearings were held where evidence was heard. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the Department was subject to the provisions of the APA when making prevailing wage rate determinations and rules for use. The contractor's claim alleging insufficient notice failed when the facts showed that they were present at the hearings and had ample opportunity to be heard. Additionally, the contractors did not have standing to assert the unconstitutionality of the Minimum Wages on Public Works Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 196.1, et seq. (1971), based on vagueness of the terms "prevailing rate of wage" and "locality" because only a public body could be criminally liable for failure to pay such rates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Okla. Press Ass'n v. Piedmont Publ. Co. (In re Piedmont Publ. Co.)


No. 53,249


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 51; 628 P.2d 1163; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 209; 7 Media L. Rep. 1533



April 28, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An appeal from the District Court of Canadian County, Oklahoma, Honorable John V. Whelan, Judge. Appeal from order of trial court refusing to vacate judgment declaring appellee publishing company as qualified to publish legal notices and publications although appellee's newspaper was reproduced in another county.



DISPOSITION:  JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a corporation comprised of numerous legal newspapers and two individual publishers, challenged a decision from the District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma), which refused to vacate judgment declaring appellee, a publisher of a weekly newspaper, as qualified to publish legal notices and publications although appellee's newspaper was reproduced in another county allegedly in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 25, § 106 (Supp. 1977).


OVERVIEW: Appellee's newspaper was delivered to the United States mails at Piedmont, Oklahoma. It was written, typeset, cut and pasted, distributed, circulated, and advertising prepared from appellee's production facilities at Piedmont. However, the newspaper, in final form, was taken outside of the county for offset reproduction. Appellee petitioned the trial court for an order declaring it to be qualified to publish legal notices pursuant to § 106, which was granted. Appellants claimed that the act of "reproducing" was synonymous with "printing" and therefore appellee could not qualify to publish legal notices under § 106. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court had held in a 1973 amendment to § 106, that the word "printed" meant more than the simple act of reproduction. The court held that the amendment imposing restrictions on out-of-county printing related only to more substantial, integral, and important components of "printing" rather than reproduction only. Therefore, where the only act done out of the county was the mere reproduction of the finished product, appellee's newspaper was being "printed" within its county for the purposes of legal qualification under § 106.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Bd. of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Okla. v. Cryan


No. 52,579


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 52; 638 P.2d 437; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 230



April 28, 1981 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 18, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court in and for Tulsa County, Honorable Ronald N. Ricketts, Trial Judge. An appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, the Honorable Ronald N. Ricketts, presiding, from a judgment and sentence for indirect contempt. The contempt sentence was issued for violation of an injunction requiring appellant to cease the unauthorized practice of dentistry. The fine and punishment assessed for contempt under 59 O.S. 1971 § 328.49 were the minimum permissible sentence. Contemnor brings this appeal objecting to the existence of criminal attributes of the statutory penalty for contempt provided by the legislature for unauthorized practice.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma) that found him guilty of indirect contempt for failing to cease the unauthorized practice of dentistry and imposed a fine and punishment under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.49 (1971).


OVERVIEW: After it was determined that defendant was practicing dentistry without a license in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.49, the district court issued an injunction barring defendant from such further unauthorized practice. When it was subsequently learned that defendant continued to practice dentistry, contempt proceedings were instituted. After defendant was found to be in indirect contempt, the district court sentenced him to 30 days in the county jail and assessed a fine of $ 500. Defendant appealed. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's argument that the contempt adjudication did not serve the purpose of coercing compliance with the injunction where, although he had violated the injunction, he had not violated it within the last five months. An indirect contempt under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 565 (1971), was the willful disobedience of any court order, and defendant's violation of the district court's injunctive order rendered him susceptible to contempt proceedings. Further, Okla. Const. art. 2, § 25, contained no prohibition against a punitive sentence in an indirect contempt proceeding and did indicate that the district court could only act remedially.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

In re Estate of Bigheart

Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 40; 627 P.2d 1260; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 210



April 7, 1981 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] <DSPQ4>


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court, Osage County, Oklahoma, Honorable Mermon H. Potter, Trial Judge. Appellant, the surviving wife of a half-blood Osage Indian who died owning restricted property, appeals from the trial court's order denying her any benefits under 84 O.S. 1971, § 44, our forced heir statute, in view of The Act of Congress, February 27, 1925, § 7, 43 Statute 1008, as amended.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged an order from the District Court, Osage County (Oklahoma), which denied her request for benefits under the forced heir statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 84, § 44 (1971) when she elected to take against the decedent's will that left appellee principal beneficiaries, the decedent's mother and two children, the majority of the decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was a half-blood Osage Indian and owned certain restricted property. He left a will. The will stated that the wife was entitled to $ 10 and that the principal beneficiaries were to receive the remainder of the estate. The will was admitted to probate and the wife elected to take against the will under the forced heir statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 84, § 44 (1971). The wife did not establish that she was of Indian blood as required. The trial court denied her request to take under § 44 in light of The Act of Congress, February 27, 1925, § 7 43 Stat. 1008, as amended. She challenged the trial court's order, arguing that the Congressional Act was unconstitutional because Congress lacked power to alter the effect of Okla. Stat. tit. 84, § 44 (1971). The principal beneficiaries contended that all of the issues presented by the wife in the case at bar had been resolved in a previous case. The court agreed with the principal beneficiaries and upheld the trial court's order. The court held that the Congressional Act had been deemed constitutional and agreed with the holding that Congress had the power to regulate inheritance issues with respect to restricted Indian properties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Tulsa Area Hosp. Council, Inc. v. Oral Roberts Univ.


No. 53,059


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 29; 626 P.2d 316; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 195

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 25, 1981 and April 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable Ronald N. Ricketts, Judge. Appellants appeal from the order of the district court, remanding the cause to the Oklahoma Health Planning Commission for further consideration.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a university and a health planning commission, sought review of an order from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which remanded the cause to the commission in favor of appellee hospital council for further consideration after the commission granted a certificate of need, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2651 (Supp. 1975), to the university for the construction of a hospital where holistic medicine was to be practiced.


OVERVIEW: The commission granted a certificate of need to the university for the construction of a hospital. The council appealed to the district court, which vacated the order granting the certificate to the hospital and remanded the cause to the commission for further findings. The district court found that the granting of the certificate was clearly erroneous and in violation of the Establishment Clause. Appellants sought review and the court stated that to properly issue a certificate of need, the commission was required to find that the action proposed in the application was necessary and desirable in order to provide the required institutional health services in the area to be served; the proposed action could be economically accomplished and maintained; and that it would contribute to the orderly development of health services in the area. The court found that the commission complied with the statutory requirements. The court also found that the granting of the certificate of need was not clearly erroneous in view of the reliable material, probative, and substantial evidence. The court concluded that the granting of the certificate of need did not advance or inhibit religion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the district court that had remanded the cause to the commission for further consideration.

Red River Constr. Co. v. City of Norman


No. 53,895


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 20; 624 P.2d 1064; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 192



February 24, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Div. 2. Plaintiff sought an injunction to prohibit enforcement of an allegedly void City ordinance as well as damages suffered thereby under 42 U.S.C. § 1983 in the District Court of Cleveland County. The trial court held the ordinance was constitutional, finding for defendant on all issues. This trial court judgment was previously modified by this court in Cause No. 54,094. The Court of Appeals subsequently reversed in part and remanded for trial. Certiorari has been granted previously.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division 2 vacated; trial court reversed in part; injunction granted. Trial court's judgment on the second cause of action is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company filed a lawsuit against defendant city seeing an injunction to prohibit the enforcement of an ordinance as well as damages suffered thereby under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), reversing in part a decision of the trial court, held that the ordinance, which restricted by weight traffic on certain streets, was invalid. The city sought a writ of certiorari from that decision.


OVERVIEW: The company owed a lease for the purpose of mining riverbed sand at the southern end of one of the city's streets. That street was the only route on which the company could transport its mined sand into commerce. The city, however, passed an ordinance that limited the weight of trucks that could travel on the street. The ordinance only affected the company. The court enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance. The court stated that the ordinance did not bear a rational relationship to the city's concern for health, welfare, and safety. The ordinance would have had the effect of requiring the company to use smaller trucks more often. The problematic threat caused by the sand would remain fixed, but the real health and safety threat, which was the object of the ordinance caused by the increase of the number of trucks, would be proportionately increased. The court noted that the present truck traffic had not damaged the street or violated the city noise ordinance. Thus, the ordinance was beyond the scope of the city's police power.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision was vacated. The trial court's order, insofar as it denied the company a permanent injunction to restrain enforcement of the ordinance, was reversed. The court enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance.

Sellers v. Corp. Comm'n of Okla.


No. 52,347


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 19; 624 P.2d 1061; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 193; 69 Oil & Gas Rep. 292



February 24, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma. Appellant seeks to vacate a forced pooling order entered by the Oklahoma Corporation Commission.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant seller challenged a judgment from the Oklahoma Corporation Commission, (Oklahoma), which, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 87.1(e) (1977), forced a pooling order between the seller and appellee drilling company.


OVERVIEW: The seller was the owner of two and a half acres of minerals in a drilling and spacing unit. The Commission ordered a pooling agreement between the seller and the drilling company. The seller appealed, arguing that the drilling company did not unconditionally agree to drill, that the evidence was insufficient, and that the pooling agreement was unconstitutional. The court affirmed. The court held that § 87.1(e), in order to protect correlative rights and to prevent the drilling of unnecessary wells, required forced pooling if the mineral owners had not agreed to pool their interests or where a separate owner had drilled or proposed to drill a well on the drilling and spacing unit. Section 87.1(e) did not require that a separate owner promise to drill a well, only that the Commission had the authority to order forced pooling if a well was proposed. There was no authority that required the separate owner to bind himself inextricably to drill a well before the unit could be pooled. Second, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the order. Third, the court held that that § 87.1(e) was constitutional. The court concluded that the pooling agreement was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

STATE ex rel. DEPARTMENT OF HUMAN SERVS. v. MALIBIE


No. 56,005


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 Okla. LEXIS 350



February 18, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION AND PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Human Services (Oklahoma) sought mandamus directed to some County Commissioners (Oklahoma) and members of some County Excise Boards (Oklahoma) to require them to comply with Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 175.11, which required that counties appropriate at least one-fifth of one mill on the assessed valuation of the counties pursuant to the Crippled Children's Act (Act). The main issue was whether § 175.11 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General (Oklahoma) rendered an opinion that § 175.11 violated Okla. Const. art. X, § 9, which provided that no ad valorem tax could be levied for state purposes. The Department argued to the contrary. Under the authority of Okla. Const. art. VII, § 2 and due to the public nature of the case, the court assumed original jurisdiction to decide whether § 175.11 violated the state constitution. The court reviewed its past decisions as to the constitutionality of laws similar to § 175.11 under Okla. Const. art. XXI, § 1, which provided that certain institutions created for the public good had to be established and supported by the state. Uniformly, laws requiring that counties assume some of the burden for financing such institutions were held to violate art. XXI, § 1. One such law was quite similar to § 175.11. The court held that Okla. Const. art. X, § 9 provided another reason for adhering to the court's views in those cases. The court held that § 175.11 violated both Okla. Const. art. X, § 9 and Okla. Const. art. XXI, § 1. The court held that the Act was a program controlled and administered by the state for which county ad valorem tax revenues could not be appropriated.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Department's petition for the issuance of a writ of mandamus.

State ex rel. Dep't of Human Servs. v. Malibie


No. 56005


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 18; 630 P.2d 310; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 304



February 18, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Proceeding on Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Mandamus. In this original proceeding, we are asked by the Department of Human Services to assume original jurisdiction and issue a Writ of Mandamus, requiring the members of various County Excise Boards and various County Commissioners to comply with the provisions of 10 O.S.1971 § 175.11. Finding that the provisions of 10 O.S.1971 § 175.11 violate both Article 10, Section 9, and Article 21, Section 1, of the Oklahoma Constitution, we assume original jurisdiction, but refuse to issue the Writ prayed for.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED. PETITION FOR THE ISSUANCE OF A WRIT OF MANDAMUS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action before the court was an original proceeding on application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for writ of mandamus. The court was asked by petitioner Oklahoma Department of Human Services to assume original jurisdiction and issue a writ requiring respondent members of county excise boards and various county commissioners to comply with the provisions of the Crippled Children's Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 175.11 (1971).


OVERVIEW: Relying upon an Attorney General's Opinion, many county commissioners and members of county excise boards failed to comply with provisions of § 175.11 because that statute was found to be unconstitutional. The Department asked that a writ be issued requiring various county commissioners and members of various county excise boards to comply with the provisions of that statute. The Department argued that since county ad valorem revenues were only used to pay for treatment provided to each county's residents, the funds were being appropriated and used for a county purpose, and, thus, Okla. Const. art. X, § 9 was not being violated. The court stated that it found this argument to be specious. The Act was a state program controlled and administered by a Department of the State and State officers. The court concluded that the provisions of the Act, which required that county ad valorem tax revenues be appropriated to fund the program, constituted an appropriation of county ad valorem revenues for a state purpose, and, thus, such provisions violated § 9.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction, but refused to issue the writ prayed for.
