Wickham v. Gulf Oil Corp.


No. 52,871


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1981 OK 8; 623 P.2d 613; 1981 Okla. LEXIS 184; 71 Oil & Gas Rep. 399



January 27, 1981 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Roger Mills County. The Honorable Charles M. Wilson, District Judge. The appellants, Kenneth Wickham, Jr. and Nannette Crane Wickham, bring this appeal from the District Court of Roger Mills County, the Honorable Charles M. Wilson, presiding. Plaintiffs sought to remove a cloud on their title consisting of certain leasehold interests held by appellees. Appellants contended 52 O.S. 1971 § 87.1(b) applied to contractual interests created prior to the effective date of the statute. The trial court sustained appellees' demurrers to the petition and thereafter dismissed the action. Appellants perfect this appeal.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review from a decision of the District Court of Roger Mills County (Oklahoma) that refused to remove a cloud on their title created by interests held by appellee oil companies pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 87.1(b) (1971). The property owners asserted that § 87.1(b) applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: Oil companies held lease interests which created a cloud over the title of certain property owners. The property owners sought to have that cloud of title removed pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 87.1(b) (1971). They asserted that § 87.1(b) applied retroactively, but the trial court disagreed and awarded judgment to the oil companies. That decision was affirmed by the court, which noted that legislative intent was of paramount importance in determining whether statutes should be applied retroactively. Absent legislative intent to the contrary, statutes would not be interpreted retroactively where doing so altered rights and duties under an existing contract. The court noted that words alone were not the only decisive factor in divining legislative intent in this regard. Nonetheless, the court held that § 87.1(b) was not meant to be interpreted retroactively. In its decision, the court noted that the passage of § 87.1(b) by amendment to an older act did not necessarily mean that it operated retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award of judgment to the oil companies.

Kimery v. Public Serv. Co.


No. 51,510


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 187; 622 P.2d 1066; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 383



December 9, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 17, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court, Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable B. R. Beasley, District Judge. The surviving widow and children of Samuel E. Kimery (decedent) brought a wrongful death action against Public Service Company for the wrongful death of decedent. Decedent was electrocuted when he and his co-worker were painting an industrial building and their aluminum ladder came into contact with high voltage lines owned by Public Service Company. The jury returned a general verdict for Public Service Company and judgment was rendered accordingly. Appellants appeal from the order overruling their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the survivors of the decedent, sought review of an order from the District Court, Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which overruled their motion for a new trial following a general verdict in favor of appellee, an electrical utility company, in a wrongful death action brought by the survivors.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was electrocuted when his ladder came into contact with a high-voltage line. His survivors brought a wrongful death action against the electrical utility company. The utility company's defense rested on a claim of ordinary contributory negligence and contributory negligence per se resulting from the decedent's violation of the "six-foot law," Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 981 (1971). On appeal of a judgment in favor of the utility company, the court affirmed. The decedent was warned of the presence of the high-voltage line. Thus, his survivors could not challenge the alleged constitutional infirmity of § 981 for failing to require the utility company to notify the general public of the presence of the high-voltage lines. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague when measured by the decedent's conduct. Nor was it unconstitutional class legislation in violation of Okla. Const. art. V, § 51. It did not confer any immunity from tort liability upon electrical utilities. The burden of care it imposed upon the public was intended to promote the safety and welfare of the general public. The trial court's instructions on contributory negligence and negligence per se were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order overruling the motion for a new trial.

Mobile Components, Inc. v. Layon


No. 51,141


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 173; 623 P.2d 591; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 384



November 25, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 17, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable William W. Means, Judge. Appeal from order sustaining motion for summary judgment declaring the Oklahoma Mechanics' and Materialmen's Lien Statute, 42 O.S.1971, § 141, et seq., unconstitutional. Judgment of the trial court reversed and cause remanded.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an assignee, various businesses, a county treasurer, an executrix, and others, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which granted summary judgment for appellees, a bank, various companies, county commissioners, and others, in declaring that the Oklahoma Mechanics' and Materialmen's Lien Statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 42, § 141 et seq. (1971), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute over the ability to foreclose on a materialmen's lien statement, the primary issue was the constitutionality of § 141 et seq. Appellants claimed that the procedures were valid, while appellees relied on recent U.S. Supreme Court decisions regarding other remedies to argue that they were denied due process under the lien statute. On review, the court found that the trial court erred in finding the statute to be unconstitutional, so it remanded the case for further proceedings. The court concluded that the statutory procedures did not violate due process principles because the mere filing of a lien statement did not entitle a claimant to a lien on the land. The court rejected the claim that there was an unconstitutional "deprivation" from the filing of a lien. The court noted that a landowner was not deprived of substantial use and enjoyment of the property when such a lien was filed, but notice was simply given to all that a pending claim might be enforced against the land. Thus, the court held that under the Oklahoma lien statutes, there was no deprivation of a property right without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case.

 

276 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Earnest, Inc. v. LeGrand


No. 54,177


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 180; 621 P.2d 1148; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 374



November 25, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 19, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding brought by employer and its insurance carrier to review order on appeal entered by Workers' Compensation Court en banc, awarding death benefits and holding that under the Workers' Compensation Act there is no right of subrogation in a claim for death benefits and claimant widow is not required to make an election between death benefits or third party action; Yvonne Sparger, Trial Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and its insurance carrier, sought review of the order of respondent Workers' Compensation Court (Oklahoma), which awarded death benefits to respondent worker's widow, held that under the Workers' Compensation Act there was no right of subrogation in a claim for death benefits, and held further that the widow was not required to make an election between death benefits and cause of action against negligent party.


OVERVIEW: The widow filed a claim for death benefits after her husband was killed in a work-related accident. Petitioners moved to require her to elect between death benefits or a right of action against the negligent party, and asked that she assign her cause of action to the employer if she elected to proceed under the Act. The workmen's compensation court held it had no jurisdiction to rule on questions of election, assignment, or subrogation, and on appeal, the workmen's compensation court en banc upheld the award of death benefits and held that there was no right of subrogation under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 44 (1979). Petitioners appealed. The court found that § 44 did not provide for an election of benefits and found further that amendments to that section were in irreconcilable conflict with other parts of the same provision, concluding that § 44 did not provide a right of subrogation. The court rejected petitioners' argument that denial of the right of subrogation was an abrogation of their common law right, stating that the right to death benefits under the Act and the right to pursue a wrongful death action were purely statutory rights, neither of which arose from the common law.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the order of the Workers' Compensation Court entered en banc. The order affirmed awarded death benefits to the widow and held that petitioners did not have a right of subrogation.

 

277 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Tubbs v. Harrison (In re Tubbs)


No. 52,346


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 177; 620 P.2d 384; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 377



November 25, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Okmulgee County. Hon. J. Kirk Woodliff, Judge. Proceeding by noncustodial parent to vacate -- as void for want of a constitutionally adequate notice -- a prior decree changing a minor child's surname to that of her stepfather. Parent appeals from trial court's refusal to vacate its decree.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed the decision of the District Court, Okmulgee County (Oklahoma) that refused to void a decree changing the surname of the father's daughter to that of her stepfather, on the mother's petition, where the notice of the name change proceeding was obtained by publication despite the father's known whereabouts, his payment of child support, and his exercise of visitation rights.


OVERVIEW: Despite knowledge of the father's address, the mother changed the surname of the parties' eight year old daughter pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1633 (1976), which allowed notice by publication only. On appeal, the father argued that his unsevered parental bond as a non-custodial parent who was paying child support and exercising his visitation rights were in jeopardy if the mother was allowed to summarily change his daughter's name without notice to him. Agreeing therewith, the court reversed the district court decision and held that it erred in refusing to void the decree allowing the mother to change the daughter's name. Basing its ruling on the fact that the father's address was indisputably known when the action was commenced and that the parental bond was an essential right, a basic civil right, a fundamental right, and a personal right more precious than a property right, the court held that the bond was constitutionally protected by the due process and equal protection clauses. However, the court did not declare § 1633 unconstitutional. It merely held that § 1633 provided insufficient constitutional notice for a hearing that involved such an important right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court.

In re Initiative Petition No. 314


No. 55,638


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 174; 625 P.2d 595; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 390



November 25, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceedings in this Court pursuant to 34 O.S.Supp.1979, § 8, challenging the apparent sufficiency of signatures affixed to Initiative Petition No. 314, and attacking the validity of the Initiative Petition as being in contravention of the "one general subject" rule as provided in Art. 24, § 1, Okl. Const.



DISPOSITION: INITIATIVE PETITION HELD VIOLATIVE OF ART. 24, § 1, OKL. CONST., AND NOT LEGALLY ENTITLED TO BE PLACED ON BALLOT FOR PURPOSE OF POPULAR ELECTION THEREON.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Contestant citizens filed an action pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 8 (1979) challenging the sufficiency of signatures affixed to an initiative petition and attacking the validity of the initiative petition as being in contravention of Okla. Const. art. 24, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The citizens claimed that the initiative petition was a resubmission of an earlier initiative. They claimed that under Okla. Const. art. 5, § 6 it therefore required the signature of 25 percent of the legal voters. They also claimed that the initiative petition was invalid because it violated the "one general subject" rule of Okla. Const. art. 24, § 1. The court held that the initiative petition was invalid. The court ruled that (1) the initiative petition constituted a resubmission because there were no differences of any substance between the initiative petition and the prior initiative; (2) the initiative petition violated Okla. Const. art. 24, § 1 because it contained more than one general subject and the voters were not able to vote separately for or against each proposal; and (3) the initiative petition should therefore be stricken from the ballot.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the initiative petition was invalid and ordered it stricken from the ballot.

 

279 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Butler v. Bd. of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Okla.


No. 52,851


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 162; 619 P.2d 1262; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 368



October 28, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma, Honorable Park W. Lamerton, Judge. In this case, we are asked to determine whether the issuance of an injunction, prohibiting the defendant below from engaging in certain acts deemed to constitute the practice of dentistry, was proper. In determining this question, we hold that The Board of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Oklahoma has the capacity to bring injunctive actions in order to prohibit non-dentists from performing acts which constitute the practice of dentistry. Additionally, we hold that neither the placing of a newspaper ad advocating denturism, nor the cleaning of dentures, constitutes the practice of dentistry, as that term is defined in the State Dental Act.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED IN PART, AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dental technician appealed a decision of the District Court of Garfield County (Oklahoma), that permitted appellee Board of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Oklahoma to bring an action enjoining him from practicing dentistry under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.49 (1971). He also asserted that the court improperly restrained his advertisement and improperly found that the cleaning of dentures was dentistry.


OVERVIEW: The State Board of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Oklahoma brought an action against a dental technician seeking to enjoin him from practicing dentistry under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.49 (1971). The trial court awarded judgment to the board, and the court affirmed that decision in part and reversed it in part. The court found that the board was statutorily authorized to regulate the practice of dentistry and to enforce the statute that regulated dentistry. Therefore, the court found that the board was authorized to bring an injunction action against the technician and declared that the board's existence created no unconstitutional deprivation of equal protection or due process of law. Nonetheless, the court found that the trial court erred when it prevented the technician from publishing an advertisement that it decided had nothing to do with dentistry. Similarly, the court held that the cleaning of dentures did not constitute dentistry within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.19 (k) (1971), and therefore held that the trial court wrongly prohibited the technician from engaging in such activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the issuance of the injunction but reversed the trial court's decision that restrained the publication of the disputed advertisement and that held that the cleaning of dentures constituted dentistry.

 

280 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sun Oil Co. Del. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 52,965


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 150; 620 P.2d 896; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 380



October 7, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 5, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Oklahoma Tax Commission. Appellants appeal from an order of the Oklahoma Tax Commission denying their applications for refund of taxes paid pursuant to 68 O.S. 1979 Supp., § 1402(a) which was declared unconstitutional by this court in Phillips v. Oklahoma Tax Commission, Okl., 577 P.2d 1278 (1978).



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission, which denied their applications for refund of taxes paid pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1402(a) (Supp. 1979), which was declared unconstitutional by the court.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought a refund of taxes erroneously paid through a mistake of law based upon the court's decision that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1402(a) (Supp. 1979) was unconstitutional. The taxes were paid without protest. The taxpayers claimed refunds under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 227 (1971). In reversing the decision, the court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 227 (1971) could not be construed as precluding a taxpayer from recovering taxes erroneously paid without protest through an error in computation if the claim was timely filed and did not preclude recovery if the claim was based on a mistake of law. Since all the taxes for which the taxpayers sought refunds were paid to satisfy the liabilities which accrued prior to the 1978 amendment of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 227 (1971), the taxpayers' right to refunds had to be determined under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 227 (1971) prior to its amendment. Under Okla. Const. art. 5, § 54, the repeal of a statute could not affect any accrued right. The taxpayers' payment under a statute that was subsequently declared unconstitutional constituted an erroneous payment through a "mistake of law" under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 227 (1971).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

Welling v. Am. Roofing & Sheet Metal Co.


No. 50,528


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 131; 617 P.2d 206; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 320



September 16, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, Honorable Ronald Ricketts, Judge. Plaintiffs, homeowner, brought action to discharge mechanics and materialmans lien and defendant counterclaimed seeking foreclosure and in personam judgment in amount of lien. Trial court rendered judgment in favor of defendant on counterclaim ordering foreclosure of lien, and awarding defendant attorney fees.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed a decision in favor of defendant roofer by the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma on the roofer's counterclaim for lien foreclosure, attorney fees, and an in personam judgment against the homeowners, which was part of the homeowners' claim to set aside the subcontractor's lien pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 42, § 177 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The homeowners hired the contractor to install a new roof. After having obtained a bid from the subcontractor, the homeowners decided to rip off the old roof themselves to reduce the price. The roofer then put a new roof on the house. When the homeowners refused to pay the roofer because the roof leaked, the roofer filed a subcontractor's lien. The homeowners filed an action to set aside the lien. Although the subcontractor's lien was filed late, the trial court found that the roofer was a contractor for purposes of installation of the roof under Okla. Stat. tit. 42, § 142 (1977) because it dealt directly with the homeowners on the reduced price. The court held that the roofer was a subcontractor because the roofer performed the work through the contractor. Therefore, the roofer was not entitled to foreclose the lien because it filed the lien too late. However, the subcontractor was entitled to damages for unjust enrichment because it installed the new roof at a good faith cost. The homeowners were still entitled to the offset from the damages because of the poor quality of the roof. Because both parties prevailed, both parties were entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision for the subcontractor and ruled for the homeowners on the lien foreclosure issue. The court affirmed the decision for the subcontractor on the issue of a judgment against the homeowners and affirmed the decision for the homeowners regarding an offset from the award. The court modified the order so that both parties received attorney fees and the cause was remanded to determine the homeowners' attorney fees.

Smith v. Bovaird Supply Co.


No. 52,358


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 129; 616 P.2d 1157; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 312



September 9, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Mayes County, Oklahoma. Honorable Edwin M. Moore, Trial Judge. Appeal from judgment granting an injunction.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the decision of the District Court of Mayes County (Oklahoma), which granted judgment in favor of defendant neighbors, enjoining the landowners permanently from asserting any further claim to a way of necessity and permanently enjoining the prosecution of any further action in the district court or any other court to establish a way of necessity over and across lands of the neighbors.


OVERVIEW: The landowners owned land on the tip of a peninsula surrounded by water. The fourth side was bordered by lands owned by the neighbors. The landowners filed an action contending that they were entitled to exercise the right of eminent domain for they were entitled to a way of necessity across the neighbors' lands. The neighbors filed motions, demurrers, and answers challenging the right to a "way." Before the district court could rule, the landowners dismissed the action without prejudice to future filing and the neighbors moved for judgment on their cross petitions. The district court granted judgment in favor of the neighbors, enjoining the landowners permanently from asserting any further claim. The landowners appealed and the court reversed, dissolving the injunction. The court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 27, § 6 (1971) and Okla. Const. art. II, § 23 indicated that an individual had certain rights by virtues of such enactments as to a grant of the power of eminent domain. Because the enactments of the statutory and constitutional provisions supplied a remedy that was the landowners' only possible remedy, the district court had no power to restrict that right by injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decision and dissolved the injunction.

OVERVIEW: The patient was taken into custody. A police report alleged that the patient was irrational, confused, disoriented, and unable to respond to simple questions. The patient was later taken to a hospital where he was examined by a psychiatrist who recommended confinement. Thereafter, the deputy sheriff filed a petition alleging that the patient was mentally ill and required hospital care and treatment. The court found that the trial court failed to follow certain procedural steps. No separate and independent proceedings were held to determine competency. The patient was never declared incompetent. In addition, a proper physician endorsed affidavit was never filed and that the patient was never served. Therefore, the court concluded that the patient's statutory rights were violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order committing the patient to a mental hospital.

Boyle v. Boyle


No. 51,909


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 123; 615 P.2d 301; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 297



August 6, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 7, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1. The District Court, Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable Patricia M. Hoebel, District Judge, awarded custody of three minor children to the father. On appeal, the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1, reversed the judgment of the District Court and remanded with instructions to place custody with the mother. The father seeks certiorari.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED; DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; AND JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee father sought a writ of certiorari for review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1 (Oklahoma), which reversed the district court's award of custody of the parties' three minor children to the husband and remanded with instructions to place custody with appellant mother.


OVERVIEW: The parties had three minor boys aged ten, seven and five at the time of the divorce proceedings involving the mother and father. The district court entered a divorce decree and granted custody of the three minor boys to the father. The mother appealed, and the Court of Appeals reversed on the basis that the maternal preference in Okla. Stat. tit. 30 § 11 (1971) was controlling. The father petitioned for a writ of certiorari. The court vacated the appeals court decision and affirmed the district court. The court held there was nothing in the record indicating that the trial court, after hearing and observing the parties and the witnesses, believed both the father and mother could equally provide for the best interests of the children, and therefore there was no need to resort to the statutory presumption. The trial court specifically found that the father could serve the children's best interest, which was the paramount factor. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in awarding custody to the father.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of certiorari and vacated the decision of the court of appeals. The court affirmed the decision of the district court, which awarded of custody of the parties' three minor children to the father.

Draper v. State


No. 55,144


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 117; 621 P.2d 1142; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 397



July 22, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected On Rehearing December 23, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding for Writ of Prohibition or Mandamus. Petitioners requested the assumption of original jurisdiction and a motion to stay the effectiveness of the Attorney General's Opinions Nos. 79-311 and 79-313B. The Court assumed original jurisdiction and entered the Motion to Stay April 30, 1980. The petitioners also sought writs of prohibition and mandamus to preclude the issuance of further analogous opinions by the Attorney General or, in the alternative, to mandate the withdrawal of the contested opinions.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED. ATTORNEY GENERAL'S OPINIONS NOS. 79-311 and 79-313B HELD TO BE INVALID AND OF NO EFFECT. WRIT OF MANDAMUS AND WRIT OF PROHIBITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner legislators sought a writ of prohibition or mandamus against respondent, the State Attorney General, to preclude the issuance of further opinions concerning the constitutionality of an appropriations bill or, in the alternative, withdrawal of contested opinions.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General issued two opinions that found that an appropriations bill was unconstitutional because it commingled general appropriations with special appropriations. The legislators filed a petition for a writ of mandamus in an original proceeding to prevent the issuance of any further similar opinions or withdrawal of the contested opinions. The Attorney General argued that the court had no jurisdiction over the Office of Attorney General. The court disagreed and held that it had jurisdiction because the issue was one of statewide concern. The court then held that the constitution contained no limitation or prohibition upon the legislature's power to enact an appropriations bill similar to the one at issue. Mandamus was improper, however, because Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 18b(q) (1979) required the Attorney General to provide the legislature with opinions when asked. The Attorney General met this requirement. The court therefore chose not to issue a writ of prohibition, but rather determined that the opinions were invalid and of no effect.


OUTCOME: The court invalidated the Attorney General's opinions that the legislator's appropriations bill was unconstitutional.

Looney v. Farmers Ins. Group


No. 53,346


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 111; 616 P.2d 1138; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 292



July 15, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 15, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County. The Honorable Charles L. Owens, District Judge. Judgment creditor brought garnishment proceedings against insurance company alleging judgment arose from bodily injury covered by contract of insurance. Trial court rendered judgment for insurer, ruling that debtor was a named insured and household member, therefore excluded under the terms of the automobile liability contract. Allegations of error raised by appellant discussed and refused; trial court affirmed.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured person sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) entered in favor of appellee insurance company. The injured person had filed a garnishment action against the insurance company to recover the full amount of her judgment against a driver who was insured by the company. In a tort action, the injured person had obtained a default judgment against the insured.


OVERVIEW: The injured person was hurt in an automobile accident. The injured person had been traveling in a vehicle driven by the insured, who was her husband. The injured person filed an action against the insured and the other party to the accident. The company denied coverage to the insured because of certain exclusion provisions in his insurance policy and refused to defend. Thereafter, the injured person obtained a default judgment against her husband. She then commenced a garnishment action against the company to recover the full amount of her judgment. The trial court rendered judgment for the company. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held (1) that since the primary purpose of the family-household exclusion clause was to protect the company against collusive or friendly lawsuits, the injured person could not have contended that she was denied equal protection under the laws; and (2) that the exclusion in the liability policy specifically applied to the injured person. She was more than a mere family member of the insured; she was also an insured under the policy. Her relationship with the insured placed her within the policy definition of named insured.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of judgment in favor of the company.

Okla. Ordnance Works Auth. v. Dist. Court


No. 54,916, No. 54,917, No. 54,936, No. 54,955, No. 54,991, No. 55,026


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 100; 613 P.2d 746; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 307



June 24, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] The co-respondents commenced a transitory action for damages against the petitioners in the Wagoner County District Court. Each petitioner challenged the court's venue. The respondent judge overruled all challenges to venue and ordered the litigation to proceed. Petitioners commenced separate proceedings for this court to assume original jurisdiction and to issue a writ of prohibition prohibiting the respondent judge from further proceeding in the cause.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED; CASES CONSOLIDATED UNDER CASE NO. 54,916; AND WRITS OF PROHIBITION ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Co-respondent business owners commenced a transitory action for damages against petitioners, certain governmental agencies and corporations. Each petitioner challenged the trial court's venue. Respondent judge overruled all challenges to venue and ordered the litigation to proceed. Petitioners commenced separate proceedings for the court to assume original jurisdiction and to issue a writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The business owners operated businesses near a lake. They alleged that petitioners negligently permitted or caused to be discharged certain waste materials into a tributary creek of the lake, thereby causing them to sustain damages to their businesses. The cases we presented on the theory that the creek was in one county and that all petitioners' acts or omissions in permitting or causing to be discharged the waste materials occurred in that county, but that some of the alleged damages occurred in the county of the trial court. The judge had overruled all challenges to venue and ordered the litigation to proceed. Petitioners sought writs of prohibition. The court granted them. The court found that the issue presented was whether the trial court had venue of the business owners' transitory action for damages against petitioners. The court held that venue of co-respondents' action against the Oklahoma Ordnance Works Authority and the Grand River Dam Authority did not lie in the county of the trial court. They were "public officers" within the contemplation of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 133 (1971); as such, the venue of all petitioners was dependent upon the public officers' venue.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction and issued the requested writs of prohibition.

 

288 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Howard v. Okla. Corp. Comm'n


No. 53,665


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 96; 614 P.2d 45; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 305



June 17, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding on application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for writ of mandamus. Relators filed an "Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Mandamus" seeking to compel the Corporation Commission to comply with § 12 of Enrolled Senate Bill 49 of the First Regular Sessions of the 37th Legislature. The Corporation Commission, through its staff attorneys, filed a response. The Attorney General of Oklahoma has filed motions challenging the right of the Corporation Commission's attorneys to represent it in this action, questioning the relators' standing to sue, and to dismiss. Held: Relators have standing to sue, Commission's employee-attorneys may represent it and Attorney General may appear ex officio.



DISPOSITION: MOTION TO DISMISS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, members of the legislature, brought an original proceeding in mandamus seeking to compel respondent Oklahoma Corporation Commission to comply with the terms of recently passed legislation. The Commission entered an appearance through its employee-attorneys and an attorney general entered an appearance purporting to represent the Commission. The attorney general moved to dismiss the complaint for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed and the governor signed an act that required the Commission to prescribe a method for giving consumers credits on their utility bills. The attorney general rendered an opinion holding that portion of the legislation invalid because it was enacted in violation of the state constitution. The legislators sought by their mandamus action to compel the Commission to comply with the legislation. The attorney general argued that the legislators' action was brought in the name of the state and he was, therefore, the proper representative to bring the action. He argued that he thus represented both parties and sought dismissal of the complaint. The court held that it had jurisdiction of the action. The Commission had a right to counsel of its own choosing. The legislators sought to vindicate an important public right under circumstances where the attorney general could not be expected to represent the interest. They therefore had standing to bring the action. The attorney general's views on the issue were important and should be heard. The court therefore decided to realign the parties.


OUTCOME: The court denied the attorney general's motion to dismiss. It realigned the parties into a three party case. The legislators could represent the interests of the state, the Commission could be represented by its employee-attorneys, and the attorney general could appear ex-officio.

Southwestern Bell Tel. Co. v. Okla. County Excise Bd.


Nos. 54,893, Consolidated under No. 54,893, 54,913


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 97; 618 P.2d 915; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 360



June 17, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Dismissed October 27, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an Order of the Oklahoma Court of Tax Review Consolidated with a Related Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction. This cause is a consolidation of a direct appeal filed from a decision of the Oklahoma Court of Tax Review, and a declaratory judgment action brought by the Board of Trustees of the Employee Retirement System of the City of Oklahoma City. On motion of the parties, both causes were consolidated for consideration in this Court. The question presented in both causes is whether certain sinking fund levies levied by the Cities of Oklahoma City and Lawton violated the provisions of Article 10, Section 26, of the Oklahoma Constitution, which require municipalities and counties to be on a "cash basis." Finding that the levies did violate the provisions of Article 10, Section 26, of the Oklahoma Constitution, we affirm the ruling of the Court of Tax Review, holding that it should be applied prospectively.



DISPOSITION: RULING OF THE OKLAHOMA COURT OF TAX REVIEW AFFIRMED AND APPLIED PROSPECTIVELY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities sought review of an order from the Oklahoma Court of Tax Review that was entered for appellees, a telephone company and a fuel corporation, holding that certain sinking fund levies that were levied by the cities for a certain fiscal year were illegal, insofar as they would retire certain specific judgments.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company and the fuel corporation officially protested certain sinking fund levies. The tax court held that the levies were illegal and the cities appealed. Additionally, the board commenced an original action asking the court to rule upon the validity of portions of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 149 (Supp. 1977). On motion of the parties, the causes were consolidated. The court determined that it was the intent of the legislature that judgments rendered under the provisions of § 149 could be rendered without proving that the city appropriated funds to pay for the premium debt underlying the judgment. The court held that the levies violated the provisions of Okla. Const. art. 10, § 26, requiring municipalities to operate on a cash basis. Thus, the fund was under no mandatory obligation to provide services for which the cities made claim. It was necessary for the fund to allege and prove there were funds on hand out of which the claims made against the cities could be paid. The fund's failure to do so was fatal, and the court held that the judgments entered against the cities, based on the fund's claims, were not properly satisfied through a sinking fund levy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the tax review court to be applied prospectively.

 

290 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Thayer v. Phillips Petro. Co.


No. 52,377


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 95; 613 P.2d 1041; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 280



June 17, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma Honorable Richard E. Comfort, Judge. Appellant appeals from the judgment of the district court holding a portion of the Small Claims Act, 12 O.S. Supp. 1975 § 1757, unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a small claims action against defendant corporation. After the corporation removed the action to district court, appellant was victorious and sought attorney fees under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1757 (1975). The District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) denied the application for attorney fees, and held that the act violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. XIV because it allowed attorney fees only to prevailing plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: The corporation removed the small claims action to district court and lost. Appellant sought attorney fees under § 1757, which imposed attorney fees on losing defendants. The corporation claimed that the unilateral attorney fees clause violated equal protection. The court disagreed, finding that the clause withstood strict scrutiny because it served a compelling public interest. The unilateral attorney's fees feature was triggered by defendants' election to fundamentally alter the character of the lawsuit from a summary, informal small claims matter into a formal, protracted litigation involving greater complications and most significantly, the appearance of attorneys. Defendants' election in such cases served to defeat the unmistakable public policy goal of establishing small claims forums as "peoples" courts, uncomplicated by the formal demands of superior courts. The discriminatory portion of the statute that imposed attorney fees on one party for the benefit of his opponent without granting defendant a corresponding right, did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment right to equal protection of the law, or Okla. Const. art. 2, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment.

 

291 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Okla. Tax Comm'n v. Smith


No. 55,079


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 74; 610 P.2d 794; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 245



May 5, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, The Honorable Harold C. Theus, Presiding Judge. In an appeal from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County holding portions of House Bill 1484 of the 37th Legislature of the State of Oklahoma unconstitutional as measured against both State and Federal Constitutions, it is held House Bill 1484 neither violates the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the Federal Constitution, nor impermissibly encroaches on the Oklahoma Constitution's reservation to the people of the right to Initiative. Judgment of the trial court is reversed.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma Tax Commission challenged a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer and held that certain provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2352 (Supp. 1979) et seq. (Act) were void. Specifically, the trial court declared Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 2355(A), 2355.1 (Supp. 1979) invalid.


OVERVIEW: The Act was passed prior to an election on an income tax initiative. The Act was intended to overturn the initiative, however, the initiative failed to pass. The tax classification at issue in the Act taxed a higher percentage of the taxpayer's total cash flow at a lower rate for those not using the federal tax deduction and a lower percentage of the taxpayer's cash flow at a higher rate when the deduction was used. On appeal, the Commission argued that deductions from taxable income were purely a matter of grace dependent upon the legislative will alone. The court reversed the judgment, holding that the Act neither violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution, nor impermissibly encroached on the Oklahoma Constitution's reservation to the people of the right to initiative. Additionally, the legislature had the power to create the deduction for federal tax paid. Having the power to create the deduction in itself established two classes of income taxpayers, those using the deduction and those refraining to do so. The classification of taxpayers was rationally related to the end to be achieved, which was the taxation of income.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

292 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Reirdon v. Wilburton Bd. of Educ.


No. 53,610


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 67; 611 P.2d 239; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 254



April 22, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Latimer County, Oklahoma Honorable Pat Pate, Judge. Appellant appeals from the dismissal of the cause of action under the Oklahoma Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act, 51 O.S. Supp. 1978 §§ 151-170, for failure to give the prescribed notice dictated by 51 O.S. Supp. 1978 § 156 to the Clerk of the School Board.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment by the District Court of Latimer County (Oklahoma), which dismissed the mother's action alleging negligent administration of corporal punishment, filed under the Oklahoma Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 156 (Supp. 1978), against appellees, the school board and teacher.


OVERVIEW: The mother alleged that a teacher negligently paddled her 12-year-old son in violation of the Tort Claims Act, resulting in physical injury. The trial court dismissed the action because the mother had not given the school board and teacher written notice within four months of the injury as required by the Act. The court reversed on appeal. The court rejected the mother's argument that the notice requirement was unconstitutional. The court held that the notice requirement furthered legitimate state interests by fostering a prompt investigation and opportunity to remedy the problem quickly. The court, however, agreed with the mother's alternative argument that there was substantial compliance with the notice requirement. The court found that the mother had sent a letter to the board president. Although the notice did not state the relief sought or amount of damages requested, such failure did not invalidate the notice given. The court found that the board and teacher were on notice of the claim at an early date to enable them the opportunity to prepare a defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the mother's claim.

Okla. State Election Bd. v. Coats


No. 54,756


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 65; 610 P.2d 776; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 242



April 21, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma Honorable Homer Smith, Judge. Appellant appeals from a declaratory judgment action in which 19 O.S. Supp. 1974 § 215.8 was held to impose additional qualifications on the district attorney of Oklahoma County who intends to become a candidate for the United States Senate during his term of office, and to be unconstitutional because it denied him equal protection of the laws.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the state election board, its chair, a member, and its secretary, sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which, in a declaratory judgment action brought by appellee, a district attorney who intended to run for the U.S. Senate, held that Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 215.8 (Supp. 1974) imposed additional qualifications on the district attorney, and was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: When he decided to run for the U.S. Senate, the district attorney filed a petition for declaratory judgment, seeking a ruling on the applicability and validity of § 215.8, contending that it was inapplicable because it added qualifications not imposed by U.S. Const. art. I, § 3. He also argued that § 215.8 denied him equal protection of the laws. The trial court agreed and held that the statute was unconstitutional. Appellants sought review and the court found that the statute lent itself to two differing constructions, but held that it did not impose additional qualifications on the candidacy of district attorneys who chose to run for federal office since the impediment attached to the office and not to the officeholder. The court held that the statute was not invidiously discriminatory under either the rational basis or strict scrutiny test because it preserved the efficiency, objectivity, and integrity of the district attorneys, preventing any possible abuse to the office during the campaign to promote the officeholder's candidacy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Okla. Alcoholic Bev. Control Bd. v. Burris


No. 52,197


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 58; 626 P.2d 1316; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 261; 20 A.L.R.4th 593



April 15, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable Richard V. Armstrong, Trial Judge. The Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Board appeals from a judgment of the district court reversing its order requiring appellee to remove its sign as violative of Constitution and Statutes of the State of Oklahoma prohibiting advertising of alcoholic beverages.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Board challenged a judgment of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which reversed its order requiring appellee liquor retailer to remove its sign as violative of the state's constitution and statutes prohibiting advertising of alcoholic beverages. The Board ruled the signs and their arrangement were tantamount to advertising the liquor store, illegal under Oklahoma law.


OVERVIEW: The retailer made a request to the Board to transfer his retail liquor license to a new premises. The Board approved the transfer conditioned on the removal of a beverage mart sign located on contiguous property also owned by the retailer. The Board indicated the large beverage mart sign indirectly attracted customers' attention to the adjacent liquor store in violation of the Board's rules and regulations. The Board issued a declaratory judgment of a violation. On appeal, the trial court reversed the Board's order. The trial court concluded that the rule relied on by the Board was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, and that the determination that the sign violated such rule was based upon insufficient evidence. The court reversed the trial court, finding that although the rule could be more precise, it was not so vague and overbroad as to require holding it to be void. Therefore, the rule met constitutional scrutiny. The court did not agree that the Board's ruling was clearly erroneous because photographs of the premises were introduced, the Board's investigation showed a violation, and the retailer did not introduce evidence to refute the violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Berry v. Bd. of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Okla.


Nos. 53,472, 53,473, 53,474, 53,475; Consolidated under No. 53,472


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 45; 611 P.2d 628; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 253



March 25, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma Honorable Richard V. Armstrong, Judge. The appellants appeal from the granting of a temporary injunction by the district court restraining them from engaging in practices which are forbidden by The State Dental Act, 59 O.S. 1971 §§ 328.1 - 328.52.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant denturists sought review of a decision in favor of appellee, Board of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Oklahoma, by the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma in an action to prevent the denturists from practicing dentistry.


OVERVIEW: The denturists, technical dentists practicing prosthetic dentistry, claimed that the Board's injunction violated the Oklahoma Open Meeting Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 25, §§ 301-314 (Supp. 1977), because the decision to seek an injunction against the denturists was not made at an open meeting. The Board claimed that the decision to seek an injunction was a judicial determination, which was not subject to the Act, and was thus properly determined by the Board's attorney and agreed to by a Board member. The court held that the Board violated the Act. As a public body, the Board had to have a public meeting to pass a resolution with votes publicly cast on whether to direct specific action against the denturists. The Board also failed to make and keep minutes from that meeting. The State Dental Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 328.1 - 328.52 (1971), did not unlawfully delegate public power to a private group. The Board had a right to seek injunctive relief under Okla. Const. art. V, § 39 and Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.49 (1971). The Board members' pecuniary interest in dentistry was not substantial enough to make their enforcement of the Act unconstitutional where the Act limited their powers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in favor of the Board and ruled in favor of the denturists.

 

296 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cantrell v. Sanders


No. 54,125


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 43; 610 P.2d 227; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 229



March 25, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied as Amended April 28, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma Honorable Jane P. Wiseman, Special District Judge. The appellants, Tulsa County officials, appeal from a summary judgment in favor of the appellee-taxpayers in their suits for refunds. The district court held that the Tulsa County Board of Equalization did not have the authority to hear and correct the taxpayers' grievances and that the county assessor had unconstitutionally assessed the taxpayers' property at a higher ratio than that applied to other real property in Tulsa County. We affirm the judgment of the district court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county officials, challenged a decision from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayers in their actions for refunds. The trial court held the county Board of Equalization did not have the authority to hear the grievances and the county assessor had unconstitutionally assessed the taxpayers' property at a higher ratio than that applied to other real property in the county.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers paid their taxes under protest and filed actions for refunds. The taxpayers attacked the action of the county assessor in applying different assessment percentages to different categories of property. The court held that the actions of the county assessor in applying to the taxpayers' properties different assessment percentages from the percentages applied to other properties resulted in an unconstitutional unequal burden of taxation. Under the county assessor's system of assessment, there were 10 categories of real property, arguably 14 since four had two sub-categories. Against the value of property in these various categories, eight different percentages were applied to arrive at the assessed valuation, ranging from a high of 25 percent to a low of 6 percent. This was a disparity in tax burdens. Under Okla. Const. art. X, § 5, taxes were required to be uniform upon the same class of subjects. Under the county assessor's system, taxes were not uniform upon real property. Real property was one class of subjects. Okla. Const. art. X, § 5 mandated that taxes be uniform upon the same class of subjects; that provision was not affected by the 1971 amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court holding that the taxpayers were due refunds due to the unconstitutionally unequal burden of taxation on their properties.

ABC Drilling Co. v. Hughes Group


No. 52,050


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 39; 609 P.2d 763; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 231



March 18, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, State of Oklahoma. The Honorable Jack R. Parr, District Judge. The Hughes Group appeals the trial court's overruling of its motion to vacate a default judgment, wherein the invalidity of the judgment was correctly alleged to arise from the court's lack of jurisdiction over the person of the foreign corporate defendant.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a foreign corporation, sought review of a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which overruled defendant's motion to vacate a default judgment entered against the corporation in plaintiff drilling company's breach of contract and fraudulent misrepresentation action. Defendant alleged that the judgment was void for lack of personal jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly failed to deliver necessary materials for plaintiff to drill oil and gas wells and falsely represented that it had the ability to fulfill its obligations. Plaintiff served the Secretary of State, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 18, § 1.204a (1971), as was required for a foreign corporation. Although not required to do so under the statute, the Secretary mailed the petition and summons to defendant's service agent, but it was subsequently returned. Defendant was actually notified of the action when it received a notice of taking a deposition. The trial court found personal jurisdiction because service had been rendered as required by § 1.204a. The court found that the judgment was void for want of jurisdiction. Further, § 1.204a was constitutionally impermissible because it allowed a judgment to be rendered without service of process upon an undomesticated foreign corporation and because it was not reasonably calculated to apprise defendant of an impending action. Defendant had not entered into a series of acts constituting "doing business" so as to invoke domestication status. Therefore, defendant was not estopped from presenting jurisdictional error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling on the motion to vacate, vacated the default judgment, and remanded the cause.

Schuminsky v. Field


No. 54,476


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1980 OK 22; 606 P.2d 1133; 1980 Okla. LEXIS 288



February 12, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding wherein petitioner seeks writ prohibiting respondent Judge from trying trial court defendants' counterclaims advanced in forcible entry and detainer case, with a jury. This Court already has assumed original jurisdiction and granted a stay.



DISPOSITION: WRIT OF PROHIBITION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landlord brought a proceeding seeking a writ to prohibit respondent trial judge from requiring him to go to trial before a jury in a case pending in the District Court for Pottawatomie County (Oklahoma). The landlord argued that in his action for entry and detainer against defendant tenants, no jury was permitted and the judge should have dismissed the tenants' counterclaims as well.


OVERVIEW: The landlord owned a commercial building in which the tenants ran a drug store. He claimed that the tenants violated their lease by failing to pay him excess rent based on the volume of their business, to keep the premises free of debris, and to refrain from subleasing any portion of the premises. The landlord filed his forcible entry and detainer action against the tenants and demanded the amount of the excess rentals he claimed were owed. The tenants filed various counterclaims and a jury demand, all of which the landlord moved to dismiss as being not permitted under the entry and detainer statute. The trial court granted the jury demand and ruled that most of the counterclaims could proceed in the action. The landlord filed his petition for a writ of prohibition against the trial judge. The court noted that the forcible entry and detainer action expressly provided for the right to jury trials. The statute, however, prohibited the assertion of any counterclaims that were not specifically permitted by it. The purpose of such actions was to determine quickly the right to possession of land. The matters raised by the tenants had to be addressed in a separate suit.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of prohibition.

Jan Eric Cartwright, Attorney General of Oklahoma, et al., (Petitioners) filed an Application for this Court to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Issue a Writ of Mandamus ordering and directing H. M. Dunbar, County Assessor of Garfield County (Respondent), to place certain real and personal property on the Garfield County ad valorem tax rolls, and to declare 60 O.S. 1977 Supp. § 178.7 unconstitutional. Respondent, Garfield County Industrial Authority, a public trust, (GCIA) holds legal title to the property which Petitioners seek to have placed on the tax rolls, and Respondents Koehring Company (Koehring) and Chesterfield Cylinder Company, Inc. (Chesterfield) have separate possessory and contractual interests in such property. Respondents GCIA, Koehring and Chesterfield were authorized to Intervene. ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED: THE INTERESTS WHICH KOEHRING AND CHESTERFIELD HAVE IN THE PUBLIC TRUST PROPERTY HELD TAXABLE FOR THE YEAR BEGINNING 1980;  [***2] 60 O.S. 1977 SUPP. § 178.7, DECLARED UNCONSTITUTIONAL AS THE SAME MAY BE APPLICABLE TO KOEHRING AND CHESTERFIELD INTERESTS AFTER DECEMBER 31, 1979; AND WRIT DENIED AS HEREIN EXPLAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the Attorney General of the State of Oklahoma and associated school districts, filed a writ of mandamus against respondent County Assessor of Garfield County seeking to order him to place real and personal property on the county ad valorem tax rolls and to declare Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 178.7 (Supp. 1977) unconstitutional. Under Okla. Const. art. X, § 6A provided that intangible personal property consisting of a leasehold interest in real and personal property held in trust for the use and benefit of a county was not subject to ad valorem taxation. The court held that intangible personal property was defined as any interests in property held in trust or on deposit within or without the state. The court determined that, where the constitution and laws exempted from taxation all property of municipalities within the state, without reference to the use to which the property was put, it was exempt from all taxation regardless of the character of the use thereof. The court found that the fact that the property was held under a purchase contract failed to modify the tax exempt provisions. The court denied the writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus.

State ex rel. DOT v. Pile


No. 51,541


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 152; 603 P.2d 337; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 321



November 13, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Harper County, State of Oklahoma The Honorable Frank Ogden, District Judge. The State of Oklahoma appeals the sustention of a demurrer to a petition, alleging the trial court erred in holding the relief sought on the face of the petition, pursuant to 69 O.S. 1971 § 1271, et seq. contravened the Constitutional guarantee of freedom of speech under the facts of this case.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Oklahoma appealed a judgment from the District Court of Harper County, State of Oklahoma, which sustained appellee citizen's demurrer to the state's petition for an injunction to compel the removal of a billboard from the citizen's property. The state, through the department of highways, filed the petition under the authority of Okla. Stat. tit. 69, §§ 1271-1275 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The citizen had a billboard on her property, visible from a rural state highway, that stated "GET US OUT OF THE UNITED NATIONS." The state alleged that the sign was a public nuisance under Okla. Stat. tit. 69, § 1273(a) (1971), which defined outdoor advertising devices. The citizen demurred, and the trial court sustained the demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that a highway was an appropriate public forum for the dissemination of speech activity. The court determined that freedom of speech could not be made subservient to any definition of beauty or aesthetics that the state offered for not permitting billboards in rural locales. The court rejected the state's contention that the restriction on billboards was in the interest of the health and safety of the motoring public. The court concluded that the manner and place restrictions imposed upon the citizen's speech activity had little if any relationship to the legitimate governmental purpose to be served by the legislation. The court found that the trial court correctly held that non-commercial speech was not regulated by the statute, thus avoiding a declaration that the act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Williams v. Mashburn (In re Williams)


No. 50,114


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 150; 602 P.2d 1036; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 314



November 6, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Michael J. Tullius, Trial Judge. The appellant seeks review of an order terminating her parental rights to her natural child under 10 O.S. 1975 § 1130. The order terminating parental rights is reversed inasmuch as there is no indication from the record on appeal that the prior adjudication of dependency and neglect gave the parent notice of the conditions giving rise to such dependency and neglect. The parent is entitled to such notice, and without it there is no criterion by which to adjudicate the parent's change of substandard conditions at the termination hearing.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which terminated her parental rights to her natural child under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (1971). The mother asserted several errors on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The mother had been confined in a state hospital and had already been adjudged an incompetent person when the district court issued an order terminating her parental rights. The mother sought review of the district court's order alleging that she had been denied due process and the right to confront witnesses. The court reversed the order terminating the mother's parental rights. Specifically, the court held that where there were no standards promulgated from the adjudication of dependency and neglect to put the mother on notice as to what conditions would have to be shown to be corrected in order to prevent termination of her parental rights, the district court's order terminating her parental rights had to be reversed. The mother's confinement in a mental hospital, while necessitating custody of a child being placed elsewhere, did not constitute failure to give the child the necessary parental care or protection required for his mental or physical health within the purview of Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (1971).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment terminating the mother's parental rights.

 

303 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Ogden


No. 52,629


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 130; 600 P.2d 1223; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 336



September 18, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding on application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for Writ of Mandamus.  [*P0] In this original proceeding, two active members of the Oklahoma Bar Association, who no longer reside within the State, petitioned this Court asking us to assume original jurisdiction and issue a Writ of Mandamus, requiring the Respondent Trial Judge to permit them to practice law within the courts of the First Judicial District of Oklahoma, without having to associate with resident members of the Bar, or maintain a continually operating law office within this State. Finding that under the Rules promulgated by this Court in Creating and Controlling the Oklahoma Bar Association, the Petitioners have the right to practice law within this State without the imposition of conditions such as association with resident attorneys and operation of an in-State office, we issue the Writ of Mandamus requiring the Respondent Trial Judge to permit the Petitioners to practice within the First Judicial District of Oklahoma. In so ruling, we find the provisions of 5 O.S. 1971, § 18, promulgated by the Legislature, to constitute an unconstitutional infringement upon this Court's inherent power [***2] to regulate and control the Bar.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED AND WRIT OF MANDAMUS ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner two attorneys filed a petition for the court to assume original jurisdiction and issue a writ of mandamus requiring respondent trial judge to permit them to practice law within a certain district of Oklahoma without having to associate with a resident Oklahoma attorney.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys were bar association members in Oklahoma that had their law offices in Texas. The trial judge consistently disallowed the appearance of the attorneys in Oklahoma for failure to associate with a resident Oklahoma attorney. The court held that because the attorneys were active members in the bar association they were permitted to practice law in all Oklahoma courts within the jurisdiction pursuant to the Rules Creating and Controlling the Oklahoma Bar Association. The court noted that the attorneys could only be deprived of their right to practice law through judicial action. The court concluded that the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 5, § 18 that required members of the Oklahoma Bar Association to maintain residency or a continually operating law office in the state as a condition of the right to continued practice were unconstitutional. The court indicated that the fact that Texas had less stringent requirements regarding reciprocity than Oklahoma did not make Oklahoma's requirements less stringent.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandamus requiring the trial judge to permit the attorneys and all attorneys similarly situated to practice before the trial courts in the same manner and with the same rights enjoyed by all active members of the Oklahoma Bar Association.

Webb v. Wiley


No. 52,673


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 119; 600 P.2d 317; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 289



July 24, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Garvin County, Honorable Joe D. Shumate, Trial Judge.  [*P0] Appellant seeks review of an order whereby appellants Application to Withdraw Consent to Adoption was denied, and an Interlocutory Decree of Adoption was granted to appellees.



DISPOSITION: ORDER OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural mother sought review of the order from the District Court of Garvin County (Oklahoma), which denied the mother's application to withdraw consent to adoption and granted an interlocutory decree of adoption to appellee adoptive parents.


OVERVIEW: After the mother executed her consent to the adoption, the adoptive parents filed a petition for adoption, and two weeks later the mother filed an application to withdraw consent. The mother contended that Oklahoma's provision for adoption of children born out of wedlock was unconstitutional since it deprived the putative father of a right to object to the adoption. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the natural mother did not have standing to assert the constitutional rights of the putative father because constitutional rights were personal and could not be asserted vicariously. The mother failed to show how she was prejudiced by not receiving the investigative reports prepared by a DISRS before the hearing on adoption and her argument was insufficient to overcome the presumption in favor of the correctness of the judgment of the trial court that she was not prejudiced. The trial court did not err in its determination that the mother consented to the adoption voluntarily without coercion, undue influence, or fraud, and that the best interest of the child would not be furthered by withdrawing the consent to adopt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.
