Red Slipper Club, Inc. v. City of Okla. City


No. 50,010


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 118; 599 P.2d 406; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 267



July 24, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 17, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County. The Honorable Homer Smith, Trial Judge.  [*P0] The City of Oklahoma City appeals a ruling of the trial court finding 1975 city ordinance invalid because such ordinance levies a license tax greatly in excess of the cost of administering the licensing program.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which found in favor of appellee private club and held that Oklahoma City, Okla., City Code ch. 20, § 17 (amend. 1975) was invalid because it levied a license tax greatly in excess of the cost of administering the licensing program.


OVERVIEW: The private club sought injunctive relief to prevent the city from enforcing the license fee. The trial court entered an order holding that the regulation of private clubs was within the city's police power, but also held that the fee was unconstitutional because it was not based on the cost of the regulation. The city challenged the ruling, contending that the trial court erred in finding that the private club overcame the presumption of validity attaching to the municipal ordinance. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the ordinance should have been upheld unless the amount required for the license was clearly arbitrary and unreasonable. The record showed that the license fee generated income of over $ 300,000, but the cost of administering the program was much less, so long as police expenses were excluded. The city contended that the trial court should have allowed evidence of police patrol costs into evidence as competent evidence of costs and administering and enforcing the licensing and regulation scheme. But the court disagreed, ruling that the evidence lacked probative value because it included expenses devoted to locations other than that of private clubs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

306 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Morland Dev. Co. v. City of Tulsa


No. 49,621


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 96; 596 P.2d 1255; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 232



June 26, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring Opinion June 27, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1. Appellants appeal from an order of the District Court, Tulsa County, Honorable William W. Means, District Judge, enjoining them from using their land in violation of a zoning ordinance enacted by the City of Tulsa. On assignment to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1, the order of the district court was affirmed in part and reversed in part and the cause remanded for further proceedings. Both parties seek Certiorari.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED; DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; ORDER OF THE DISTRICT COURT REVERSED; AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO GRANT REQUESTED RELIEF TO APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought certiorari for review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1 (Oklahoma), which affirmed the trial court's order granting appellee city's motion for summary judgment and permanently enjoining the owners from conducting land-fill operations on their property in violation of addition enacted to the city's comprehensive zoning ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Following the city's addition to its floodway zoning ordinance, the city filed suit to enjoin the owners' land-fill operations, which did not comply with such addition. The lower court affirmed the trial court's grant of relief. On further appeal, the owners argued that the ordinance was unenforceable against their property because the city failed to comply with the notice requirements of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 405 (1971), to which the city countered that § 405 was not applicable and that it had complied with Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 404 (1971) by providing notice by publication. In reversing, the court ruled that the city's adoption of a comprehensive zoning plan was a matter of general public interest and required only general notice by publication pursuant to § 404 but that when the specific restrictions and zoning changes were adopted affecting the owner's prior conforming use, specific notice to the owners was required under Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 405 (1971). The court held that a valid ordinance was a precondition to entitlement to injunctive relief and that the owners could raise the ordinance's invalidity without first seeking administrative relief.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, vacated the lower court's decision, reversed the trial court's order, and remanded with instructions to grant the relief requested by the owners.

 

307 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


City of Norman v. Liddell


No. 51,000


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 91; 596 P.2d 879; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 236



June 19, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma Honorable Elvin Brown, Trial Judge. An appeal from the sustaining of defendants' demurrer to petition based on statute of limitations and dismissal of a suit by City of Norman for payment under a completion bond for sidewalks in a mobile home park in Norman.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City challenged an order of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which sustained the demurrers of defendants, landowners and their surety, and dismissed the City's action seeking specific performance of the landowners' agreement to construct and install sidewalks or, in the alternative, a judgment on the surety bond for the City's use in construction of the sidewalks.


OVERVIEW: The landowners supported their demurrer by arguing that, under Norman, Okla., Ordinance #1890, an action on a surety bond had to be initiated prior to the expiration of the bond. The City claimed that the five year limitation of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § (1971) applied and began to run from the date of a breach of a condition of the bond. The court noted that under the City's ordinance, sidewalks had to be completed by the time that 65 percent of the lots of the subdivision were developed or within two years of the approval of the bond, whichever was first. If 65 percent of the lots were not developed, owners had two years for performance before the surety was liable on the bond. Thus, a breach of a condition of the bond might not accrue until the two years expired. The court concluded that it would violate Okla. Const. art. V, § 46 to construe the ordinance as a statute of limitations. The court held that the ordinance provision stating that the City had to institute an action prior to the expiration of the bond to recover the cost of uncompleted sidewalks was not a statute of limitations, but merely a directory provision. Therefore, non-compliance did not bar the City's action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

308 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Reliable Life Ins. Co. v. Cook


No. 50,279


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 88; 601 P.2d 455; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 297



June 12, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 10, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma Honorable Carmon C. Harris, District Judge. Appellant appeals from an action for deficiency judgment by appellee where a deficiency judgment of $247,611.84 was entered against appellant.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mortgagee brought an action in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for a deficiency judgment against appellant mortgagor following a foreclosure sale of the mortgagor's property. The trial court entered a deficiency judgment of $ 247,611.84 against the mortgagor. The mortgagor appealed.


OVERVIEW: On June 17, 1974, a foreclosure judgment was entered against the mortgagor for $ 933,376 and $ 93,338 in attorney's fees. The property was sold at public sale to the mortgagee for $ 620,100 that was two-thirds of the property's market value. The sale was confirmed on August 11, 1975 and the action for deficiency judgment was filed on October 16, 1975. The mortgagor alleged that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 686(1971) required the mortgagee to file its motion for deficiency judgment simultaneously with the motion to confirm the sale. The court held that the mortgagee had 90 days after the sale to file the motion for the deficiency judgment. The mortgagor alleged that the deficiency judgment violated his due process rights. The court held that the mortgagor was provided with sufficient protection within the proceedings of the deficiency judgment. The deficiency judgment was the difference between the greater of the market value or sale price of the property and the amount of the judgment. Because the mortgagor did not appeal the foreclosure judgment, the court held that the mortgagor was estopped from protesting the amount of the attorney fees. The fees were pursuant to the contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Kirk v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 53,103


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 80; 595 P.2d 1334; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 287



June 5, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Muskogee County, Oklahoma Honorable William H. Bliss, Judge. The Board of County Commissioners of Muskogee County, Oklahoma, Appellant, appeals from the decision of the district court which granted salary increases to a certain class of elected county officials who did not receive the increases which were given to county officials performing the same duties, but who did not take office until January, 1979, pursuant to 19 O.S. Supp. 1978 § 180.62.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, The Board of County Commissioners of Muskogee County, sought review of the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma), which granted salary increases to appellee county officers.


OVERVIEW: A statute was enacted that separated all county officers into two classes. The county officers involved in the litigation were in the class that received lower salaries. The county officers had been assigned duties that were not germane to their respective offices. The trial court found that the county officers were not compensated for the additional duties. The trial court also found that because the county officers were performing the same duties as officers who received salary increases, the county officers were denied equal protection of the laws. On appeal, the court upheld the trial court's judgment. The court found that the constitutional prohibition against salary increases under Okla. Const. art. 23, § 10 was invidiously discriminatory because there was distinction made in a group of individuals that comprised one class. The court determined that there was no rational basis for the law and it denied equal protection of the laws. The court concluded that the county officers were entitled to the salary increase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Daniel H.


No. 49,830


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 33; 591 P.2d 1175; 1979 Okla. LEXIS 211



March 6, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Juvenile and Family Relations Division, Honorable Joe Jennings, Trial Judge, from order adjudicating children dependent. The appeal challenges the constitutionality of 10 O.S.Supp.1972, § 1101(d) on ground of vagueness.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Juvenile and Family Relations Division (Oklahoma), which adjudicated the minor children of the mother dependant and made them wards of the court.


OVERVIEW: The mother of the minor children was hospitalized for mental illness. She left the children with their grandmother, who could no longer provide for their care. The grandmother placed the children in the children's home and the State filed a petition to declare the children dependent. The mother challenged the sufficiency of the allegations. The trial court held a hearing and found the evidence sufficient to adjudicate the children dependent. The children were placed in the temporary custody of the children's home. The mother appealed and argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1101(d) (Supp. 1972) was void for vagueness. The court held that the "proper parental care and guardianship" provision of § 1101 was sufficient for a dependency proceeding. The court held that the mere fact that the mother was no longer hospitalized did not make the trial court's denial of her demurrer to the evidence error. The court noted that the mother did not show that her mental health had improved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

311 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Transok Pipe Line Co. v. Richardson


No. 49638


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 165; 593 P.2d 1079; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 566; 65 Oil & Gas Rep. 539



December 26, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 9, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Grady County; Clarence L. Maher, Trial Judge. Landowners sought writ of mandamus to require gas pipe line company to connect premises and furnish gas, as provided by 52 O.S.1971, § 10. Trial court issued its peremptory writ of mandamus. Gas pipe line company appeals.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND PEREMPTORY WRIT OF MANDAMUS DISSOLVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gas pipeline company (company) challenged a judgment from the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma), which granted appellee landowners' peremptory writ of mandamus requiring the gas pipeline company to connect premises and furnish gas to the landowners' residence and hog operations, as provided by Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 10 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The landowners granted the company a pipe line right of way across their premises. After installation of the pipeline the landowners requested the company, at its expense, a connection to their premises and the furnishing of gas at the same rate as charged in the nearest city, under Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 10 (1971). The company refused, and the landowners brought a suit seeking a writ of mandamus to require the requested action of the company. The trial court granted the writ and the company appealed. It argued that the application of §10 was unconstitutional and violated state and federal due process guarantees, and the taking of private property for private use. The state supreme court dissolved the writ of mandamus. Compelling a public utility to service a market not theretofore professed or undertaken as public business was an appropriation of private property without just compensation. Section 10 did just that. The company had not undertaken, professed to undertake, or desired to make natural gas available for residential purposes and for a hog operation to require the company to furnish and make available the gas sought by the landowners was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Peremptory writ of mandamus requiring the gas pipeline company to connect the landowners' premises and furnish them with gas was dissolved.

Walton v. Charles Pfizer & Co.


No. 49833


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 164; 590 P.2d 1190; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 439



December 26, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected on Denial of Rehearing February 12, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court, Tulsa County; Jay Dalton, Trial Judge. Plaintiff filed an action for damages for personal injuries against multiple defendants, including the City of Tulsa. After proceedings during which the plaintiff dismissed the action as to all other defendants the City of Tulsa filed a motion for summary judgment, for plaintiff, which was sustained From the judgment, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant City in the patient's action seeking to recover for adverse effects he suffered from several different vaccinations administered by the City, free of charge. The patient asserted that the City was not immune from liability.


OVERVIEW: The patient suffered adverse reactions, consisting of permanent paralysis of his lower extremities, and damage to the lower organs of his body, as a result of several vaccinations that were administered to him, free of charge, at a health clinic run by the City. Within one year after attaining the age of majority, the patient filed an action for damages against the City. The district court, on the City's motion, granted summary judgment to the City on the ground that there was no substantial controversy as to any material fact. The court affirmed the judgment. Specifically, the court held that under Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 1752 (1971), the City was performing a "governmental function" when it administered the vaccinations to the patient because such activities were required, and not merely permitted by law. As such, the court found that the City was immune from the liability alleged in the patient's complaint, which sought damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

313 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Wiseman v. Okla. Bd. of Corr.


No. 52532


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 158; 614 P.2d 551; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 568



December 15, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order of January 31, 1979. As Corrected On Denial of Rehearing July 15, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application to assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Mandamus directing the Oklahoma Board of Corrections and the Oklahoma Department of Corrections (Respondents) to comply with Section 17 Enrolled House Bill No. 1567 of the 1978 Legislature. Respondents had refused to comply with section 17 because the Governor had vetoed that section but had approved the bill in all other respects. JURISDICTION ASSUMED; WRIT OF MANDAMUS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, Board of Corrections (Board) and Department of Corrections (Department), to comply with section 17 of Enrolled House Bill No. 1567.


OVERVIEW: Section 17 of House Bill 1567 required the Board to establish criteria for recommending inmates to be considered for parole; and required the Department to certify the total inmate population incarcerated in the various institutional facilities under their custody. Neither the Board nor the Department complied with § 17 because of the Governor's veto. Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus directing The Board and the Department to comply with § 17. The court found that since the Governor had to affirmatively approve all of the general legislation provisions of HB 1567 for such provisions to become law, and the Governor's approval was qualified by reason of his vetoing § 17, his qualified approval was a nullity. The court found that the Governor, having failed to approve HB 1567 within 15 days after the adjournment of the Legislature, the general legislation sections or provisions of HB 1567 failed to become law. Since none of the general legislation provisions of HB 1567, including § 17, became law, the court held that petitioner was not entitled to a writ directing The Board and the Department to comply with § 17.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus.

McGlumphy v. Jetero Constr. Co.


No. 48,719


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 154; 593 P.2d 76; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 562



December 5, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 23, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable William W. Means, Trial Judge. Materialman seeks payment for materials furnished subcontractor on construction projects through enforcement of lien, and other, rights, against certain entities, including the general contractor. By counterclaim, and by making sub-contractor a third party defendant, general contractor seeks to impress particular funds paid by sub-contractor to materialman with a trust to pay for unpaid materials furnished. General contractor asks for indemnity from any materialman's recovery against it and to recover additional expenses in completing the sub-contract; all as against the sub-contractor. That sub-contractor cross-petitions against the general contractor for monies owed for unpaid, but performed construction work. On trial to the court, judgment was entered allowing recovery to materialman as sought in the petition, including attorney fees, denying any relief against the materialman, and allowing judgments, with offsetting credit, sought by the general contractor and the subcontractor as against each other. Judgment allowed general contractor [***2] and bondsman to be indemnified by sub-contractor for judgment rendered against them in favor of materialman. Original defendants, including the general contractor, appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a general contractor and its insurer, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), allowing appellee electrical material supplier to recover payment for materials furnished to appellee electrical subcontractor on construction projects through the enforcement of a materialman lien against the general contractor.


OVERVIEW: A general contractor and its insurer sought to impose a trust upon the funds paid by its electrical subcontractor to an electrical material supplier for certain unpaid material that was supplied on two construction projects. The trial court allowed the supplier to recover payment for the materials that were furnished to the subcontractor. The court found the existence of an implied contract which required that the supplier provide electrical material for the subcontractor's use in complying with sub-contract on particular jobs and, therefore, a materialman lien was permissible under Okla. Stat. tit. 42, § 143 (1971). The court also held that the general contractor was owed the construction trust funds that were paid to the subcontractor. The funds were needed to pay valid lienable claims against the construction projects that generated the funds. The supplier was charged with notice and, therefore, was required to inquire as to the source of the payments from the subcontractor and make payments according to the statutory trust imposed by Okla. Stat. tit. 42, §§ 152, 153, rather than make a blanket application to the oldest purchase, on the basis of a letter agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the judgment of the trial court that was entered in favor of an electrical material supplier. The court reversed the attorney's fee award, making it part of the remand.

McFarland v. Atkins


No. 50,560


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1979 OK 3; 594 P.2d 758; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 552



November 28, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 15, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County Oklahoma. Honorable William S. Myers, Jr., Judge. Appellant-Plaintiff filed suit against Appellees alleging that The Oklahoma City Planned Parenthood Association was not operating in compliance with the rules, regulations, and standards set by the State Board of Health, nor with certain Oklahoma laws. A temporary restraining order was issued restraining Appellee charitable organizations from allocating additional funds to Planned Parenthood. Appellant brings appeal from Trial Court's order, after a show cause hearing on the temporary restraining order, which sustained the demurrers and motions to dismiss of all Appellees on the basis that the Appellant had no standing to bring the action.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order by the District Court of Oklahoma County Oklahoma in favor of appellee Planned Parenthood, Department of Health, and several charities. Appellant alleged that appellee Planned Parenthood association was not operating in compliance with the regulations set by the State Board of Health and Oklahoma law. Appellant challenged the ruling of the trial court that appellant had no standing to bring the action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that she had standing to seek an injunction requiring the State Commissioner of Health to enforce the rules, regulations, and standards of the State Board of Health for Family Planning Centers.The court found that appellant was not authorized to seek injunctive relief against the Commissioner. Appellant further contended that she had standing to sue the Commissioner by virtue of her status as third party beneficiary of the contract between the State Health Department and Planned Parenthood.Appellant alleged no more than that she was a citizen of Oklahoma and thus benefited from the agreements in precisely the same manner that any other citizen benefited. There was no allegation that the contracts were made expressly for her benefit. Thus, appellant did not have standing to bring suit against the Commissioner as a third party beneficiary. Appellant argued that she had standing, as a taxpayer, to sue to enjoin the unlawful expenditure of State funds. Appellant's status as a taxpayer did not authorize or allow her to so enforce the law. Further, appellant had no standing to bring suit against the charitable organizations involved on a third party beneficiary basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Carder v. Court of Crim. Appeals of Okla.


No. 51,477


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 130; 595 P.2d 416; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 491



October 3, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari Granted to Court of Criminal Appeals to review that Court's judgment in O-77-656, State ex rel., Dept. of Inst., etc. v. Maley, Okl. Cr., 569 P.2d 1020 (1977); that Court's judgment vacated inasmuch as it was issued in excess of its jurisdiction; Order of trial judge, Honorable John Maley, dismissing action (J-77-14) ordered reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent department of social services brought an action in mandamus against respondent judge, seeking vacation of an order dismissing a case brought against petitioner youth. The youth and petitioner father intervened. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Oklahoma) entered an order purporting to assume original jurisdiction and granting mandamus against the judge. The youth and the father sought review.


OVERVIEW: The youth was adjudicated as a delinquent child and a ward of the court. He was placed in the custody of the department. Within months, the father sought return of the youth's custody. Over the department's objections, the judge issued the order dismissing the case against the youth. In response, the department brought the action for mandamus in the court of criminal appeals, arguing the judge had no jurisdictional power to enter the order and, under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, §§ 1116(a)(3), 1118, jurisdiction over the youth terminated when he was placed with the department. The court of criminal appeals agreed and granted the department's request for mandamus. On review, the father and the youth argued the court of criminal appeals' determination was beyond its power to render. The department contended delinquent children, such as the youth, upon commitment to its custody, are its children, and are thereafter beyond the reach of the courts. The court granted certiorari and reinstated the order of dismissal because the court of criminal appeals had no authority to issue the relief sought by the department and the judge possessed the authority to voluntarily terminate his jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court treated the request for review of the father and the youth as a proceeding for certiorari, set aside and vacated the court of criminal appeals' order, and reinstated the judge's order of dismissal.

Mathews v. State Election Bd. of Okla.


No. 52,590


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 113; 582 P.2d 1318; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 471



August 11, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Mandamus compelling Respondent State Election Board and the members thereof to strike the name of Intervenor, Joe Cannon, also a candidate for District Judge, Seventh Judicial District, Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, Office No. 14, or, alternatively, mandate Respondent Board to conduct an evidentiary hearing to determine if Intervenor will have been a bona fide resident of the State of Oklahoma for six months next preceding the 1978 election.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION GRANTED. PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a candidate for district judge, sought a writ of mandamus compelling respondent Oklahoma State Election Board and its members to strike the name of intervenor, the candidate's opponent, or alternatively to mandate the Board to conduct an evidentiary hearing to determine if the opponent would have been a bona fide resident of Oklahoma for six months next preceding the election.


OVERVIEW: The candidate sought a mandamus to require the Board to strike his opponent's name from the general election, nonpartisan judicial ballot or in the alternative require the Board to determine if the opponent satisfied residency requirements to run for district judge. The opponent was formerly a resident of Oklahoma and held the office of district judge until the date of his resignation. He then resided in Florida. He returned to Oklahoma in June 1978 and as of the November 1978 election would not have held office for six months. The candidate contested the opponent's candidacy before the Board, which dismissed the candidate's contest without hearing evidence. The court denied the candidate's petition for writ of mandamus. The court held that where there was neither an explicit statutory nor constitutional provision setting forth explicitly the length of residence required to run for district judge, and the requirement contained in Okla. Const. art. III, § 1, requiring six months durational residency to be a qualified elector was unconstitutional, there was effectively no residency requirement as a qualification for district judge.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the Board did not act in an arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable manner in dismissing the candidate's contest without hearing evidence and the court would not issue a writ of mandamus.

320 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Puckett v. Cook


No. 51,850


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 108; 586 P.2d 721; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 466



July 18, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 6, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Prohibition. Action by plaintiff in action pending before judge to prohibit judge from giving effect to order consolidating plaintiff's case with case of another.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED; WRIT OF PROHIBITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner passenger filed an application for the court to assume original jurisdiction in his suit for personal injuries and requested the court to issue a writ of prohibition to prevent respondent judge of the Oklahoma County District Court (Oklahoma), from giving effect to an order consolidating the passenger's suit with the suit by the passenger's wife for personal injuries sustained when they were both injured in a bus accident.


OVERVIEW: In urging relief, the passenger argued that the trial erred in holding that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 559 (1971) was unconstitutional in restricting consolidation of cases and that consolidation was an abuse of discretion. In denying relief, the court held that in prohibiting consolidation without the consent of all parties § 559 unconstitutionally encroached on the power of the judiciary to hear and decide justiciable controversies provided by Okla. Const. art. VII, § 7 and thus was an abridgement of the separation of powers set forth in Okla. Const. art. IV § 1. The court ruled that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 79 (1971) merely permitted the court to grant consolidation in the exercise of sound judicial discretion and that there was nothing inherently improper in a statute defining procedure so long as it did not seek to supplant the exercise of judicial discretion. The court found that the two suits were for injuries sustained by the passenger and his wife in the same accident, both claimed damages against the same bus company, and both actions involved the same medical expert and common questions of fact as to liability. The court held that consolidation was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction for purposes of issuing its opinion but denied the passenger's application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for writ of prohibition.

 

321 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Haas


No. 49,914


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 109; 586 P.2d 1093; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 467



June 18, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma, Honorable Elvin J. Brown, Trial Judge. Action brought for defamation of character based on libel contained in a letter addressed to the editor of, and published in a newspaper. Trial court granted summary judgment to defendant letter writer, determined plaintiff to be a public figure, and applied a qualified privilege. Plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant member of a local civic group challenged a judgment of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which granted defendant letter writer's motion for summary judgment on the member's libel suit.


OVERVIEW: The alleged defamatory statements were contained in a letter that was addressed to the editor of, and published in a university newspaper. The letter was in response to a letter written by the member similarly addressed and published in the same newspaper a few days before the letter writer's response. The court reversed the judgment and remanded. The court held as follows: 1) the member was a public figure because he voluntarily injected himself into the vortex of the public controversy by writing his letter addressed to the editor with the intent it be published and his letter sought to engage the public's attention to influence public issues; 2) the member was a public defamation plaintiff for the limited range of issues encompassed within his letter, and as a result, he was subject to the New York Times standard for defamation; 3) there was no longer a "conditional privilege" available, either by statute or common law, as a defense to a public defamation plaintiff; and 4) viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the member, reasonable men could have reached a different conclusion as to whether the letter writer wrote his letter with actual malice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court granting the letter writer's motion for a summary judgment and remanded the case.

 

322 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


J.F.C. v. Dep't of Insts., Soc. & Rehab. Servs.


No. 50,107


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 56; 577 P.2d 1300; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 380



April 25, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Hon. Stewart M. Hunter, Trial Judge. From an order terminating mother's parental rights in six children, appellant mother appeals.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which terminated her parental rights to six children, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (Supp. 1975). The children were previously adjudged dependent and neglected under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1101 et seq. (1972) and placed in the custody of appellee Oklahoma Department of Institutions, Social and Rehabilitative Services.


OVERVIEW: The court held that a prior decision had disposed of the mother's claim that she was entitled to a jury trial. With respect to the mother's claim that there were no ascertainable standards for the application of Oklahoma's termination statutes, the court held that the standards were those determined in the prior adjudication of dependency and neglect. The court pointed out that termination could only be determined after the mother, over a period of six months, failed to correct the conditions condemned in the dependency hearings. Therefore, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (Supp. 1975) was not unconstitutionally vague because the mother had fair warning of the sanction and a guide by which to act. The court also rejected the mother's contention that § 1130 unconstitutionally placed the burden of proof upon her as to the issue of termination. The court opined that § 1130 gave the mother only the burden of persuasion as to whether she corrected the conditions imposed upon her in the adjudicatory stage. However, because the record did not contain the pleadings and standards that evolved from the prior adjudication, the trial court's order was against the weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holdings that the mother was not entitled to a jury trial, that Oklahoma's termination statutes were constitutional, and that the statutes did not wrongfully place the burden of proof on the mother. The court reversed the judgment terminating the mother's rights because the trial court's order was not supported by the evidence. The matter was remanded for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion.

 

323 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ruth v. State (In re Ernest James C.)


No. 49,277


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 51; 578 P.2d 352; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 371



April 11, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 24, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division 1. Appeal from District Court of Tulsa County terminating appellant's parental rights in minor children. Court of Appeals reversed trial court. Appellees seek certiorari.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED. COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED, TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Department of Institutions, Social and Rehabilitative Services (DISRS) sought certiorari following a judgment from the Court of Appeals, Division 1 (Oklahoma), which reversed a decision to terminate appellant mother's parental rights. The mother claimed that a verified petition for termination had been required, that Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1126 (1971) had required a trial de novo, and that adoptability testimony had been inadmissible.


OVERVIEW: The children were declared dependent and neglected and were adjudged within the purview of the Juvenile Act. Subsequently, an unverified motion to terminate the mother's parental rights was filed. After a referee recommended a termination of rights, the mother filed a request for a hearing in the trial court, pursuant to § 1126. Thereafter, the trial court denied the mother's request and confirmed the referee's decision. When the appeals court reversed, the DISRS sought certiorari. Upon review, the mother claimed that a verified petition for termination had been required, that the trial court had erred in failing to grant a trial de novo, and that testimony as to the adoptability of the children had been inadmissible. The court held that no verification of pleadings was required where pleadings were filed in a juvenile action after children were adjudicated within the purview of the juvenile statutes and where the need for termination was fixed after the juvenile petition and summons were filed and issued. The court also held that § 1126 did not require a trial de novo and that exclusion of the adoptability testimony would not have changed the decision to terminate.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment which reversed a decision to terminate the mother's parental rights.

In re Christopher H.


No. 49,500


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 50; 577 P.2d 1292; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 373



April 11, 1978

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma; Hon. Joe Jenning, Trial Judge. Appeal from order confirming findings of referee and terminating parental rights.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural mother sought review of an order entered in the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which confirmed findings of a referee and terminated her parental rights as urged by appellee Department of Institutions, Social and Rehabilitative Services.


OVERVIEW: In 1974, a petition was filed alleging the infant child was dependent and neglected by reason of failure of father to provide support and mental illness of mother. At that time, the mother was a patient at a mental institution and was alleged to be emotionally incapable of caring for the child. An order sustaining the petition was rendered. Six months later, a motion seeking termination of parental rights was filed. The motion alleged that the child was seen at a hospital for a cut on the head, scratches on the body, and that the mother was unemployed and had no suitable residence for the child. The motion also urged that the mother failed to continue psychological counseling. A referee recommended termination of parental rights under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130, and the district court confirmed the findings. The mother appealed. On review, the court held that the referee's decision was not supported by the weight of the evidence, which tended to show that the mother was not confined to an institution, was able to care for the child, and that the child was well dressed and healthy in the mother's custody. The court remanded for dismissal of the motion to terminate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the district court and remanded with directions.

 

325 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re Christopher H.


No. 49500


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 54; 580 P.2d 143; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 569



April 11, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Majority opinion 577 P.2d 1292.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the mother of a minor child, challenged a decision from the juvenile court (Oklahoma), which entered judgment for petitioner, the State of Oklahoma, and terminated the mother's rights pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1103 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The child was seen at a hospital for a cut on his head and a scratch on his body. The child was adjudicated as a dependent and neglected child by reason of his mother's incapacity due to illness. The State then sought termination of the mother's parental rights, which was granted. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. First, the court found that the juvenile court lacked jurisdiction because the action to terminate rights was filed on an unverified petition. Second, the court determined that the fact that the mother was unemployed and the additional allegation that the mother had failed to continue counseling for her emotional problems, which had originally caused him to be dependent, were not elevated into the scope and intent of § 1130. The court held that the juvenile court's construction of the statute was unconstitutional. Third, where a petition for neglect was filed, which did not seek termination and the child was adjudicated neglected, the mother did not thereafter have the burden of proof in a subsequent termination action. Fourth, the court held that the standard of proof required to support an order of termination was that of clear and convincing proof.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

326 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Carl v. Bd. of Regents of Univ.


No. 50,591


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 49; 577 P.2d 912; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 374



April 11, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Cleveland County, Oklahoma. Honorable Elvin J. Brown, District Judge. R.B. Carl, M.D., and State of Oklahoma, on relation of Larry Derryberry, Attorney General (appellants) challenge on appeal certain rulings of the District Court dismissing their action for injunctive relief which had the effect of compelling the Admissions Board of the University of Oklahoma College of Medicine to comply with Oklahoma's then existing "open meeting law". 25 O.S. 1971, § 201; which was repealed by Ch. 214, 1977 Session Laws. The Board of Regents of the University of Oklahoma (appellee) contended and the trial court ruled as a matter of law the Admissions Board was not a "governing body" of a state agency, was not supported in whole or in part by public funds, and was engaged in activities in the nature of personnel matters thus rendering Oklahoma's then existing "Open Meetings Law" inapplicable to activities of the Admissions Board.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, State and a member of the Medical School's Admission Board, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which dismissed appellants' complaint that sought to enjoin appellee university Board of Regents from allowing the Admission Board to meet in closed sessions in violation of the open meeting law, Okla. Stat. tit. 25, § 201 (1971).


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged the trial court judgment that dismissed their action for injunctive relief, which sought to enjoin the Board of Regents from allowing the Admission Board to meet in closed sessions. Appellants argued that the Admission Board was subject to § 201. The Board of Regents asserted that § 201 applied only to meetings of governing bodies and did not include a non-governing board such as the Admission Board, which had no power to govern. The court determined that the Board of Regents, the parent entity that created the Admission Board, came within the purview of § 201, and the Admission Board was a subordinate entity that also came within the purview of § 201 because it exercised decision making authority for the Board of Regents. The court concluded that the trial court erred in dismissing appellants' complaint based on its finding that the open meeting law, § 201, did not apply to the Admission Board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment.

Neal v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 50,292


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 47; 578 P.2d 1191; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 360



April 4, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding to review order entered by State Industrial Court En Banc, denying claim for compensation for lack of jurisdiction, claimant not having been injured in course of hazardous employment. Honorable Yvonne Sparger, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a workers' compensation claimant, filed a proceeding to review an order entered by State Industrial Court (Oklahoma), en banc, that denied his claim for compensation against respondent employer for lack of jurisdiction, the claimant not having been injured in course of hazardous employment.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was a tire and battery changer in the employer's automotive service section. He used hydraulic jacks and pneumatic tools. He was injured by battery acid. His claim was denied on the basis that the place where he worked was not a workshop within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 3(11) (1971) of the Workers' Compensation Law. In reversing the decision the court erased any distinction made on the basis of whether the place where the work was performed was a garage or a service station, or one where minor repairs were made versus major overhauls. The court also dispatched an attempted distinction based on the whether power tools were used only incidentally in the performance of the work. The court noted that § 3(11) declared a workshop to be any place where machinery was employed and manual or mechanical labor exercised for gain in repairing or adopting for sale any article or thing. The court also held that it was not significant that the injury occurred while the claimant was not using any power tools.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order that denied the claim for compensation and remanded the cause for adjudication of any liability resulting from accidental injury in hazardous employment.

Associated Milk Producers, Inc. v. City of Midwest City


No. 49495


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 38; 583 P.2d 491; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 340



March 21, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1978.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city and its officials sought review of the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff milk producer and granted the milk producer a permanent injunction against the city that prevented the city from enforcing certain provisions of city ordinances as against the milk producer.


OVERVIEW: The milk producer operated a plant in Midwest City. Running north and south along the west side of this tract was a road that was designated a "major street" by the city ordinances. The milk producer sought to build its own warehouse on its property and filed for a building permit. The permit was granted subject to two conditions. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that the ordinances concerned were in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 85(e) (1971) as well as Midwest City, Okla., Charter, art. VIII, § 8 that adopted the general laws of the state of Oklahoma concerning such things as the paving or surfacing of streets.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Phillips v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 51,159


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 34; 577 P.2d 1278; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 339



March 14, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction and Petition for Writ of Prohibition to restrain Oklahoma Tax Commission from assessing and/or collecting use tax under 68 O.S.Supp.1977, § 1402a.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION GRANTED. WRIT OF PROHIBITION ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a businessman, asked the court to assume original jurisdiction and restrain respondent, the Oklahoma Tax Commission, from assessing and/or collecting an additional 2 percent "use" tax authorized by Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1402a (Supp. 1977) He asserted the tax discriminated against interstate commerce in violation of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl.3. Two intervenors joined in the action against the tax.


OVERVIEW: The businessman and intervenors argued that additional use tax placed a more onerous burden on products he brought into the state through interstate commerce than it imposed on products purchased within Oklahoma. Several foreign companies doing business in Oklahoma filed amici curiae briefs in support of the businessman's petition. The Oklahoma Municipal League filed an amicus curiae opposing the petition, based on the amount of tax dollars that would be lost if the tax were held unconstitutional. The court assumed original jurisdiction because the constitutionality of the statute was a matter of great public concern. The court rejected the Commission's argument that the use tax statutes could be applied to an in-state sale because by definition a use tax applied to out of state sales. Applying the equality test, as set out by the United States Supreme Court, the court held that § 1402a was unconstitutional because it was it imposed an additional tax that resulted in an unequal and discriminatory tax burden on interstate commerce. The inequality was not rectified by the existence of statutorily enacted optional and non-uniform municipal sales taxes.


OUTCOME: The court granted the businessman and intervenor's application to assume original jurisdiction. The court issued an injunction restraining the Commission from enforcing an additional use tax that was recently enacted.

 

330 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hillcrest Med. Ctr. v. Lee


No. 50,974


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 23; 575 P.2d 971; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 313



February 28, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma Honorable Robert G. Green, Judge..



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of the order of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which ruled in favor of appellee, the Oklahoma Department of Corrections, after the Department entered a special appearance and objection to jurisdiction asserting that venue properly lay in Oklahoma County, the seat of State government, under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 133 (1971), and that venue in Tulsa County was improper.


OVERVIEW: While the Tulsa County Sheriff was transporting a prisoner back to the Department's reformatory after his charges were dismissed; the prisoner was severely injured in an automobile accident. He was transported to the hospital, which was located in Tulsa County, and treated. The prisoner and the Department refused to pay the prisoner's medical bills, and the hospital filed the action in Tulsa County to recover payment. The Department alleged that as a department of the state government, it could only be sued in Oklahoma County, the seat of state government. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, citing § 133, which provided that an action against a public officer for an act done by him in virtue of his office must be brought in the county where the action arose. Thus, venue lay in Oklahoma County, the county in which the refusal of payment for the prisoner's medical services emanated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that venue against the Department was in the county in which the Department declined to pay for services rendered to the prisoner.

Post Oak Oil Co. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


Nos. 51,662, 51,669


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 20; 575 P.2d 964; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 310; 60 Oil & Gas Rep. 319



February 21, 1978 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Jurisdiction Assumed And Writ of Prohibition Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff producers brought an action against defendant Oklahoma Tax Commission (Commission) that sought a writ of prohibition and that alleged the conservation excise tax, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1107 et seq. (1977), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Commission administered a conservation excise tax, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1107 et seq. (1977), on producers of oil. The producers brought an action that sought to declare the tax unconstitutional. The court denied the writ of prohibition and held that the tax was constitutional. The court held that the tax was on the local state act of severance or production of gas without regard to sale in intrastate or interstate commerce that occurred after severance and after the levying of the tax. The court found that the levy was prior to entrance of any gas into interstate commerce and was on all gas so severed and produced without regard to subsequent entrance into either intra or interstate commerce. The court found that if there was an effect on produced gas entering on interstate commerce, that effect was incidental. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional as placing an undue and discriminatory burden on interstate commerce. The court further held that there was no discrimination between indirect owners of working interest and royalty interest as opposed to non-resident owners of working interest and royalty interest in Oklahoma.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition.

Gordon v. Gordon


No. 49,371


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1978 OK 17; 577 P.2d 1271; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 307



February 7, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 19, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Honorable Joe Cannon, Judge. Appeal by wife from the trial court's award of custody of three-year-old child of the parties to the husband in a divorce action absent a judicial finding of unfitness on the part of the mother. She alleges the order was clearly against the weight of the evidence and that the trial court abused its discretion.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted a divorce to the parties and awarded custody of their two-year-old child to appellee father. The trial court found the mother was fit, but the father contended that the custody award could not be reversed in reliance upon the maternal preference provision of Okla. Stat. tit. 30, § 11 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The mother brought an action for divorce, requesting custody of the parties' two-year old child. She had taken care of the child since his birth. She was not employed and the overwhelming majority of her time was spent at home with him. The trial court granted the divorce to both parties, and awarded custody of the child to the father. On appeal, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion by ordering the child's custody placed with his father rather than with his mother. The gender-based means chosen by the Oklahoma Legislature for determining custody in a divorce action was substantially related to the important objective of providing for the welfare of its minor citizens and the classification scheme contained in Okla. Stat. tit. 30, § 11 (1971) was constitutional. The evidence did not support the trial court's finding that the child's welfare and best interests would have been best served by placing his custody with his father. The mother was a fit and proper person to have the child's custody and the award of custody to the father was clearly against the weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case in a divorce action.

Fowler v. Brashear


No. 50705


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1978 OK 11; 574 P.2d 621; 1978 Okla. LEXIS 574



January 31, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Washita County; Weldon Ferris, Trial judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant buyer challenged an order from the District Court of Washita County (Oklahoma), which sustained appellee sellers' motions for summary judgment as to the buyer's action seeking specific performance and ordered the cause to proceed as a partition suit.


OVERVIEW: The buyer brought suit for specific performance of an sales contract for some 240 acres of real property that he entered into with the sellers' agent. The buyer, who lived in Alaska and was the sellers' brother, owned an undivided one-ninth interest in the real property. The sellers, who owned the other eight-ninths, sought partition. The trial court sustained the sellers' motions for summary judgment on the specific performance claim and ordered the suit to proceed as a partition action. The buyer appealed, contending that the statute of frauds was discriminatory and unconstitutional. The court disagreed, holding that: (1) the statute of frauds required the agency agreement to sell real property to be in writing and to be subscribed by the party to be charged; (2) the statute did not violate the prohibition against discrimination between citizens of different states; (3) the agent did not deny his authority as the sellers' agent; (4) the agent admitted by his affidavit that his authority was not in writing; and (5) the motions for summary judgment were properly granted where there was no material fact issue in dispute and the sellers were entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which had sustained the sellers' motions for summary judgment as to the buyer's action seeking specific performance of the sales contract. The court remanded the cause to proceed in partition as ordered by the trial court.

State ex rel. Grand Jury v. Pate


No. 51,546


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 232; 572 P.2d 226; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 804



November 29, 1977 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Jurisdiction assumed and Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State asked the court to assume original jurisdiction against respondent district judge and bar the filing of the order dismissing the "Accusation for Removal."


OVERVIEW: The State empanelled a grand jury to consider a bill of accusation for the removal of a county official. The district judge issued an order and dismissed the case. The district judge held that, under Okla. Const. art. II, § 18 (1971), the grand jury had no legal capacity to sue and was not a proper party for removal. The State then filed a petition for writ with the court asking it to assume original jurisdiction against the district judge and bar the filing of the order dismissing the accusation for removal. The question on review was whether Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1182 (1910) was repealed and amended in such a manner that a duly empanelled grand jury could legally initiate a proceeding of accusation for removal against a county official. The court noted that removal proceedings were civil in nature, but that ouster proceedings had attributes in the nature of both a criminal action and civil action; thus, Okla. Const. art. II, § 18 was held not to repeal the power of a grand jury to initiate, investigate, or indict the removal of a public officer. The writ of prohibition was granted. The case was remanded to the trial court for reinstatement and further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court assumed jurisdiction and granted the writ of prohibition to the State. The case was remanded to the trial court for reinstatement of the case and for further proceedings.

 

336 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


J.V. v. State


No. 48,897


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 224; 572 P.2d 1283; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 801



November 22, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 19, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court of Tulsa County; Joe Jennings, Trial Judge..



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother contested the order that the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) entered in favor of appellee state, terminating the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the order lacked legal basis because it: (1) issued despite her requests for a trial by jury; and (2) had insufficient evidentiary support. The mother secured partial relief. The court began by noting that the right to jury secured by Okla. Const. art. II, § 19 was limited to those cases in which the right existed either at common law or in federal court just prior to statehood.The court's review of the language, structure, and history of the Oklahoma juvenile code led the court to conclude that the right to jury only extended to hearings to determine whether the child was within the purview of the code. Conversely, a hearing on the question of termination of parental rights was not a hearing to determine whether the child was within the purview of the juvenile code. Consequently, the legislature did not provide for a jury as part of termination proceedings. The record was deficient, however, in that its condition did not permit the court to determine whether the trial court had properly concluded that termination of the mother's parental rights was in the child's best interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as it related to the finding that the mother was not entitled to a jury in the hearing determining whether her parental rights should be terminated. The court reversed and remanded the judgment to the extent that it ordered the termination of the mother's parental rights.

Hitchcock v. Allison


No. 50,525


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 221; 572 P.2d 982; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 795



November 15, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County; S. Thomas Coleman, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenants challenged an order from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which denied the tenants' writ of replevin against appellee landlord, rendered a money judgment for the landlord, and established a lien on the tenants' personal property that was in the landlord's possession.


OVERVIEW: The question was whether Okla. Stat. tit. 41, § 42 (Supp. 1973), was unconstitutional when tested by U.S. Const. amend. XIV as applied through 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and whether a private person acting under the statute did so under color of state law. The tenants rented a mobile home from the landlord, and while they were in the process of getting a divorce, they separated and left the mobile home and their personal property behind. It was winter, the furnace was not working, the pipes froze and burst, and water damaged the premises. The landlord stored the tenants' property and would not return it until they paid what they owed, so the tenants filed for replevin. The court opined that the state's legalization of certain action did not mean that the state was a participant, but that the state was establishing rules governing the parties' rights. The court noted that the disputed statute created only the right to act, but it did not require an action. The court stated that the landlord took the initiative, not the state, so it was not state action under the Fourteenth Amendment and was limited to the goods the landlord stored. The court concluded that the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which denied the tenants' writ of replevin, rendered a money judgment for the landlord, and established a lien on the tenants' personal property that was in the landlord's possession.

 

338 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. Cumberland Operating Co.


No. 50,136


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 164; 569 P.2d 974; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 690



September 20, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Okmulgee County, Oklahoma; Honorable Kirk Woodliff, Judge. Certiorari granted pursuant to 12 O.S. 1971 § 952(b)(3). Appellant seeks to apply 12 O.S. 1975 Supp. § 1055 as the measure of damages in a wrongful death action of a minor. The trial court in granting a motion for partial summary judgment held the statute was not applicable because it did not become effective until after the date of the accident which resulted in the death of the minor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order from the District Court of Okmulgee County (Oklahoma), which granted partial summary judgment to appellee corporation in the father's action for the wrongful death of his son and found that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1055 (1975 Supp.) did not become effective until after the date of the son's death.


OVERVIEW: The son was killed when he fell from an oil well pump jack. The father filed a wrongful death action against the corporation and sought to apply Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1055 (1975 Supp.) as the measure of damages. The corporation objected and argued that § 1055, which was in effect at the time the father filed the action, had not yet gone into effect at the time of the son's accidental death. The trial court agreed and granted the corporation partial summary judgment. The father sought review and argued that § 1055 was purely procedural and was therefore applicable retroactively to the time of the son's accident. The court found that § 1055 would have been applicable retroactively if the legislature had provided for that or if the statute were procedural and did not affect vested or contractual rights, that § 1055 created and enlarged the substantive rights of survivors in a wrongful death action, and that § 1055 was not applicable retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Eustice v. Brazille


No. 49,444


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 147; 567 P.2d 92; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 661; 22 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 555



July 26, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma; Honorable Ronald Ricketts, Judge. Appellee sold Appellant a motorcycle and subsequently assigned the security agreement to Bank with full recourse. Upon default by Appellant, Bank notified Appellee his recourse was due and made oral demand for payment. Appellee paid the full balance due Bank under terms of the security agreement and paid full balance due to repair shop for repairs and remodeling, and repossessed the motorcycle from the repair shop. Appellant brought suit against Appellee for conversion due to Appellee's payment of balance due Bank and repair shop and repossession of motorcycle without Appellant's consent or authority. Trial Court held Appellee purchased back the retail installment obligation of Bank, stood in Bank's shoes as a secured party, and had right to repossession under 12A O.S. 1971, § 9-503.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchaser sought review of the decision of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which held that the appellee seller had a right to repossession of a motorcycle sold to the purchaser under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 9-503 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The purchaser bought a motorcycle from the seller. The seller assigned its security interest in the motorcycle to the bank. The bank foreclosed on the security interest and the seller went to the repair shop where the bike was located, took the bike, paid the repairs, and then gave the bank the money demanded. The purchaser filed suit against the seller arguing that he had not received notice, nor had he given authority for the repossession of the bike. The trial court found for the seller. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the seller had the right to take possession under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 9-503 (1971). Okla. Stat. tit. 12A, § 9-505 did not require the seller to allow the purchaser 90 days after taking possession to recover or sue for conversion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court, which held that the purchaser had no action in conversion against the seller for repossessing the motorcycle.

 

340 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. Followell


No. 50,481


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 143; 567 P.2d 84; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 654



July 19, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to assume original jurisdiction and issue writ of mandamus to compel respondent judge to order payment of the statutory attorney fees pursuant to 21 O.S. 1976 Supp. § 701.14.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION GRANTED. WRIT OF MANDAMUS GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys filed an application with the court to assume original jurisdiction and a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent, an associate district judge, to order payment of statutory attorney fees pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.14 (Supp. 1976). The attorneys had been appointed to represent three defendants charged with first degree murder before defendants retained other counsel for the sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: When defendants retained other counsel, the attorneys filed applications with the trial court for payment of attorney fees of $ 2,500 for the representation of each defendant. The trial court held that, pursuant to § 701.14, all attorneys involved in any one case could not be paid more than $ 2,500 regardless of the number of defendants and awarded $ 1,000 to each attorney. The court did not agree with the trial court's interpretation of the phrase "payment in any one case." The court stated that while there could be one information or case number, there were three separate cases contained in each information. Each defendant represented one case, and separate trials could be ordered for each defendant. The court held that the references in § 701.14 pertained to each defendant. Further, the court held that mandamus did lie to require the trial court to pay up to $ 2,500 to each of the attorneys because the trial court erroneously interpreted the statute. The construction placed upon the statute by the trial court defeated the legislative intent to provide competent and effective assistance of counsel for indigents accused of capital offenses.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorneys' application to assume original jurisdiction and granted their petition for a writ of mandamus.

Okla. Alcoholic Bev. Control Bd. v. Heublein Wines, Int'l


No. 49,955


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 136; 566 P.2d 1158; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 649



July 12, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. On appeal to the district court from an order of the Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Board (Board) suspending the alcoholic beverage license of Heublein Wines International (Heublein), for thirty (30) days, the district court: (1) vacated Board's order of suspension because there was insufficient evidence to sustain a finding that Heublein was guilty of any willful misconduct that would justify a suspension or revocation of its license, and (2) determined that Art. 27, § 5, of the Oklahoma Constitution and 37 O.S. 1971, § 516, which prohibit advertising the sale of alcoholic beverages, did not contravene the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution. Board appealed from that part of the district court's order which vacated Board's order suspending Heublein's alcoholic beverage license for thirty (30) days. Heublein cross-appealed from that part of the order which upheld the constitutionality of Oklahoma laws which prohibit advertising the sale of alcoholic beverages.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma Alcoholic Beverage Control Board (Board) challenged the judgment of the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that vacated the Board's order that suspended appellee wine company's alcoholic beverage license based upon alleged violations of the state laws prohibiting the advertisement of alcoholic beverages. The wine company cross-appealed from the judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the adverting prohibitions.


OVERVIEW: The Board suspended the alcoholic beverage license of the wine company for 30 days, alleging a violation of Okla. Const. art. 27, § 5 and Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 516 (1971). The provisions alleged to have been violated prohibited advertising the sale of alcoholic beverages within the state. The wine company appealed to the district court and also sought a declaratory judgment declaring that the prohibitory provisions were unconstitutional. The district court vacated the Board's suspension on the ground that the wine company was not guilty of any willful misconduct. The district court also found that the prohibitory provisions did not violate the United States Constitution. The court affirmed, holding that the record did not support a finding that the wine company willfully allowed the unauthorized advertising because the evidence established that the telecasts were purely the product of mistake or inadvertence on the part of the national networks. The court further concluded that given the minimal interference with interstate commerce, the state's interest in prohibiting the advertising was superior to the wine company's interest in the unencumbered distribution of its commercials.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court that vacated the Board's suspension of the wine company's alcoholic beverage license based upon violations of the state laws that prohibited the advertisement of alcoholic beverages. The court also affirmed the judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the advertising prohibitions.

 

342 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bias v. State


No. 50,491


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 122; 568 P.2d 1269; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 618



June 14, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Creek County, Oklahoma; Hon. Rudolph Hargrave, Trial Judge. Appeal by defendant upon conviction of first degree murder. Among propositions-in-error was question of whether maximum statutory award for attorney fees was constitutional when appointed counsel expended extraordinary amount of time on the case and incurred extraordinary out-of-pocket expense. Counsel requested transfer of question to Supreme Court, Court of Criminal Appeals approved request and Supreme Court accepted the question for review.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree murder. The trial court awarded defendant's appointed counsel $ 250 under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1271 (1971) and did not award reimbursement for reasonable and necessary expenses. The case was transferred to the court for review, which accepted the question of whether § 1271's maximum statutory award was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel was appointed to defend him at his trial for first degree murder. In so doing, the defense counsel expended a total of 255.5 hours on the case and incurred over $ 500 in expenses. The trial court found that the expenses were reasonable and necessary and had caused unnecessary hardship, however, the attorney was awarded only $ 250 under § 1271. The case was transferred to the court for consideration of whether the maximum statutory award for attorney fees was constitutional when appointed counsel expended an extraordinary amount of time on a case and incurred extraordinary out-of-pocket expense. The court reversed and remanded, holding that on the particular facts of the case, the award of $ 250 was unconstitutional. Neither § 1271 nor Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 464 (1971) were unconstitutional on their face and represented the bar's duty to serve. However, where an attorney was burdened to the extent that he could claim compensation for extraordinary expenses, as was the case below, the statutory minimum was inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case.
