Wright v. Keiser


No. 48,721


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 121; 568 P.2d 1262; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 617



June 14, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Honorable Carmon C. Harris, Trial Judge. Summary judgment for defendant entered in a personal injury case based on statutes of limitation. Trial Court refused to allow tolling under 12 O.S. 1971, § 98. That court found unconstitutional a portion of that section which provides for the tolling for the time one absents himself from the state, notwithstanding the availability of statutory methods of service.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, motorist and passengers, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted defendant's motion for summary judgment in the motorist's and the passengers' action to recover for personal injuries based on a theory of negligence.


OVERVIEW: After two unsuccessful attempts to obtain service on defendant in their action for personal injuries, the motorist and the passengers learned that defendant had relocated to Nebraska after the applicable two-year statute of limitations period, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 95(3) (1971), had expired. The motorist contended that defendant's absence from the state for over one year prior to the expiration of the period operated to toll the statute pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 98 (1971), and their cause of action was timely. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment on the ground that a portion of § 98 which provided for the tolling of the limitations period for the time one absented himself from the state was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection rights. The court ruled that the fact that defendant was an absent party had no relation to the purpose of § 98, and to have ruled otherwise would have allowed the motorist to subject defendant to litigation over the incident at any time in the distant future.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the trial court's sustention of defendant's motion for summary judgment dismissing the motorist's action as barred by the statute of limitations. The court reversed in part the trial court's inclusion within the summary judgment ruling of the minor passengers' action, and remanded with instructions to vacate the order of dismissal with respect to the minor passengers' claims.

 

344 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Schwartz v. Diehl


No. 49,187


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 115; 568 P.2d 280; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 604



June 7, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2. Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Carmon C. Harris, Trial Judge; action against three Osage County officials and their bonding company. Service was obtained on the company's service agent in Oklahoma County and on the officials in Osage County. The officials appeared specially and were successful in quashing summons because of lack of venue. Court of Appeals, Division No. 2, reversed trial court. Defendants seek Certiorari.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED. OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED. JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a foreign insurer, public officials, their bonding company, and others, sought certiorari from an order of the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Oklahoma), which reversed a trial court's order quashing the summons for wrongful execution by plaintiff owner for lack of venue.


OVERVIEW: Public officials seized the owner's property in Osage County pursuant to a levy of execution. Thereafter, the owner filed a wrongful execution action against the foreign insurer, the public officials, and their bonding company, in Oklahoma County. The public officials filed a motion to quash. Although the trial court granted the motion to quash for lack of venue, the appellate court reversed and vacated that order. Certiorari was sought. The court vacated the appellate court's order, and affirmed that of the trial court, concluding that venue was not properly brought under Okla. Stat. tit. 12 § 154 (1971). That was so because the action, which was against multiple defendants, had to satisfy all applicable venue statutes. Venue was proper against the foreign insurer where the cause of action arose, or where the agent was located, which was Oklahoma County. The public officials, however, were subject to suit only in Osage County, where the cause of action arose. The public officials were not required to submit to the jurisdiction of the Oklahoma County court. Resolution of the matter on that ground obviated the need to address the constitutional issue raised by the parties.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's order. The trial court's order was affirmed.

Sheehan v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 49,878


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 112; 565 P.2d 370; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 610



June 7, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Honorable Joe Cannon, Trial Judge. Suit brought to recover estate tax paid under protest. Trial court found property was includable in taxable estate because decedent at time of death possessed a "general power of appointment" which was exercisable in decedent's favor. 68 O.S. 1971, § 807(A)(9). Taxpaying estate appeals.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executor challenged an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which held for appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission (Commission) in its assessing tax for additional property, principally corporate stock, coming to decedent through her husband's estate with the power of disposal.


OVERVIEW: Decedent wife and her deceased husband had executed reciprocal wills in which the survivor received a life estate and power of disposal with the remainder to their children. After the wife's death, the Commission assessed a tax on the wife's estate including tax on additional property coming to the wife through her husband's estate with the power of disposal. The executor of the wife's estate sued to recover estate tax paid under protest. The trial court held that the additional property was includable in the taxable estate because the wife, at time of death, possessed a general power of appointment that was exercisable. The executor appealed. The issue was the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 807(A)(9) (1971), which allowed valuation of a gross estate that included the value of interest in property a decedent possessed under a general power of appointment. The court affirmed, holding that the tax was not in effect at the time the power was created through the death of the husband, but that because the wife had alternatives to dispose of the impacted property after the statute took effect, the assessment of additional tax under § 807(A) was not arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The trial court order against the executor was affirmed.

Jones v. GMAC


No. 47,858


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 92; 565 P.2d 9; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 578; 21 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 914



May 17, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2. James Jones (appellant), commenced an action against General Motors Acceptance Corporation and Hudiburg Chevrolet, Inc. (appellees), for conversion of an automobile and other personal property. Summary judgment was rendered in favor of appellees in the District Court, Oklahoma County, Honorable Raymond Naifeh, District Judge. On assignment to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2, the judgment of the trial court was reversed. Appellees seek Certiorari.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED; OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a secured party and its assignor, sought certiorari with respect to a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2 (Oklahoma), which reversed the sustaining of appellees' motions for summary judgment and remanded the cause for trial. Appellant debtor had sought damages against appellees for the wrongful repossession of his automobile and the wrongful withholding of his personal property that was in the automobile.


OVERVIEW: Appellees contended that they rightfully acquired possession of the debtor's personalty under the provisions of a security agreement that allowed the taking of personal property as a natural incident to the lawful repossession of the collateral. The court of appeals had based its decision in reversing the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees on the unconstitutionality of a statute. On certiorari review, the court agreed that the judgment of the trial court should be reversed, but vacated the opinion of the court of appeals because the statute had been declared constitutional by an intervening opinion of the court. The court found that a question of fact existed as to whether the debtor was denied his personal property upon making a proper demand for its return. Appellees did not have a security interest in the personal property, and once a proper demand was made, the items should have been returned to the debtor. The court found that whether the debtor's personal property was detained wrongfully should be determined by a trial of the issue. There was also a question of fact as to whether the assignor was an agent of the secured party.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari and vacated the opinion of the court of appeals. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court as far as it related to the debtor's personal property that was taken with the repossessed automobile.

Loyal Order of Moose, Lodge 1785 v. Cavaness


No. 49,215


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 70; 563 P.2d 143; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 540; 93 A.L.R.3d 1234



April 19, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Honorable Joe Cannon, Judge. Appeal from an order of trial court sustaining defendants' demurrer to plaintiff's petition on the grounds action was barred by the statute of limitations of 12 O.S. 1971 § 109.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a charitable corporation, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which sustained a demurrer by defendant architect to the charitable corporation's complaint for negligence.


OVERVIEW: The corporation hired the architect to design, and construct a building. Seven years after the building was completed, there were heavy rains that cause water to accumulate on the roof. The water caused serious property damage. The corporation filed an action against the architect for negligent design, engineering, and installation. The architect demurred to the action on the ground that it was barred by the five year limitations of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 109 (1971). The district court sustained the architect's demurrer. The corporation claimed on appeal that Section 109 violated the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court ruled that the statute violated the Fourteenth amendment because it excluded one limited class of defendants, the owners or tenants in possession, from its protection and created a situation where an owner could be responsible after five years for injuries to a third person, while the architect, who was primarily responsible for the injuries would be immune from suit. The court found that there was no reasonable basis for the arbitrary classification and ruled that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that sustained the architect's demurrer to the charitable corporation's negligence complaint and remanded the case with directions that the action be reinstated.

Moore v. City of Tulsa


No. 48,889


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 43; 561 P.2d 961; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 501



March 15, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma. Honorable Robert Martin, Judge. Appellant appeals from a judgment of the district court sitting in its appellate capacity which upheld the decision of the Tulsa, Oklahoma Board of Commissioners suspending appellant's license to operate a private club.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of an order from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which affirmed appellee city board of commissioners' decision to suspend the licensee's license for a private club because it violated the city's ordinances relating to nude dancing and consumption of alcoholic beverages.


OVERVIEW: The licensee argued that the ordinance related to nude dancing in private clubs was an unconstitutional restriction of First Amendment rights, and Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 518(b) (1971) precluded licensure of private clubs by municipalities. Upon review, the court found that the ordinance was a constitutional exercise of the city's police power to promote public peace, health, and welfare. The ordinance was not based upon the censoring of a dramatic performance, but was based upon the regulation of the consumption of alcohol. Further, the court found that there was no usurpation of state authority or any conflict with any statutory provisions that prohibited the licensing of private premises where liquor was consumed. The licensee was not denied a fair hearing because the police chief initiated the investigation and filed the complaint and the police and fire commissioner participated in the hearing as a member of the board. The two offices were separate entities with different responsibilities and authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's order that suspended the licensee's license for a private club because it violated the city's ordinances relating to nude dancing and consumption of alcoholic beverages.

Helfinstine v. Martin


No. 47,719


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 42; 561 P.2d 951; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 497; 21 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 670



March 15, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Comanche County, Oklahoma; Honorable Jack Brock, Trial Judge. Appellant debtor brought suit to recover vehicle or value thereof from Appellees (creditor and its agent) for an alleged wrongful repossession. Although jury returned a verdict in favor of Appellant for actual and punitive damages, Trial Court granted Appellees' Motion for Judgment Notwithstanding the Verdict. Court of Appeals reversed and remanded.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED AND JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, creditor and agent, petitioned for a writ of certiorari after the appellate court reversed the lower court's decision that granted appellees' motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict in appellant debtor's action to recover the vehicle or its value.


OVERVIEW: The debtor entered into a retail installment contract and security agreement with appellees for the purchase of a pickup truck. The debtor defaulted. Appellees demanded payment, were refused, and then repossessed the truck by self-help. The appellate court held that appellees' act of repossessing collateral from the debtor violated Okla. Const. art. II, § 7 because it constituted a deprivation of the debtor's property without first affording him due process of law. In doing so, the appellate court overruled the lower court's holding that upheld appellees' act of repossessing its collateral. The court found that there was no state action in the self-help repossession made pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12A, § 9-503 (1971). Section 9-503 did not violate due process of law because the buying public was well aware of the fact that the contractual right of self-help repossession was an essential part of every automobile sales contract and, thus, they were not entitled to a hearing and notice before recaption. The contractual agreement authorizing self-help did not constitute a waiver of the debtor's constitutional benefits that rendered the contract null and void.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, vacated the appellate court's opinion, and affirmed the lower court's judgment that granted appellees' motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.

State v. Bev. License No. BEV-75-45 of Morris


No. 48,903


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 39; 561 P.2d 509; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 492



March 8, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of LeFlore County, Oklahoma, Honorable Harrell F. Followell, Trial Judge. An appeal by the District Attorney of LeFlore County from an order of the trial court denying its application to revoke appellee's beer license for violation of state statute forbidding the sale of beer to a minor. The minor was a male, eighteen years of age.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of an order of the District Court of LeFlore County, Oklahoma, which entered judgment denying the State's application to revoke appellee market's beer license for violation of state statute forbidding the sale of beer to a minor.


OVERVIEW: The market sold beer to a male, 18 years of age. The State sought revocation of the market's beer license alleging violation of the statute forbidding the sale of beer to a minor as defined by Okla. Stat. tit. 37, § 245 (1975), which classified minors by gender. The trial court found that a violation of the law by an employee was not grounds for revocation of a license holder's permit unless it could be shown that he acquiesced, or had a policy to that effect. The State claimed that the legislature in Okla. Stat. tit. 37, §§ 241, 242 (1971) intended to provide that a licensee was vicariously responsible for violation of the statute by his employee, agent, or servant. The market denied error on the part of the trial court and presented the issue of the constitutionality of the Oklahoma statutes classifying minors by gender. Because the United States Supreme Court recently held that these statutes were violative of the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution, the court affirmed the trial court's refusal to revoke the market's license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's refusal to revoke the market's beer license.

Office of the Governor v. Dalton


No. 50,326


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 34; 560 P.2d 971; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 481



February 22, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An original action on application to assume original jurisdiction and for Writ of Prohibition to prevent trial court from proceeding further in an action against a public official based on lack of venue.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ASSUMED AND WRIT OF PROHIBITION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a state's department of industrial development, requested that the court assume original jurisdiction and issue a writ of prohibition against respondent trial court to prevent it from proceeding further in an action brought by certain consultants for breach of contracts and for services rendered under an professional services agreement entered into with the department.


OVERVIEW: The department and the consultants entered into two contracts, a professional services agreement and a transportation study contract. The department asserted that proper venue was in Oklahoma County, and not in the trial court, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 133 (1971). The court agreed that venue was proper in Oklahoma County and issued the writ. The court found that the action in the trial court was not an action on open account, so as to bring it under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 142 (1971), because the court found no account based on running or concurrent dealings or that the agreements contained sufficient unsettled terms to satisfy the requirements of an open account. Moreover, the court sought to localize venue as to public officers under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 133 and found that the decisional act by the department to terminate the contracts emanated in the county of the official resident of the department. The letter of cancellation came from the same situs. The court reasoned that as the official acts complained of originated in Oklahoma County, venue was proper there.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction and granted the writ of prohibition.

Getty Oil Co. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 48,698


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 19; 563 P.2d 627; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 449



February 1, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 21, 1977; Supplement Opinion On Rehearing April 26, 1977, Reported at: 563 P.2d 627 at 631.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oklahoma Tax Commission. Taxpayer Oil Company appeals from decision of Oklahoma Tax Commission denying its protest to additional assessment of income tax on carryover losses from prior years disallowed as a deduction by Tax Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission, which denied the taxpayer's protest to an additional assessment of income tax on carryover losses from prior years disallowed as a deduction by the Commission.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, an oil company engaged in business throughout the country, was disallowed a carryover deduction claimed on its tax return for net operating losses and paid, under protest, an additional assessment of Oklahoma income taxes for the taxable year. After a hearing, the Commission denied the protest. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2353(12) (1971), Oklahoma taxable income meant taxable income pursuant to federal law, adjusted further as provided in Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2358 (1971), and that § 2358 provided that if a carryover loss was allowed on a taxpayer's federal return, § 2358(A)(3)(d) limited that figure to that portion attributable to activities carried on in Oklahoma. The court concluded that since the taxpayer did not have carryover loss deductions on its federal return, since gains in other states had made up for its losses, no carryover loss was allowed as a deduction on its Oklahoma tax return.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

353 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Krutsinger v. Mead Foods, Inc.


No. 50,394


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 16; 560 P.2d 195; 1977 Okla. LEXIS 457; 1977-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P61,286



February 1, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pursuant to the Uniform Certification of Question of Law Act, 20 O.S. 1976 Supp., §§ 1601 et seq., the United States Court of Appeals for the Tenth Circuit has certified to this court the following question: Whether in the year 1974 and thereafter until repeal of the Miller-Tydings Act and the Fair Trade Act of Oklahoma, it was valid to have an oral vertical price agreement under the immunity clause of the so-called Miller-Tydings Act, SEction 1 of the Sherman Antitrust Act, as amended, 15 U.S.C. Section 1, and the Oklahoma Fair Trade Act, or, in the alternative, whether a formal written contract was required in order to gain immunity from antitrust violation as provided in the Miller-Tydings Act and the Oklahoma Fair Trade Act? This court answers the question as follows: In order to gain immunity from antitrust violation as provided in the Miller-Tydings Act, the Oklahoma Fair Trade Act, 78 O.S. 1971, § 41 et seq., now repealed, did not require the contracts relating to sale or resale, as therein provided, to be formal written contracts. Such contracts could be oral. § 41.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Court of Appeals for the Tenth Circuit, appellant buyer challenged a judgment of a federal district court, which granted the motion of appellees, a seller and others, for summary judgment in an antitrust action. The appellate court remanded the case for consideration of whether a Miller Tydings Fair Trade Act price maintenance contract had to be a formal written agreement under Oklahoma law.


OVERVIEW: The seller manufactured and wholesaled bakery products and was the buyer's supplier. The seller sought to maintain prices of primary and secondary label bread by an oral agreement as between the buyer and seller. The buyer brought an antitrust action against the seller. The district court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment, and the appellate court remanded the case to the court to resolve an issue of Oklahoma law. The question the court was asked to decide was whether a Miller Tydings Fair Trade Act price maintenance contract had to be a formal written agreement under Oklahoma law. The court held that the language of Okla. Stat. tit. 78 § 41 (1971), coupled with Okla. Stat. tit. 78 § 134, allowed contracts contemplated under § 41 to be oral. The court concluded that it was thus not essential for a price maintenance contract, as allowed by the Oklahoma Fair Trade Act, to be a formal written agreement.


OUTCOME: The court held that it was not essential for a price maintenance contract, as allowed by the Oklahoma Fair Trade Act, to be a formal written agreement.

Moore v. Dep't of Insts. Soc. & Rehabilitative Servs. (In re Moore)


No. 48570


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 191; 558 P.2d 371; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 349



December 28, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; Honorable Charles E. Halley, Judge. Appeal by the natural mother of three children from a final judgment of the Trial Court terminating her parental rights and placing custody with Appellee for purposes of adoption.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural mother challenged a final judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which terminated her parental rights to her three oldest children due to severe neglect in a proceeding initiated by appellee Department of Institutions, Social and Rehabilitative Services pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The three dependent and neglected children were removed from the mother's home. Upon their supervised return to the mother, the children were in ill health, living in a state of filth, and in the primary physical care of their alcoholic maternal grandmother. The Department placed the children in protective custody and sought termination of the mother's parental rights. After a hearing at which the Department's neglect allegations were sustained by the evidence, the district court continued the case for dispositional purposes pending another home study. After a full evidentiary, dispositional hearing, the mother's parental rights to the children were terminated in the absence of a change in the mother's condition. On appeal, the court affirmed the termination by holding that the mother's testimony, coupled with the Department's written reports that were properly admitted under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1115, sustained the district court's finding that the children's best interests were served by placement in the Department's custody. None of the mother's testimony reflected any change in her behavior or in the conditions that had led to the earlier finding of dependency and neglect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment terminating the mother's parental rights to three children.

 

355 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Nucholls v. Bd. of Adjustment of Tulsa


No. 47,854


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1977 OK 3; 560 P.2d 556; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 675



December 21, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma Honorable Ronald Ricketts, Judge. Appellant appeals from declaratory judgment of district court determining that a portion of a city ordinance was unconstitutional and entering an injunction restraining appellant from enforcing the ordinance which prohibited the Board of Adjustment from granting a principal use variance.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a local zoning board and a city, sought review of a declaratory judgment from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which determined that a portion of a city ordinance, which prohibited the zoning board from granting a principal use variance to appellee property owners, was unconstitutional and enjoined the city and the zoning board from enforcing the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sought a variance authorizing the operation of a real estate office in a zoning district established exclusively for residential purposes. The zoning board ruled that it did not have jurisdiction to grant a principal use variance based on Tulsa, Okla., Rev. Ordinance tit. 42, ch.14, § 1470.1 (1969). The property owners filed a petition for a declaratory judgment, and the district court granted their motion for summary judgment, declaring § 1470.1 invalid. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the local ordinance was in conflict with Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 407 (1971). The court stated that to limit the zoning board's authority to only set-back building regulations under § 410 would be an unduly restrictive interpretation of § 407. The zoning board had the authority to permit principal use variances. If the state legislature had intended to restrict such authority, it would have amplified the matters enumerated in § 401. The intent of the Oklahoma Zoning Act was to give property owners the opportunity to present their claims of hardship to the zoning board. The local ordinance exceeded the city's powers delegated by statute and was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment, declaring that a portion of a city ordinance restricting the zoning board's authority was invalid.

 

356 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


McFall v. City of Shawnee


No. 47754


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 185; 559 P.2d 433; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 663



December 7, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2. Byron McFall and others similarly situated (appellants) brought suit challenging the constitutionality of an ordinance of the City of Shawnee (appellee) assessing nonresident lessees of lakeside lots $100.00 annual fee and resident lessees $25.00 annual fee. The District Court, Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma, Honorable Donald E. Powers, District Judge, upheld the constitutionality of the ordinance and rendered judgment for the City. On appeal, the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2, reversed and remanded with directions to enter judgment for appellants. Appellee seeks certiorari.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI GRANTED; DECISION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; AND JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city sought certiorari from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), which reversed a trial court's determination that a city fee, which assessed appellant nonresident lessees a higher annual fee for lakeside lots than that applied to resident lessees, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city leased lakeside lots and instituted an ordinance that assessed a fee to the lessees. The ordinance required the nonresident lessees to pay a higher fee than their resident lessee counterparts. The nonresident lessees filed an action against the city, challenging the constitutionality of assessing different fees based on their residency. The trial court determined that the ordinance was constitutional and the nonresident lessees sought review. The appellate court reversed the trial court's decision and the city sought certiorari. The court granted certiorari and held that, in order to uphold a municipal ordinance that subjected the nonresident lessees to higher fees based solely on their residency, there had to be a rational relationship between the treatment and the city's reason for the additional fees. The court found that the city's ordinance was presumed to be constitutional and that the nonresident lessees had the burden of proving the lack of a rational relationship. Since the nonresident lessees failed to provide evidence that there was no rational relationship between the additional fees and their residency, the ordinance was determined to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, vacated the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's decision, and affirmed the trial court's holding.

Hous. Auth. of the Cherokee Nation of Okla. v. Langley


No. 49095


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 142; 555 P.2d 1025; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 608



October 19, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Adair County; L. T. Spray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant housing authority sought review of a decision of the District Court, Adair County (Oklahoma), which dismissed its petition for condemnation of property that was owned by appellees, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 63, §§ 1057, 1078 (1971), Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 51 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The housing authority asserted that it requested that the trial court make findings of fact and conclusions of law, and that its failure to do so was reversible error. The court disagreed. Although the court believed it would have been a commendable practice, it did not find that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 611 (1971) was sufficiently encompassing to require the trial court to make findings of fact and to state conclusions of law when it sustained a demurrer or a motion to dismiss, or that failure to do so was reversible error. However, the court reversed the trial court's order because it held that the trial court erred in sustaining a demurrer based on the allegation that the Oklahoma Housing Authorities Act was unconstitutional as it related to the granting of the power of eminent domain to Indian Housing Authorities. The court held that the acquiring of property under the provisions of the Oklahoma Housing Authorities Act was a constitutional taking of property for the public use and welfare. The court also found the statutes in question to be a constitutional exercise of the complete power of the legislature to delegate the right of eminent domain to Indian Housing Authorities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

359 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


NCAA v. Owens


No. 50103


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 136; 555 P.2d 879; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 594



October 12, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Original jurisdiction assumed. Petition for writ of mandamus denied. Stay denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner athletic association sought a writ of mandamus to require respondent trial court to fix a bond and stay the temporary injunction obtained by plaintiffs, university coaches and members of the board of regents, in their action to enjoin the enforcement of the association's new rule regarding the number of coaches.


OVERVIEW: The association passed a new rule limiting the number of coaches on the member universities' teams. One university's board and coaches filed an action for an injunction to prohibit the association from implementing the rule. The trial court granted the injunction, and refused to fix a bond to stay the enforcement of the injunction. The association filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to require the trial court to fix a bond. The court denied the writ and denied the stay. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 993 (1971), providing for appeals of temporary injunctions, did not require the trial court to grant a bond or a stay pending appeal. To hold that a bond and a stay were mandatory would allow the legislature to impermissibly invade the court's role in granting injunctions. The trial court had discretion to grant or deny the bond and stay, and its action was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court denied the association's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the trial court to grant it a bond and a stay of the enforcement of the injunction obtained by the board and the coaches. The court denied the motion to stay.

Gaddy v. Okla. State Bd. of Osteopathy


No. 48359


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 125; 554 P.2d 1375; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 572



September 28, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Homer Smith, Trial Judge. Proceedings in district court for judicial review of order of Oklahoma State Board of Osteopathy requiring applicant to show his qualification to practice Osteopathy by proof of license from another state having reciprocity with Oklahoma or passing the examination of the National Board of Examination for Osteopathic Physicians and Surgeons, Inc. Court affirmed order of the administrative agency. Applicant appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant osteopath appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which affirmed an order by appellee Oklahoma State Board of Osteopathy, requiring the osteopath to show his qualification to practice by proof of license from another state or passing the examination required for osteopaths. The osteopath claimed that the order deprived him of an existing license without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: In 1961, the osteopath, who was licensed in Oklahoma, was investigated, surrendered his federal narcotic stamp, was charged with unprofessional conduct, and was the subject of a disciplinary complaint before the Board. In lieu of a hearing, he surrendered his license. He moved to Missouri, where he practiced under a Missouri license until it was revoked by that state's board. From 1962 through 1964, the Board issued renewal receipts to the osteopath. In 1972, the osteopath applied for renewal or reinstatement and, after a hearing, the Board entered an order requiring him to show proof of a license from another state or apply for reexamination. The court affirmed. The osteopath's 1961 surrender of his license was not temporary and ended his status as a licensee in the state. The renewal receipts resulted from administrative error and were of no effect because no license existed and, therefore, could not be renewed. Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 314 (1971) did not apply to the surrender of a license, the hearing requirement had been satisfied, and the Board's order acted within its authority under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 633 and 634(1971).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McClendon v. Slater


No. 49974


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 112; 554 P.2d 774; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 553



August 19, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING. An application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for writ of mandamus to require Secretary of the Oklahoma State Election Board to file and place names of petitioners on the Oklahoma November, 1976, General Election ballot as Presidential Electors for Thomas Jefferson Anderson for President and Rufus Shackelford for Vice-President of the United States on the American Party ticket.



DISPOSITION:  JURISDICTION ASSUMED; WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens sought a writ of mandamus to require respondent Secretary of the Oklahoma State Election Board to file and place the names of the citizens on the general election ballot as presidential electors for candidates of a given party.


OVERVIEW: The citizens filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to require the Secretary to file and place the names of the citizens on the general election ballot as presidential electors for candidates of a given party. The citizens contended that the state could not regulate the election process by its election laws. They argued that the power to regulate and legislate as to rules concerning presidential electors had been reserved in the people under U.S. Const. amend. IX and Okla. Const. art. V, § 1. The court held that: (1) Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 10-101 (Supp. 1975) was a proper exercise of the power granted by the United States Constitution to the state legislature, that it was not restrictive but definitive, and that it was a reasonable regulation of the method of selection of the electors of a recognized political party and not in conflict with the Oklahoma Constitution; and (2) the state had a duty to regulate all election processes and the state had exercised its compelling interest in doing so reasonably and properly through the election code and under the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus.

Hennessey v. Ind. Sch. Dist. No. 4


No. 48751


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 101; 552 P.2d 1141; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 542



July 27, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lincoln County; Donald E. Powers, Trial Judge. An appeal from trial court's denial of a writ of mandamus to require Independent School District No. 4 to permit Wellston Parent Teacher Association to use the school building for its meetings pursuant to 70 O.S. 1971 § 5-130.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent teacher association (PTA) challenged a decision of the District Court, Lincoln County (Oklahoma), which denied its petition for a writ of mandamus to require appellee school board to permit the PTA to use the school building for its meetings pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 5-130 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The PTA sought to use school facilities for its meetings. The school board had previously permitted other outside organizations to use the building, but denied the PTA's request to use the school facilities. The PTA sought a writ of mandamus compelling the school board to allow the PTA to use the school facilities. The trial court denied their request and the court reversed. It found that there was no evidence that the school boards rules had been violated or of a legitimate reason why the PTA should be forbidden use of the building. Further, the school board's rules and regulations that refused to affiliate with any association that was disruptive or unsupportive of the school board were unconstitutional as an abridgment of freedom of speech and a denial of equal protection. The school board only had absolute discretion to determine whether or not to open school buildings to the public and, once that discretion had been exercised and a decision was been made to permit use of property, the school board could not adopt a discriminatory and unconstitutional policy as to who would be allowed access to the facilities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which denied the PTA's petition for a writ of mandamus to require the school board to allow the PTA to use the school building for its meetings.

 

363 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sowders v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 48516


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 95; 552 P.2d 698; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 531



July 20, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM ORDER OF OKLAHOMA TAX COMMISSION. Appellant seeks refunds of Oklahoma Income Taxes paid for the taxable years 1969 through 1974, which claimed refunds are the difference between the taxes he paid as a single individual and what he would have paid if he had been a married individual and filed a joint return. He asserts this difference in taxes results from an unconstitutional classification of natural persons in the Oklahoma Income Tax Act, under both the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and Article X § 5 of the Oklahoma Constitution. The Oklahoma Tax Commission denied the refunds.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission. The taxpayer sought refunds of state income taxes paid, which claimed refunds were the difference between the taxes he paid as a single individual and what he would have paid if he had been a married individual and filed a joint return.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer asserted that the difference between the taxes he paid as a single individual and what he would have paid if he had been a married individual and filed a joint return resulted from an unconstitutional classification of natural persons in the Oklahoma Income Tax Act. The taxpayer asserted hat the classification of natural persons made in the law was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and under Okla. Const. art. X, § 5. The court noted that the disparity in the tax rates between a single individual and a married individual arose solely from a provision in the Oklahoma law that permitted a married individual to file a joint return. The court held that the Oklahoma Legislature had a rational basis for the distinction drawn between married and single persons for purposes of the applicable rates of taxation. The action of the legislature in creating the classifications was founded on the "ability to pay." Because the separate classification of single and married taxpayers was a reasonable classification, the classification did not violate either the Oklahoma or Federal Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Commission denying the tax refunds.

 

364 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Amax Pet. Corp. v. Corp. Comm'n


No. 47774


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 91; 552 P.2d 387; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 524; 55 Oil & Gas Rep. 162



July 13, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma. The Corporation Commission instituted proceedings to require the plugging of certain abandoned gas wells by the lease owner and operator and by the landowner whose predecessors in interest had taken an assignment of the oil and gas lease from said lease owner and operator. By its order, the Corporation Commission dismissed the action as to the landowner and ordered the said lease owner and operator to plug the gas wells involved. The lease owner and operator appeals from that order.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant operator sought review of an order from appellee Oklahoma Corporation Commission that required the operator to plug abandoned wells on the landowner's property in accordance with the Commission's rules and regulations. The order also dismissed the landowner and absolved her from any responsibility in plugging the wells.


OVERVIEW: The operator's predecessor leased property from the landowner's predecessors and drilled and operated gas wells on the property. The gas field was abandoned around 1957, and the wells had not been operated thereafter. Two years after the wells were shut in, the operator's predecessor assigned the lease back to the landowner's predecessors. Years later, the Commission's field inspector found that the wells had not been properly plugged. The operator argued that the Commission had no authority to require it to plug the wells under Okla. Stat. tit. 17, § 53 (1971) because the wells were not abandoned and were assigned to the predecessors. The court disagreed. The wells were abandoned long before the assignment. An employee of the operator's predecessor testified that the wells were abandoned. The terms of the assignment did not relieve the operator of its obligations. Intent to abandon could be established by acts rather than from possibilities of future use of the wells. Section 53 was constitutional. An operator was responsible for plugging the well under § 53, not a stranger to the operation. The time to plug a well was when it was abandoned. The Commission's order was proper.


OUTCOME: The Commission's order that required the operator to plug the wells properly was affirmed.

 

365 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Moral v. State (In re Rodriguez)


No. 48417


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 82; 552 P.2d 397; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 495



June 15, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Charles E. Halley, Judge. Appellants appeal from the judgment of the district court denying their petition to terminate parental rights because they were indigent and unable to comply with the statute, 10 O.S. 1971 § 1131, and pay the costs of publication. A denial of due process is alleged.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a natural father and his wife, sought review of a decision from the Juvenile Division of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied their petition to terminate the parental rights of the natural mother of the father's minor child so that appellants could adopt the child.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought to terminate the natural mother's parental rights so that they could adopt the father's child. Because the mother's whereabouts were unknown, the trial court authorized service by publication under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1131 (1971). When appellants were unable to raise the money necessary for publication notice, the trial court denied their petition to have the costs taxed to the court. The trial court found that the attempt of appellants' attorney at alternative service by posting copies of the notice conspicuously was unauthorized by statute and that it thus lacked jurisdiction over the mother. On appeal, the court held that: (1) publication was the sole method for providing notice to an unavailable parent under § 1131; (2) the statute required the payment of a fee that rendered it impossible for indigent parties to have access to the sole method for terminating parental rights prior to adoption; (3) the state could not prescribe a method for dissolving parental rights prior to adoption and then procedurally deny appellants access to that method; and (4) § 1131 was unconstitutional as applied because it deprived indigents of their due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

Foster v. State


No. 48425


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 80; 551 P.2d 1119; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 496



June 15, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Cleveland County; Elvin J. Brown, Judge. H. C. Foster (appellant) sought to set aside an order forfeiting an appearance bond posted by appellant on behalf of Paul Goodwin. The trial court refused to set aside the order of forfeiture and appellant appealed.



DISPOSITION:  Order Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety challenged the order of the District Court, Cleveland County (Oklahoma) refusing to set aside the order of forfeiture in favor of appellee state for an appearance bond posted by the surety on behalf of a criminal defendant.


OVERVIEW: The criminal defendant was arrested, arraigned, and released on bond posted by the surety. At the arraignment, a preliminary hearing date was set and later continued to a later date. The surety did not receive notice of the continued preliminary hearing date. When the criminal defendant failed to appear, the bond was forfeited. On review, the surety contended that he should have received written notice at least ten days before the required appearance of his principal under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 1330 (1971), and since no written notice was given, the forfeiture order was void. The court rejected the argument, holding that the ten-day notice provision did not apply to a bond forfeiture. The court reasoned that under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 1326 (b) (1971), the ten-day notice provision before forfeiture would apply only when no hearing date ws set by the trial court. There fore no notice before forfeiture was required.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Liberty Steel Co. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 48519


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 83; 554 P.2d 8; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 497



June 15, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oklahoma Tax Commission. Appellant protested an audit of its books by the Oklahoma Tax Commission. The Commission denied the protest. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign corporation requested review of a decision of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission denying the foreign corporation's protest of an audit of its books by the Tax Commission. The foreign corporation contended that Okla. Stat. tit. 68 § 1407 (1971) violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3 and the 14th Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The foreign corporation resold goods from a foreign state to Oklahoma residents. The foreign corporation did not have offices or employees within Oklahoma, and all orders were accepted in the foreign state. The foreign corporation had outside salesmen who called on customers within Oklahoma and delivered goods to customers by trucks owned by the foreign corporation. The foreign corporation protested an audit by the Tax Commission intended to determine the foreign corporation's sales tax liability to Oklahoma. The foreign corporation contended that it was not subject to the tax because it did not make any sales within Oklahoma and that Okla. Stat. tit. 68 § 1407 (1971) was unconstitutional as it applied to the foreign corporation. The court affirmed the Tax Commission's decision. The court held that the Tax Commission properly denied the foreign corporation's protest of an audit of its books and records by the Tax Commission because § 1407 did not create a constitutionally impermissible tax burden. The court stated that the foreign corporation's transfer of possession of its goods to its customers within Oklahoma was a taxable event regardless of the time and place of passing title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Tax Commission's order denying the foreign corporation's protest.

Miller v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 46702


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 67; 550 P.2d 1330; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 479



June 1, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Order sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of an order of the State Industrial Court (Oklahoma), which affirmed the order of a trial judge denying the claimant an award under the provisions of the Workmen's Compensation Law.


OVERVIEW: At the time of his injury, the claimant was an assistant manager of a retail establishment for respondent company, an own risk employer pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 61(d) (1971). The claimant was engaged in a nonhazardous employment. The only way that the claimant could receive an award was if the company was estopped to deny that he was injured in a hazardous employment. The claimant alleged that the refusal of the industrial court to apply the provisions of the Workmen's Compensation Law was a denial of equal protection and due process. On review, the court held that the company was not estopped to deny that the claimant was engaged in a hazardous employment at the time of his injury. Because the Workmen's Compensation Law provided a substitute remedy for employees covered thereby and did not take away the common law remedy from employees not covered, and since the provisions of the Estoppel Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, §§ 65.2 and 65.3, were in effect optional with the claimant, who could either claim compensation or pursue his common law remedy, it could not be said that the Estoppel Act denied him the equal protection of the laws or due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the order of the industrial court.

 

369 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Okla. v. Burk


No. 48287


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 70; 551 P.2d 1122; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 481



June 1, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Stephens County; Hegel Branch, Jr., Trial Judge. Action by plaintiff, The Board of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Oklahoma, appellee, against the defendant, Gerald C. Burk, appellant, to permanently enjoin the defendant from the unlicensed practice of dentistry, pursuant to "The State Dental Act", 59 O.S. 1971 § 328.1 et seq. After trial, the trial court granted a permanent injunction against the defendant. This appeal is from that order.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Stephens County (Oklahoma), which at the request of appellee Board of Governors of the Registered Dentists of Oklahoma permanently enjoined the dentist from the unlicensed practice of dentistry.


OVERVIEW: The dentist was not and had never been a licensed dentist. He owned and operated a dental laboratory. An investigator for the Board went to the dentist's place of business and inquired about "partials." The dentist made impressions, constructed partials for the investigator, and fitted the partials to the investigator's mouth. After the dentist was granted immunity as to his work on the investigator the dentist testified that he did perform the work as testified to by the investigator. Another individual also testified that the dentist made partials for him and for his wife. The trial court granted the Board's request for a permanent injunction enjoining the dentist from practicing dentistry. The dentist appealed and argued that the investigator had entrapped him. The court held that no entrapment occurred. The court held that the dentist's sympathy for the investigator did not alter his personal responsibility for observing the law. The dentist argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 328.19(n) (1971) was unconstitutional. The court held that dental work bore a sufficient relation to the public health and welfare that the statute was within the regulatory power of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

370 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Pease v. Bd. of County Comm'Rs


No. 48370


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 62; 550 P.2d 565; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 473



May 18, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Osage County; Don H. Hampton, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, county residents and taxpayers, appealed an order from the District Court of Osage County (Oklahoma), which affirmed the action of appellee Board of County Commissioners that approved the claims filed by intervenor Indian Nations Council of Governments (INCOG) for assessments against the county for its membership in INCOG.


OVERVIEW: The Interlocal Cooperation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 1001 et seq. (1971), was enacted to permit cooperation among local governmental units to provide joint services for mutual advantage. Pursuant to this Act, INCOG was formed to coordinate attempts to solve area wide problems, strengthen local governmental processes, and act as a clearing house for federal and state funds. After Osage County withdrew from membership, INCOG filed a claim with the Board for assessments, which was approved. Petitioners filed suit to prevent payment of the assessments, which was denied. Petitioners appealed, contending that the INCOG agreement was unconstitutional. The court disagreed, holding that: (1) the Board had the right to authorize payment to INCOG; (2) the county's use of ad valorem tax receipts to support INCOG did not violate the constitutional proscription against levying ad valorem tax for state purposes; (3) the INCOG agreement satisfied the § 1004 requirement as its stated duration, which was dissolution effected upon a majority vote of the Board of Directors of the participating members; and (4) the INCOG agreement was approved by the Attorney General as required by § 1004(f).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which had affirmed the Board's action that approved the claims filed by INCOG for assessments against the county for its membership in INCOG.

 

371 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Transok Pipe Line Co.


No. 47921


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 53; 552 P.2d 375; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 446; 54 Oil & Gas Rep. 713



April 20, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Major County; Honorable Joe Young, Judge. Appellant, Richard R. Allen, appeals from an order of the District Court of Major County finding that his sole and exclusive remedy for Appellee's construction of a pipeline across Appellant's property under the authority of eminent domain is an action in reverse condemnation and that he cannot also maintain an action for trespass and punitive damages.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the order from the District Court of Major County (Oklahoma), which dismissed his tort action against appellee pipeline company in his action for damages from the company's exercise of eminent domain without condemnation. The trial court also held that he could not maintain an action for trespass and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The landowner filed a tort action against the pipeline company, alleging that it constructed a pipeline across a portion of the landowner's property without prior consent and that the pipeline company constructed its pipeline upon the land without resorting to condemnation proceedings. The landowner further alleged that he had never been compensated and sought to recover punitive and other non-land damages for the wrongful invasion of his property rights and for injury resulting from the emotional strain caused by the company's wrongful and wanton conduct. The trial court found that the landowner's sole and exclusive remedy for the taking of his lands was a reverse condemnation action. On appeal, the court found that under Okla. Const. art. II, § 24, any person who went into possession under the power of eminent domain without condemnation proceedings had no title. The court also found that the public utility, which was invested with the power to exercise the right of eminent domain, was not thereby clothed with an immunity to trespass actions. The court concluded that the landowner had a distinct cause of action in trespass for damages and for punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the landowner's tort action against the pipeline company for damages from the company's act of exercising eminent domain without instituting condemnation proceedings.

 

372 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Barnes v. Transok Pipeline Co.


No. 45994


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 27; 549 P.2d 819; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 401; 54 Oil & Gas Rep. 507



March 9, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the State Corporation Commission.



DISPOSITION:  Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant rural landowners filed a complaint with the Oklahoma State Corporation Commission alleging that appellee pipeline company violated safety rules and regulations in laying a natural gas pipeline. The Commission en banc sustained the referee's recommendations denying relief and dismissing the complaint but ordered hydrostatic tests by a specified date and repetition of the test at five year intervals. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the enactment of enabling legislation pursuant to the federal Natural Gas Pipeline Safety Act of 1968, 49 U.S.C.S. §§ 1671-84, the Commission issued Order No. 70510, establishing safety standards. The Commission made findings on six specific complaints the landowners presented. The court held that the finding that the welding substantially complied with the safety regulations was an insufficient adjudication of the issue presented. The court explained that the promulgated standards were the minimum required. The court added that the Commission in effect found that the pipeline company "substantially complied" with the "minimum standards" prescribed for welding, but the issue presented was whether the welding complied with the minimum standards of acceptability. The court explained that if the evidence established a particular weld or welds failed to meet the minimum standards, the landowners were entitled to some relief involving that particular defective weld or welds. The court rejected the landowners' argument that it was a denial of equal protection to enforce stricter safety standards in urban areas than in rural areas.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Commission.

No. 47253

1976 OK 28; 550 P.2d 561; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 402



March 9, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Certiorari granted: Court of Appeals decision vacated; trial court reversed and case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: All parties sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma) which upheld a directed verdict in favor of appellee bank against appellant son and remanded for further proceedings regarding appellant widow in an action on two promissory notes and a credit life insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Decedent executed promissory notes in favor of appellee bank on a truck. Appellee issued a credit life insurance policy to decedent, and the age was left blank. After decedent passed away, appellee told appellant son that the policy was invalid because of overage of the insured. There was no cause of action against appellant son because he was not a party to the note or entitled to possession of the truck. The issue of replevin of the truck was remanded for further proceedings because factual issues remained as to whether the insurance policy was effective, which would affect the disposition of the truck.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court which affirmed a directed verdict for appellee bank in an action on two promissory notes and a credit life insurance policy was vacated and remanded because appellant son was not a party to the note or entitled to possession of the automobile, and factual issues remained which should have been resolved at trial.

Cont'l Oil Co. v. Okla. State Bd. of Equalization


No. 46798


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 23; 570 P.2d 315; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 679; 58 Oil & Gas Rep. 309



February 24, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 26, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Continental Oil Company appeals from an Order of the State Board of Equalization denying it relief on its Application to adjust the rate of gross production taxes pursuant to 68 O.S. 1971, § 1001(h).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company sought review of an order of the Oklahoma State Board of Equalization, which denied it relief on its application to adjust the rate of gross production taxes pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1001(h) (1971).


OVERVIEW: The oil company paid the seven percent gross production tax under protest and filed a complaint with the Board seeking relief under § 1001(h). The Board held that § 1001(h) was unconstitutional and denied relief. On appeal, the court held that § 1001(h) was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power because it established standards and guidelines for the Board to use in raising or lowering the seven percent gross production tax rate. Because the Board failed to adjudicate whether the seven percent gross production rate was greater or less than the general ad valorem taxes for all purposes would be, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. It held that it was the sole responsibility of the Board to determine the assessed valuation of the property, to set the assessment ratio for that class of property, and to apply it uniformly throughout the state. It further held that any property, including hydrocarbon reserves, that had to be assessed in compliance with § 1001(h) could be constitutionally assessed at no more than 35 percent of its fair market value, estimated at a price that the property would bring at a voluntary sale.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Stat. tit. 12, § 719 et seq. (1971), which reduced arrearages in child support to an amount including costs and attorney's fees and ordered garnishment of the husband's wages.

376 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Griffin TV, Inc.


No. 47172


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1976 OK 13; 549 P.2d 85; 1976 Okla. LEXIS 678



January 27, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 27, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County; Jack R. Parr, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant television station sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), entered upon the jury verdict in favor of appellee pet shop owner. The judgment awarded the owner actual and punitive damages. The owner had filed a defamation action against the station.


OVERVIEW: In connection with certain complaints against the pet shop that were broadcast by the station, the owner commenced a defamation action against the station. The station raised the affirmative defense of truth. By jury verdict, all evidentiary conflicts were resolved in favor of the owner and against the station. The trial court therefore entered judgment in favor of the owner, awarding him actual and punitive damages. The station appealed the judgment. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court for a new trial. The court held that the trial court improperly entered judgment in favor of the owner because the legislative creation of presumed malice under the Oklahoma libel and slander statutes was unconstitutional. If the injured individual in a defamation action was a private individual, then the states were allowed to define for themselves the appropriate standard of liability of the news media, but the choice was not unlimited. The standards could not impose liability without fault.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's entry of judgment and award of actual and punitive damages in favor of the owner in his defamation action against the station. The court also remanded the matter to the trial court for a new trial.

 

377 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Trevino v. Cannon


No. 49118


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 174; 544 P.2d 513; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 593



December 23, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Jurisdiction assumed; write of prohibition granted; temporary order held invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former husband sought a writ of prohibition to prevent the enforcement of an ex parte and temporary order directed to the husband's employer under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1276 to withhold the husband's wages.


OVERVIEW: The husband's former wife had brought a divorce action, but the husband could not be found in order to serve the summons. An alias summons was issued to the husband's employer, and the trial court also issued a temporary and ex parte order directing the employer to withhold payment of all wages and earnings of the husband until further order of the court. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1171.1 (1971) controlled, which prohibited prejudgment garnishment of personal wages. The court rejected the wife's contention the order was proper under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1276, which was a general statute governing the disposition of property in a divorce action. The court held that a statute that was enacted for the primary purpose of dealing with a particular subject prevailed over a general statute that did not refer to the particular subject matter but contained language that might be broad enough to cover the subject matter if the special statute was not in existence. Accordingly, the garnishment statutes and proceedings controlled, and not having been complied with, the ex parte and temporary order directing the employer to withhold the husband's wages was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction in the matter and granted the writ of prohibition.

Dablemont v. State


No. 47097


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 162; 543 P.2d 563; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 571



December 2, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Bill Ladd, Dist. Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Department of Public Safety, sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma) that reversed the judgment of the Department revoking the driver's license of appellee licensee, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 753 (1971) of the Oklahoma Implied Consent Law, Okla. Stat. tit. 47, §§ 751-760 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The Department revoked the licensees' driver's license after she refused to submit to a chemical blood-alcohol test. A hearing was requested pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 754 (1971) for an administrative hearing on the Department's decision to revoke. The revocation order was sustained at the administrative hearing, but on appeal to the district court, was reversed. The court reversed and remanded, holding that because the licensee's driver's license was not effectively revoked and she was not deprived of her driving privileges, she was not denied her procedural due process rights. The suspension was stayed pending completion of judicial review in which the licensee was afforded the opportunity to present evidence. Because the licensee was not deprived of any constitutional rights, she could not attack the Implied Consent Laws on constitutional grounds.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Burmah Oil & Gas Co. v. Corp. Comm'n


No. 48436


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 138; 541 P.2d 834; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 531; 53 Oil & Gas Rep. 205



October 14, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Original Jurisdiction assumed; Writ of Prohibition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner gas company sought a writ of prohibition against respondent Oklahoma Corporation Commission to prohibit the Commission from proceeding further with the claim of an individual for an order directing the company to furnish natural gas service to his premises as provided by Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 10 (1971). The company argued that the statute was unconstitutional if applied and that the Commission had no authority to enforce the statute.


OVERVIEW: The company was a private corporation engaged in the business of exploring for and producing oil and gas and associated hydrocarbons. The company owned and maintained a gathering line across lands owned by the individual for the purpose of transporting gas produced by the company from its wells to a gas processing plant. The line across the individual's land was maintained pursuant to a private easement, which was acquired by the company through purchase and not through eminent domain. The company had never engaged in the gas distribution business. The court held that the Commission had limited jurisdiction under Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 10 (1971), which required that a corporation connect a property owner outside of a municipality to any gas line that crossed the owner's land. The statute conferred no jurisdiction upon the Commission to enforce the provisions thereof. The court previously held that the Commission was without authority to hear disputes between two or more private persons or entities in which the public interest was not involved. Accordingly, the Commission had no jurisdiction over the action and the constitutional question was not reached.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition and directed the Commission to dismiss the individual's complaint.

Estate of Kasishke v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 47353


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 133; 541 P.2d 848; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 527



October 7, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent taxpayer appealed the judgment of respondent Oklahoma Tax Commission, which denied the taxpayer's protest against the assessment of additional estate taxes and taxpayer's claim for refund of estate taxes previously paid.


OVERVIEW: Estate taxes were filed for decedent's estate by the taxpayer, its administrator. The Commission assessed additional tax. Two years later, while the protest was pending, the taxpayer amended the protest seeking a refund. The Commission found that the taxpayer did not file a timely petition. A timely protest was filed but it did not refer to assessments on a bond that the taxpayer was challenging. The addition of the challenge to the tax on the bonds was not an amendment to the original protest and did not relate back to the original filing. The taxpayer argued that Okla. Stat. Art. 68, § 227 (1971) provided a three year statute of limitations for actions to recover taxes erroneously paid and the court found that § 227 did not apply to estate taxes, which required more rapid settlement. The time limit in Okla. Stat. Art. 68, § 815 (1971) was not applicable to overpayments made by reason of federal tax liability not being finally determined at the time taxes were assessed. Even though the claim was not timely filed regarding the assessment on the bonds, an issue of taxability of those bonds was shown and § 815 permitted the correction of an assessment as justice required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commissions order and remanded to direct that the taxpayer be allowed a setoff against the assessments for taxes previously paid.

 

381 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Caywood v. Caywood


No. 48915


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 177; 541 P.2d 188; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 516



September 29, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] That portion of the act declared unconstitutional and void; interlocutory order of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court certified an immediate appeal of its order that interpreted the language contained in Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1278 (1971), as amended as Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1278 (Supp. 1975), in which the trial court refused to award all marital property to a wife in a pretrial order in a divorce proceeding.


OVERVIEW: In a divorce action by pretrial order, the trial judge refused to automatically award wife all of the marital property based on an amendment to §1278. The trial court certified an immediate appeal of its order. The court affirmed, holding that the language of the body of the amended statute ignored the expressed wording in the title. The wording of the actual statute could not require that the wife receive all of the property, whether it were owned by her alone or not. Such language was contrary to the language of the title. Therefore, that portion of the amended statute that provided for the wife to receive the marital property, which was not necessarily her separate property, was void as contrary to Okla. Const. art. 5, § 57. The attempt to grant all the separate property of both parties to the wife was invalid and void.


OUTCOME: The interlocutory order of the trial court was affirmed.
