Johnson v. Ward


No. 48514


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 129; 541 P.2d 182; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 510



September 23, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Ronald N. Ricketts, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which denied their request for a temporary injunction that would have restrained defendant highway department from closing a segment of a street near the property owners' residences.


OVERVIEW: The department was constructing an expressway, and as a result, a street in proximity to the property owners' home would close. The property owners argued that they would have been adversely affected by the closing of the street because of increased traffic, flood problems, and loss of income to local businesses. They sought to enjoin the closing of the street. On appeal, they argued that the department did not comply with Okla. Stat. tit. 11, §§ 659.1-659.3 (Supp. 1974). The court affirmed the judgment because Okla. Stat. tit. 69, § 1302 authorized the department to close off the street. The property owners also argued that they had a right of ingress and egress to their premises by way of the closed street and could not be deprived of this right without due process of law and compensation for loss. The court found that § 1302 specifically authorized the department to close off the street incident to construction of limited access facility. Therefore, there was no violation of the property owners' due process rights.


OUTCOME: Denial of the request for a temporary injunction was affirmed.

State ex rel. Clifton v. Reeser


No. 47347


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 126; 543 P.2d 1379; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 500



September 16, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Certiorari granted; decision of Court of Appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant optician sought certiorari review of an order from the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), enjoining him from examining the human eye and duplicating or fitting contact lenses or regular lenses without a prescription.


OVERVIEW: The State had filed suit based on Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 942 (1971) and obtained an injunction against the optician to stop him from examining the human eye or duplicating contact lenses without a written prescription from an ophthalmologist, oculist, or optometrist. The trial court refused to enjoin the optician from duplicating regular lenses or using a Kerotometer, a machine that measured lens curvature. The court of appeals reversed in part, enjoining the optician from duplicating regular lenses as well but did not reach the question concerning the Kerotometer. On certiorari review, the court agreed that, under § 942, without a written prescription, no optician could supply a lens, whether a new lens or a duplicate of a lost or broken lens. However, the court agreed with the trial court that § 942 permitted an optician to use a Keratometer as an aid in fitting contact lenses. Section 942 was more broadly worded than statutes regulating opticians in other states. The use of a machine to measure lens curvature required technical rather than medical expertise, was necessary to the proper fitting of contact lenses, and was not traditionally performed by opthalmologists.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' reversal of the portion of the trial court's judgment that failed to enjoin the optician from duplicating regular lenses. However, the court affirmed the portion of the trial court's order refusing to enjoin the optician from using a machine that measured the lens curvature of eyes.

State ex rel. Field v. Hess


No. 46876


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 123; 540 P.2d 1165; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 597



September 16, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Comanche County; Jack Brock, Trial Judge. Action brought by State, on relation of district attorney, to abate a public nuisance by permanently enjoining the operation of business denoted as an "Adult Book Store," under 50 O.S.1971, §§ 1, 2, 8, 11. Trial judge, after hearing, granted the permanent injunction. Defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed with permanent injunction modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State filed suit to permanently enjoin appellant bookstore owner's operation of an adult bookstore as a public nuisance under Okla. Stat. tit. 50, §1 (1971). The District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma) determined that the bookstore was a public nuisance and granted a permanent injunction enjoining the operation of the bookstore. The bookstore owner appealed the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the adult bookstore was a public nuisance and enjoined the bookstore owner from operating the bookstore. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's finding that the bookstore was a public nuisance, but modified the terms of the injunction. The court held: (1) the materials that were placed in evidence before the trial court were obscene; (2) the exhibiting, selling, and trafficking in obscene works in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21 §§ 1021(3), 1040.51 was an act offending decency; (3) the State was not required to present expert testimony on the issue of whether the materials were obscene because the materials themselves were actually placed into evidence; (4) the act exhibiting, selling, and trafficking of the material placed in evidence was a public nuisance under Okla. Stat. tit. 50, § 1 (1971) because the act offended decency; and (5) the trial court erred when it permanently enjoined the operation of the bookstore, it should only have enjoined the sale, distribution, and exhibition of the particular materials and works introduced into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the works introduced in evidence were obscene and their exhibition, distribution, and sale constituted a public nuisance subject to abatement through a permanent injunction. The court modified the permanent injunction to enjoin the sale, distribution, exhibiting, bartering or trafficking in the particular and individual works or publications used as exhibits in the trial court.

 

385 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


MILLER v. SEARS ROEBUCK & CO.


No. 46702.


Supreme Court of Oklahoma.


1975 Okla. LEXIS 475; 46 O.B.A.J. 1375



July 15, 1975.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed a judgment from the lower court (Oklahoma), denying the employee workers' compensation benefits and finding that the Workers' Compensation Act did not apply to respondent employer, an own-risk employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as an assistant store manager trainee in the employer's retail and catalogue store. The employee's duties involved administrative work and manual labor. He was injured when stepping from a dock, lacerating his right hand and injuring his lower spine. The employee filed for workers' compensation benefits. The employer alleged that, because it was an own-risk employer, the Workers' Compensation Act was inapplicable. The lower court refused to apply the estoppel provision in Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 65.2. The employee appealed. The court reversed and remanded. First, the court held that an insurance carrier included own-risk employers within its definitive scope. Next, the court held that construing the Act in light of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, §§ 3 (9), 65.2 (1971), it was apparent that own-risk employers fell into the same category as employers that insured privately. Effect could be given both statutes only by recognizing Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 3(9), as declarative of a legislative intent that own-risk employers bear the same responsibilities under the Act. The court reversed all prior decisions inconsistent with the instant opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

386 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Util. Supply Co. v. City of Broken Arrow


No. 47236


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 106; 539 P.2d 740; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 466



July 8, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 1. On appeal from the judgment of the District Court, Tulsa County; Robert G. Green, Judge, which entered an injunction preventing the enforcement of a resolution passed by the City Council of Broken Arrow, Oklahoma, designating the size of pipe to be laid in the waterlines within the corporate limits. The trial court held the resolution was unconstitutional. The Court of Appeals affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Appellant seeks certiorari.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari granted. Decision of the Court of Appeals and judgment of the Trial Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee utility supply company sought an injunction to prevent the enforcement of appellant city's resolution designating the size of pipe to be laid in the city's waterlines. The trial court entered temporary and permanent injunctions. The Court of Appeals (Oklahoma) affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The city sought certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted an injunction to prevent the enforcement of the water pipe resolution. The court of appeals affirmed. On review, the court reversed and held that the city's resolution was neither arbitrary, capricious, nor unreasonable. The court found that the resolution was passed after lengthy deliberations conducted at several council meetings and was the result of the considered judgment of the city council based upon its experience, its specific needs, capabilities, and the recommendation of its technical engineering advisors. The court noted that the resolution did not impose any regulation as to how the company could conduct its business or interfere in the internal affairs of its business. The court determined that the company's position that it would incur some expense to manufacturer the appropriate pipe was not sufficient grounds to invalidate the resolution. The court noted that it would not interfere with an exercise of the city's police power unless the act was manifestly unreasonable and oppressive, unwarrantedly invaded private rights, clearly transcended the police powers given to them, or infringed upon the rights secured by fundamental law.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari. The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals that affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted an injunction against the enforcement of the city's resolution.

 

387 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Elk City v. Johnson


No. 48497


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 97; 537 P.2d 1215; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 456



July 1, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for Writ of Mandamus. Original action for Writ of Mandamus commanding defendant Mayor to issue proclamation as to the result of election held under Art. 10, Sec. 35, Oklahoma Constitution. Settle v. Bd. of County Com'rs of Muskogee (1969), Okl., 462 P.2d 646 is overruled.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought a writ of mandamus commanding respondent mayor to issue a proclamation as the result of an bond election held under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 35. The mayor had refused to issue the proclamation because the Oklahoma Constitution limited the election to "qualified taxpaying voters." "All qualified voters" had been permitted to vote in the election, in which issuance of bonds was approved by a legal majority.


OVERVIEW: The city held an election in which "all qualified voters" were allowed to vote. The mayor refused to issue the election proclamation because, under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 35, only "qualified taxpaying voters" could vote. After reviewing several decisions of other states and the United States Supreme Court, the court concluded that that portion of art. 10, § 35, limiting the franchise to taxpaying voters of the municipality or county, voting at an election for the purposes therein described, violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend XIV and was unconstitutional. The court granted the writ of mandamus and directed the mayor to issue the proclamation, specifically overruling an earlier decision to the contrary in Settle v. Board of County Com'rs of Muskogee, Okla., 462 P.2d 646.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ.

 

388 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


City of Edmond v. Wakefield


No. 46746


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 96; 537 P.2d 1211; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 453



July 1, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Oklahoma County; Carmon C. Harris, Judge. Appellants appeal from a judgment of the district court holding unconstitutional an ordinance of the City of Edmond, Oklahoma, which provides for the retention of contributions made by policemen to the Police Pension and Retirement Fund if policemen resign or are discharged before retirement.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and the trustees of a pension fund, appealed a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which held Edmond, Okla., Ordinance No. 2.52.220 unconstitutional. Plaintiff former policemen brought the suit challenging the ordinance, which provided for retention of contributions made by policemen to a retirement fund if the policemen resigned or were discharged before retirement.


OVERVIEW: The city's pension system was financed in part through a two percent mandatory contribution from all policemen. No one was forced to become policemen, so the contributions were considered voluntary. They only became involuntary once the policemen had joined the force, when they could not withdraw consent without losing their jobs. Some of the former policemen who had resigned or been discharged sought to recover contributions they had made to their pension and retirement fund, but the city refused, pursuant to Ordinance No. 2.52.220. The policemen filed an action in mandamus to compel the payments on the grounds that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment in their favor, and defendants appealed. The court reversed and remanded for dismissal, holding that the ordinance was not unreasonable because it was possible that there was no perfect correlation between the two percent of gross salary contributions and the benefits the policemen received while employed by the city, but there was some correlation. The enforced contribution with a no refund policy, in light of the extra protection afforded the officers and their families, was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for dismissal of the policemen's action.

 

389 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Carpet City v. Stillwater Mun. Hosp. Auth.


No. 48353


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 75; 536 P.2d 335; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 419



May 20, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding for Writ of Mandamus.

Original Proceeding involving Application to Assume Original Jurisdiction, and Petition for Writ of Mandamus to compel the Stillwater Municipal Hospital Authority, a public trust to comply with the provisions of the Public Competitive Bidding Act of 1974, 60 O.S. 1974 Supp. § 101 et seq. Original jurisdiction assumed.



DISPOSITION: Writ of Mandamus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bidder sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, a hospital and the board of trustees, to comply with the Public Competitive Bidding Act of 1974, Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 101 et seq. (Supp. 1974), in constructing a new hospital. The writ was sought after the trustees, who had allegedly failed to comply with the Act in awarding a bid for carpet installation, reversed its decision to withdraw the award and re-solicit bids.


OVERVIEW: Incident to the construction of a hospital, the trustees awarded the bid for carpet installation to the contractor. Having failed to comply with the Act, the trustees withdrew the award and re-solicited bids. When the trustees reversed their actions, re-awarded the contract to the contractor, and waived the Act's bond requirements, the bidder petitioned for a writ of mandamus to direct the trustees to comply with the Act. In granting the writ, the court held that where the specifications of an architect required carpet installation as an essential part of a public building's construction, the bids for it were subject to the Act. The court also held that the trustees' acceptance of a previously rejected bid had not complied with the Act because: (1) rejection of all the bids had required a re-solicitation; and (2) the exception under Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 130 (Supp. 1974) was inapplicable. Moreover, the court held that a public agency could not extend the mandatory time requirements of Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 113 (Supp. 1974) by re-awarding a bid. Finally, the court held that the bond requirement of Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 131 (Supp. 1974) was mandatory and could not be waived.


OUTCOME: In granting the bidder's writ of mandamus, the court compelled the hospital and the trustees to comply with the Act.

 

390 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Moran v. State ex rel. Derryberry


No. 47716


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 69; 534 P.2d 1282; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 407



May 2, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Jack R. Parr, Trial Judge..



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the state of Oklahoma and several state officials, challenged a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that enjoined them from appropriating assets from the State Insurance Fund (Fund) to support public school activities. Appellants claimed that they had the authority to appropriate Fund assets for purposes not listed in the State Insurance Fund Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 1 et seq. (1971 & Supp. 1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellee businesses were insured by the State Insurance Fund (Fund), from which workmen's compensation claims were paid. Appellees sued appellants, the state of Oklahoma and the Fund's commissioner and managers, to enjoin legislative appropriation of Fund assets to support public school activities. Appellees moved for summary judgment, claiming that the legislature had no authority to appropriate Fund assets for purposes not listed in the State Insurance Fund Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 1 et seq. (1971 & Supp. 1974). The trial court granted the motion. Appellants challenged the decision, claiming that the legislature had authority to appropriate Fund assets for any purpose. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision. It explained that the Fund assets did not belong to the state, because if the Fund were to become insolvent or fail to pay a workmen's compensation award, appellees and other employers insured by the Fund, not the state, would be required to pay the award. Because Fund assets did not belong to the state, the state had no right to appropriate them for purposes other than workmen's compensation and appellees were entitled to an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to enjoin appellants, the state of Oklahoma and several state officials, from appropriating assets from the State Insurance Fund (Fund) to support public school activities. The court explained that the Fund's assets, from which workmen's compensation claims were paid, belonged to appellees and other employers insured by the Fund, not the state, so appellants had no right to appropriate them.

 

391 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


York v. Halley


No. 48329


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 51; 534 P.2d 363; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 381



April 8, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Original jurisdiction assumed, writ of mandamus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parents applied for relief against respondent judge by mandamus, to decide whether the parents were denied due process when the judge refused to hold an adversary hearing to test the allegations of a petition seeking temporary custody of their children.


OVERVIEW: The children were removed from their home based on an ex parte order entered pursuant to a petition that stated that the children were neglected, malnourished, and in need of immediate medical treatment. The children were placed in the temporary custody of a relative. The parents requested a show cause or evidentiary hearing to determine the merits of the application for temporary custody. The judge denied the parents' request because time was not available. The parents conceded that the judge had the authority to enter the ex parte order under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1104(b) (1971). The court agreed with the parents that for the judge to remove their children from their home and custody for a period of two months without a meaningful hearing, in which they might have presented testimony and evidence to support their position that the allegations in the petition were untrue, was unconstitutional and a denial of due process. The court also held that the failure to schedule a hearing for two months after depriving the parents of custody was an impediment to the continuance of the parent-child relationship. The fact that the judge had no time to conduct the hearings was no excuse.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus.

 

392 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re Napier


No. 47260


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 24; 532 P.2d 423; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 338



February 18, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Juvenile Division, Joe Jennings, Trial Judge. A referee entered an order finding appellants to be children in need of supervision and recommending appellants be placed in custody of Vianney School for Girls. Trial court confirmed findings and recommendation of referee. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, children in need of supervision, sought review of an order of the District Court, Tulsa County; Juvenile Division (Oklahoma), which confirmed a referee's findings that the children were in need of supervision and recommending that the children be placed in a girls school. The district court also affirmed the referee's overruling of a motion to dismiss based on the unconstitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 10 § 1101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Counsel for the children stipulated that the children had engaged in the conduct alleged in the petition before the referee. The sole issue on appeal was whether the governing statutes were unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed. Reviewing decisions in other states construing similar statutes, the court refused to find that the definition of children in need of supervision found in Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1101(c) was vague. Its terms were common and easily understood. Further, the statutes did not have any "chilling" effect on the children's rights. The fact that the statutes might be overly restrictive in hypothetical marginal cases was not sufficient to rule them unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court found the statutes to be constitutional and affirmed the order entered by the district court.

City of Midwest City v. Cravens


No. 47552


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 22; 532 P.2d 829; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 332; 88 L.R.R.M. 3367



February 14, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Floyd L. Martin, District Judge. The Fraternal Order of Police, as the bargaining agent for the Midwest City Police Department, filed a charge with Appellant, Public Employees Relation Board, alleging that Appellee, The City of Midwest City, was engaged in unfair labor practices in contravention of the Firefighters' and Policemen's Arbitration Law. The Appellee sought injunctive relief in the District Court enjoining the Appellant from exercising further jurisdiction in the cause. The trial court found the Firefighters' and Policemen's Arbitration Law to be in contravention of Article XVIII, § 3, of the Constitution, and enjoined the Appellant from exercising further jurisdiction over Appellee and Appellant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the District Court reversed in part; judgment permanently enjoining the Public Employees Relation Board from exercising further jurisdiction in the cause affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) granted injunctive relief to appellee municipality in its action against appellant, the Public Employees Relation Board. The municipality and the Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: A union, as the bargaining agent for the municipality's police department, sought to negotiate the terms and conditions of an employment contract with the municipality. When the municipality refused to negotiate the salary portion of the contract on the grounds that it called for a reclassification of police personnel, the union filed a charge with the Board. The union claimed that the municipality had engaged in unfair labor practices. The municipality then filed an action for injunctive relief against the Board. The trial court granted the municipality injunctive relief and permanently enjoined Board and its members from exercising further jurisdiction over the municipality. The trial court also found that the Firefighters' and Policemen's Arbitration Law was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the Law was constitutional and only required the municipality to meet at reasonable times and to confer in good faith with respect to wages, hours, and other conditions of employment. OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in part and affirmed it in part.

 

394 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Okla. Gas & Elec. Co. v. Corp. Comm'n


No. 47861


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1975 OK 15; 543 P.2d 546; 1975 Okla. LEXIS 321



February 4, 1975 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner utility brought an original action seeking a writ of prohibition to enjoin respondent, the Oklahoma Corporation Commission, from determining an application brought by respondent landowners, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 17, § 152 (1971), to bar the utility's construction of an electric generating station and a cooling reservoir. The Commission had retained jurisdiction concerning two allegations of the landowners' application.


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed that the proposed generating station was not necessary to sufficiently supply electric power and that the utility was not making the best use of its existing plants. The owners requested that the Commission direct the utility to abandon its project. The utility claimed that the Commission had no jurisdiction to adjudicate the owners' issues. The court assumed jurisdiction, finding that prohibition was a proper remedy to challenge an agency's jurisdiction under Okla. Const. art. VII, § 4. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 17, § 152 (1961) gave the Commission general supervision over all public utilities, but it did not give the Commission authority to regulate the internal operation and management of the utilities to the extent that it could prohibit the construction of a proposed generating station. The legislature could not vest to the Commission duties that were inconsistent with its constitutional duties of general rate regulation and supervision under Okla. Const. art. IX, §§ 18, 19. Therefore, the Commission lacked jurisdiction to consider the owners' application.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of prohibition and prohibited the Commission from further action in the present cause except for granting a dismissal of the proceeding.

Indep. Sch. Dist. v. McReynolds


No. 46737


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1974 OK 136; 528 P.2d 313; 1974 Okla. LEXIS 429



November 5, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding to review order, affirmed by State Industrial Court on en banc appeal awarding death benefits under law in effect on date of death.

A.L. Voth, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION:  Award sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, an employer and others, sought review of an order of the State Industrial Court (Oklahoma), which affirmed a trial judge's order, awarding claimants, a surviving wife and children, death benefits. The benefits were compensation for the death of an employee, the deceased, as the result of an accidental injury in covered employment.


OVERVIEW: The deceased had a history of heart problems during his years of employment with the employer. The deceased suffered an attack during work and was awarded total permanent disability benefits. The deceased suffered other episodes of heart trouble and died about two or three years later from another heart episode. The lower court affirmed the trial judge's order finding that the deceased suffered an accidental injury at work, which resulted in his death. The court found that the lower court's determination of the issue of whether the deceased's death resulted from an accidental injury at work or resulted from other causes was supported by competent evidence. The court found that the date of the deceased's death controlled the amount of recovery. The right of the claimants to claim death benefits under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 22(7) (1971) did not accrue until the date of the deceased's death. Adjudication of those rights was properly made under the law applicable on that date.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the award.

 

396 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. Slater


No. 47877


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1974 OK 139; 559 P.2d 428; 1974 Okla. LEXIS 436; 45 O.B.A.J. 2540



November 5, 1974 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Cert. denied, 422 U.S. 1046 (1975) 


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; William Means, Judge, in an action for writ of mandamus to have Appellant placed on the ballot as a candidate for Governor.



DISPOSITION: District Court sustained Respondent's motion to quash and plea to the jurisdiction and venue. Application for mandamus denied. Petition in error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed a "petition in error" against the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which sustained a motion to quash and plea to the jurisdiction and venue filed by respondent Secretary of the State Election Board in the candidate's action for a writ of mandamus to have to his name placed on the ballot as an independent candidate for governor. The Secretary filed a motion to dismiss the "petition in error."


OVERVIEW: The candidate alleged that he was indigent and unable to pay the filing fee for the office. In his "petition in error," the candidate complained that the Secretary's decision denied him a place on the ballot. The court held that the trial court was correct in dismissing the candidate's case since it was improperly brought in Tulsa County. Any action against the State Election Board had to be filed in Oklahoma County. The court treated the candidate's pleadings as both a petition in error and an attempt for an original action for writ of mandamus. Although the appeal and action could have been dismissed on procedural grounds, the court decided that case against the candidate on its merits. Under Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 161 (1971), the candidate was required to either pay the filing fee or file a petition signed by five percent of the qualified electors. The candidate did neither, but argued that the statute was unconstitutional The court disagreed. The statute provided a reasonable alternative to a filing fee for the state to test the "seriousness" of a candidate. Thus, its method was reasonable, did not unduly discriminate against indigents, and was constitutionally firm.


OUTCOME: The court denied that candidate's application for mandamus and dismissed his petition in error.

Sowders v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 46211


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1974 OK 122; 527 P.2d 852; 1974 Okla. LEXIS 420



October 22, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oklahoma Tax Commission. Appellant filed claim requesting refund of income taxes erroneously paid. An auditor for the Commission denied the claim and appellant appeals. The Commission filed motion to dismiss.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed and remanded to Tax Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission filed a motion to dismiss appellant taxpayer's petition in error, which requested review of an auditor's denial of his request for an income tax refund.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed income tax returns as a single person. The taxpayer filed amended returns requesting a refund for the amount by which the taxes paid exceeded the taxes payable under the rates applicable to married persons. The taxpayer alleged that the denial of income-splitting benefits to single persons was unconstitutional. The Commission's auditor denied the claim. The Commission did not respond to the taxpayer's request to advise him if an administrative hearing was a prerequisite for a direct appeal to the court. The court had no jurisdiction over the taxpayer's appeal because the Commission issued no order or ruling from which appeal was authorized. However, the court held that the taxpayer's amended returns and supporting schedules were procedurally sufficient as claims for refunds under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 2352 and 2373 (1971), and entitled him to an order denying or approving the claim because the returns were signed under penalty of perjury and indicated the taxpayer's name, the periods for which the income taxes were paid, and the gist of his claim.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the taxpayer's appeal and remanded the cause to the Commission to proceed in accordance with the applicable statutory provisions.

 

398 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hamilton v. City of Okla. City


No. 45756


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1974 OK 109; 527 P.2d 14; 1974 Okla. LEXIS 397



September 17, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division II.

Action for damages sustained from the alleged false imprisonment of the plaintiff by an Oklahoma City Police Officer. The trial of the case in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Honorable Jim Barnett, Presiding, resulted in a directed verdict for plaintiff on the issue of liability and a jury award of $1,800.00. The Court of Appeals, Division II, Affirmed the Judgment of the trial court.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari granted. Court of Appeals opinion vacated. Trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted appellee, a claimant who was jailed, a directed verdict in an action alleging false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The city sought review of the trial court's decision contending that the Oklahoma Governmental Tort Liability Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 11, §§ 1751-1766 (1971), which provided that cities with populations over 200,000 would be liable for its torts arising out of its governmental functions was unconstitutional because it violated Okla. Const. art. 5, § 46 and Okla. Const. art. 5, § 59, which prohibited special legislation. The lower appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court affirmed, holding that if a legislative act was founded in reason and was general in terms, it would not be rendered invalid simply because at the time the statute was enacted only certain municipalities fell within its classification. The courts did not concern themselves as to whether an act of the legislature was wholesome and salutary in its operation or whether such legislation was unwise and harmful. Statutes were presumed to be valid absent a conclusive showing that the legislation was arbitrary or capricious and bore no reasonable relation to the object to be accomplished.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the directed verdict granted to the claimant in the action alleging false imprisonment.

 

399 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Olim v. Mayberry


No. 46107


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1974 OK 81; 524 P.2d 24; 1974 Okla. LEXIS 370



June 25, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Carmon C. Harris, Dist. Judge. Appellant appeals order of district court upholding constitutionality of 47 O.S. 1971 § 6-204(c) which provides that an unvacated forfeiture of bail or collateral deposited to secure defendant's appearance in court for traffic violations shall be treated as equivalent to conviction.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the judgment of the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that denied him relief by upholding the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 6-204(c) (1971), which provided that a forfeiture of bail deposited as security for appearance in court for traffic violations should have been treated as equivalent to conviction, in the driver's action for mandamus against appellee Department of Public Safety.


OVERVIEW: The district court ordered the correction of the driver's driving record when a mistake had been made in posting the dispositions of traffic charges as please of guilty when they had in fact been bond forfeitures. The driver amended his petition alleging that it had been unconstitutional for the Department to have maintained a file and report to the public existence of bond forfeitures. Insurance companies tended to have charged the driver a higher premium because of their knowledge of the numerous occasions on which he had forfeited bail on traffic complaints. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of any relief. The driver asserted that treating a bond forfeiture equal to a conviction was unconstitutional. The court ruled that the driver had failed in entering an appearance, waiving the right to appear, and that in order to have avoiding having a bond forfeiture entered on a driving record, a licensee must have merely appeared and answered the arresting officer's charges. The court concluded that the legislature, by enacting § 6-204(c), intended to have attributed to a bond forfeiture the same legal consequences as those which attended a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of relief in favor of the Department in the driver's action for mandamus.

 

400 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bd. of Examiners in Optometry v. Lawton


No. 45380


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1974 OK 69; 523 P.2d 1064; 1974 Okla. LEXIS 340



June 11, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Carmon C. Harris, Judge. Appellant appeals judgment of the District Court which held that an action for declaratory judgment was proper to determine the construction and validity of 59 O.S. 1971, § 594. The Court found the statute to be unconstitutional and entered a permanent restraining order against appellants.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State and the Oklahoma Board of Examiners in Optometry (Board), sought review of a declaratory judgment by the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which found Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 594 (1971), unconstitutional and entered a permanent restraining order against the Board in appellee optometrist's action for declaratory relief and an injunction.


OVERVIEW: Section 594 provided that an optometrist could not have his practice adjacent to or in geographical proximity to a retail optical outlet or optical store. The optometrist had leased an office in a building where a retail optical outlet had leased space on the opposite side of the hall. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that a proper justiciable controversy existed for declaratory judgment because the optometrist was not required to hazard a breach of § 594 before bringing an action for declaratory relief. The court noted that the optometrist could be subjected to criminal prosecution and lose his license for violation of the statute. Upon review of the language of § 594, the court held that the statute was vague and ambiguous because it was unclear what constituted "adjacent to" a retail optical outlet and what constituted "geographical proximity." Although the court noted that the terms in question might be definite enough in other situations, the court found that they were not sufficiently definite in the relevant statute as it imposed criminal penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.
